In the Old Testament, this image often refers to hell ([11:6](https://ref.ly/Ps11:6); [18:8](https://ref.ly/Ps18:8); [50:3](https://ref.ly/Ps50:3); [68:2](https://ref.ly/Ps68:2); [78:21](https://ref.ly/Ps78:21); [79:5](https://ref.ly/Ps79:5); [80:16](https://ref.ly/Ps80:16); [89:46](https://ref.ly/Ps89:46); [97:3](https://ref.ly/Ps97:3); [104:4](https://ref.ly/Ps104:4); [140:10](https://ref.ly/Ps140:10); see [Isa 66:24](https://ref.ly/Isa66:24)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 21:9

## Psalms 21:10 (id: 24245)

children . . . descendants: Evil will end when God destroys all opposition to himself ([109:13](https://ref.ly/Ps109:13); cp. [18:50](https://ref.ly/Ps18:50); [22:30–31](https://ref.ly/Ps22:30-Ps22:31); [25:13](https://ref.ly/Ps25:13); [102:28](https://ref.ly/Ps102:28)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 21:10

## Psalms 21:13 (id: 24246)

Rise up (or *be exalted,* as in [57:5](https://ref.ly/Ps57:5), [11](https://ref.ly/Ps57:11); [108:5](https://ref.ly/Ps108:5)) expresses communal praise and joy in God’s greatness and power.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 21:13

## Psalms 22:1–2 (id: 24256)

A deep sense of alienation from God overwhelms the psalmist (see [10:1](https://ref.ly/Ps10:1)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 22:1–PSA 22:2

## Psalms 22:1–21 (id: 24255)

The psalmist alternates between reflections on his present dire circumstances and memories of the Lord’s past faithfulness; he ends with a prayer for rescue.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 22:1–PSA 22:21

## Psalms 22:1–31 (id: 24257)

All previous laments pale in comparison with this outcry against the enemy and God’s abandonment. The psalm contains two main sections: the lament ([22:1–21](https://ref.ly/Ps22:1-Ps22:21)) and praise for redemption ([22:22–31](https://ref.ly/Ps22:22-Ps22:31)), which leads naturally to [Ps 23](https://ref.ly/Ps23:1-Ps23:6). The apostles saw in this psalm an expression of the sufferings of Jesus Christ, who ultimately fulfilled the purpose of David’s humiliation, rejection by people, and divine abandonment ([Matt 27:35](https://ref.ly/Matt27:35), [39](https://ref.ly/Matt27:39), [43](https://ref.ly/Matt27:43), [46](https://ref.ly/Matt27:46); [Mark 15:34](https://ref.ly/Mark15:34); [John 19:23–24](https://ref.ly/John19:23-John19:24), [28](https://ref.ly/John19:28); [Heb 2:12](https://ref.ly/Heb2:12)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 22:1–PSA 22:31

## Psalms 22:3 (id: 24278)

God, the holy King, is set apart from all his creation, but he chooses to reveal himself to Israel. • God greatly desires that his people offer praises to him.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 22:3

## Psalms 22:6–8 (id: 24279)

Both the Lord and people reject the psalmist. He vividly describes his anguish ([22:1–2](https://ref.ly/Ps22:1-Ps22:2)); he lives like a lowly animal.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 22:6–PSA 22:8

## Psalms 22:7 (id: 24280)

Everyone mocks the psalmist’s confidence in the Lord (see [3:2](https://ref.ly/Ps3:2); [Matt 27:43](https://ref.ly/Matt27:43)), which shames him ([Pss 44:13–14](https://ref.ly/Ps44:13-Ps44:14); [74:10](https://ref.ly/Ps74:10); [89:50](https://ref.ly/Ps89:50); [109:25](https://ref.ly/Ps109:25)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 22:7

## Psalms 22:9 (id: 24282)

The Lord took care of the psalmist before he could do anything for himself (see [71:6](https://ref.ly/Ps71:6); [139:13](https://ref.ly/Ps139:13)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 22:9

## Psalms 22:9–11 (id: 24281)

The psalmist reflects on his past relationship with God (see [22:3–5](https://ref.ly/Ps22:3-Ps22:5)). The Lord has been his very life.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 22:9–PSA 22:11

## Psalms 22:12 (id: 24259)

Bashan*,* a region known for its herds and vegetation, produced strong bulls ([68:30](https://ref.ly/Ps68:30)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 22:12

## Psalms 22:12–18 (id: 24258)

The psalmist returns to expressing his anguish and suffering (see [22:1–2](https://ref.ly/Ps22:1-Ps22:2), [6–8](https://ref.ly/Ps22:6-Ps22:8)). His trouble comes from human beings who act like beasts.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 22:12–PSA 22:18

## Psalms 22:14 (id: 24260)

The psalmist’s sense of being poured out like water expresses a meaningless, transitory existence that leaves him depleted.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 22:14

## Psalms 22:15 (id: 24261)

Facing adversity is as horrible as dying of thirst (see [137:6](https://ref.ly/Ps137:6)). • Jesus may have had this verse in mind when he said, “I am thirsty” ([John 19:28](https://ref.ly/John19:28)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 22:15

## Psalms 22:16 (id: 24262)

The wild pack of dogs represents fierce and unscrupulous people.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 22:16

## Psalms 22:17–18 (id: 24263)

I can count all my bones: The psalmist’s enemies have utterly shamed him by taking his garments. Jesus also suffered this disgrace (see [Matt 27:35](https://ref.ly/Matt27:35)). • stare at me and gloat: Enemies make the psalmist the object of their scorn (see [Pss 35:24](https://ref.ly/Ps35:24), [26](https://ref.ly/Ps35:26); [38:16](https://ref.ly/Ps38:16); [55:3](https://ref.ly/Ps55:3); cp. [59:10](https://ref.ly/Ps59:10)). • throw dice: Literally *cast lots.* The casting of lots was sometimes a way for godly people to find God’s direction ([Lev 16:8](https://ref.ly/Lev16:8); [Num 27:21](https://ref.ly/Num27:21); [Acts 1:24–26](https://ref.ly/Acts1:24-Acts1:26)). Here, the lots are thrown simply as a game of chance. The soldiers threw dice for Jesus’ clothing after the crucifixion ([Matt 27:35](https://ref.ly/Matt27:35); [Mark 15:24](https://ref.ly/Mark15:24); [Luke 23:34](https://ref.ly/Luke23:34); [John 19:24](https://ref.ly/John19:24)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 22:17–PSA 22:18

## Psalms 22:19–21 (id: 24264)

The psalmist faces his troubles by praying for God’s rescue. Only the Lord has the strength to ward off dogs, lions, and oxen.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 22:19–PSA 22:21

## Psalms 22:20 (id: 24265)

The sword makes evident the lethal intent of the enemy.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 22:20

## Psalms 22:22 (id: 24267)

I will proclaim your name: The writer to the Hebrews ascribes these words to Jesus ([Heb 2:12](https://ref.ly/Heb2:12)). • my brothers and sisters: Literally *my brothers.* In the New Testament quotation, the Greek translation picks up the broader meaning as “my brothers and sisters.”

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 22:22

## Psalms 22:22–24 (id: 24266)

The psalmist praises the Lord and calls for the godly to join him. He tells of God’s goodness to the needy, including himself.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 22:22–PSA 22:24

## Psalms 22:23 (id: 24268)

The godly respond with awe (see [22:25](https://ref.ly/Ps22:25)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 22:23

## Psalms 22:24 (id: 24269)

Unlike his response to the wicked (see [21:8–12](https://ref.ly/Ps21:8-Ps21:12)), God cares about the needy and hears their prayers ([51:17](https://ref.ly/Ps51:17); [69:33](https://ref.ly/Ps69:33); [102:17](https://ref.ly/Ps102:17)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 22:24

## Psalms 22:25 (id: 24271)

The great assembly might include all nations ([22:27](https://ref.ly/Ps22:27); [26:12](https://ref.ly/Ps26:12); [35:18](https://ref.ly/Ps35:18)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 22:25

## Psalms 22:25–31 (id: 24270)

The psalmist vows to praise the Lord, the great King of the earth ([22:27–28](https://ref.ly/Ps22:27-Ps22:28)) who cares for the needy. God alone deserves praise.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 22:25–PSA 22:31

## Psalms 22:26 (id: 24272)

God knows his people’s needs and addresses them ([63:5](https://ref.ly/Ps63:5); [81:16](https://ref.ly/Ps81:16); [103:5](https://ref.ly/Ps103:5); [107:9](https://ref.ly/Ps107:9); [132:15](https://ref.ly/Ps132:15); [145:16](https://ref.ly/Ps145:16); [147:14](https://ref.ly/Ps147:14)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 22:26

## Psalms 22:27 (id: 24273)

families of the nations: All clans and tribes of humanity (see [Gen 12:3](https://ref.ly/Gen12:3); [Rev 5:9–10](https://ref.ly/Rev5:9-Rev5:10)) will live in submission to the Lord ([Ps 96:1–3](https://ref.ly/Ps96:1-Ps96:3); see [Pss 2](https://ref.ly/Ps2:1-Ps2:12), [72](https://ref.ly/Ps72:1-Ps72:20); [Isa 2:2–4](https://ref.ly/Isa2:2-Isa2:4); [1 Cor 15:25–27](https://ref.ly/1Cor15:25-1Cor15:27)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 22:27

## Psalms 22:28 (id: 24274)

The universal kingdom belongs to God alone ([Obad 1:21](https://ref.ly/Obad1:21)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 22:28

## Psalms 22:29 (id: 24275)

The Lord invites all people, rich and poor ([22:26](https://ref.ly/Ps22:26)), to the banquet as long as they worship him.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 22:29

## Psalms 22:30 (id: 24276)

Future generations will join those from the past who praised the Lord ([22:3–5](https://ref.ly/Ps22:3-Ps22:5)). The descendants of the godly will receive blessings ([22:30–31](https://ref.ly/Ps22:30-Ps22:31)), unlike the offspring of the wicked ([21:10](https://ref.ly/Ps21:10)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 22:30

## Psalms 22:31 (id: 24277)

The Lord’s acts of redemption ([40:9](https://ref.ly/Ps40:9); [50:6](https://ref.ly/Ps50:6); [71:15](https://ref.ly/Ps71:15), [16](https://ref.ly/Ps71:16), [24](https://ref.ly/Ps71:24); [97:6](https://ref.ly/Ps97:6)) demonstrate that he is righteous (see [4:1](https://ref.ly/Ps4:1)). His righteousness provides the character required for rule, judicial decisions, and relationships. This virtue leads to harmony and order (see [50:6](https://ref.ly/Ps50:6)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 22:31

## Psalms 23:1 (id: 24286)

The Lord promises to take care of his children ([34:9–10](https://ref.ly/Ps34:9-Ps34:10); [Isa 51:14](https://ref.ly/Isa51:14)). He demonstrated this ability to Israel in the wilderness ([Deut 2:7](https://ref.ly/Deut2:7)) and in the Promised Land ([Deut 8:9](https://ref.ly/Deut8:9)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 23:1

## Psalms 23:1–3 (id: 24284)

People in the ancient Near East commonly viewed their rulers as shepherds.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 23:1–PSA 23:3

## Psalms 23:1–6 (id: 24285)

This psalm of trust and confidence in the Lord has been a favorite of God’s people for generations. It expresses assurance of God’s presence in the midst of adversity. It evokes images of the Good Shepherd ([23:1–3](https://ref.ly/Ps23:1-Ps23:3); see [Ezek 34:12](https://ref.ly/Ezek34:12); [John 10:11](https://ref.ly/John10:11)) and of the messianic banquet ([Ps 23:5–6](https://ref.ly/Ps23:5-Ps23:6); see [Isa 25:6](https://ref.ly/Isa25:6); [Rev 19:9](https://ref.ly/Rev19:9)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 23:1–PSA 23:6

## Psalms 23:1–28.9 (id: 24283)

These psalms develop the importance of integrity ([25:4–7](https://ref.ly/Ps25:4-Ps25:7), [12–14](https://ref.ly/Ps25:12-Ps25:14), [21](https://ref.ly/Ps25:21); [26:6](https://ref.ly/Ps26:6), [11](https://ref.ly/Ps26:11); [27:7–12](https://ref.ly/Ps27:7-Ps27:12)), God’s shepherding care ([23:1](https://ref.ly/Ps23:1); [28:9](https://ref.ly/Ps28:9)), God’s guidance ([23:2–3](https://ref.ly/Ps23:2-Ps23:3); [25:5](https://ref.ly/Ps25:5); [27:11](https://ref.ly/Ps27:11)), God’s goodness ([23:6](https://ref.ly/Ps23:6); [25:7–8](https://ref.ly/Ps25:7-Ps25:8); [27:13](https://ref.ly/Ps27:13)), and living in his house ([23:6](https://ref.ly/Ps23:6); [26:8](https://ref.ly/Ps26:8); [27:4](https://ref.ly/Ps27:4), [8](https://ref.ly/Ps27:8)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 23:1–PSA 28:9

## Psalms 23:2 (id: 24287)

Sheep rest after they have eaten their fill ([Zeph 3:13](https://ref.ly/Zeph3:13); see [Isa 11:7](https://ref.ly/Isa11:7); cp. [Isa 13:20](https://ref.ly/Isa13:20); [27:10](https://ref.ly/Isa27:10)). • The Lord leads the sheep for their own benefit (see [Ps 5:8](https://ref.ly/Ps5:8)). • Sheep only drink from still water, so the shepherd seeks out peaceful streams for his flock.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 23:2

## Psalms 23:3 (id: 24288)

Cp. [19:7](https://ref.ly/Ps19:7); the Lord’s word renews my strength. • The Lord guides by rescuing his people from evil ([23:4–5](https://ref.ly/Ps23:4-Ps23:5); see [31:3](https://ref.ly/Ps31:3)), bringing them back to himself ([5:8](https://ref.ly/Ps5:8); [61:2](https://ref.ly/Ps61:2)), caring ([48:14](https://ref.ly/Ps48:14); [139:10](https://ref.ly/Ps139:10)), ruling ([67:4](https://ref.ly/Ps67:4)), counseling ([73:24](https://ref.ly/Ps73:24)), protecting ([78:53](https://ref.ly/Ps78:53); [107:30](https://ref.ly/Ps107:30); [143:11](https://ref.ly/Ps143:11)), and instructing them in wisdom ([27:11](https://ref.ly/Ps27:11); see [Prov 4:11](https://ref.ly/Prov4:11)). • The Lord’s name guarantees the relationship; he guards his reputation against any accusation of his abandoning his people or allowing them to sin (see [Pss 25:11](https://ref.ly/Ps25:11); [31:3](https://ref.ly/Ps31:3); [106:8](https://ref.ly/Ps106:8); [143:11](https://ref.ly/Ps143:11)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 23:3

## Psalms 23:4 (id: 24289)

The shepherd used his rod and staff to fend off danger.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 23:4

## Psalms 23:5 (id: 24290)

A feast demonstrates the Lord’s care and mercy toward his people (see [22:26](https://ref.ly/Ps22:26), [29](https://ref.ly/Ps22:29)). Although enemies can watch, they cannot trouble the guests. • The ritual of anointing the head with oil showed guests honor ([92:9–11](https://ref.ly/Ps92:9-Ps92:11)), hospitality, and refreshment ([104:15](https://ref.ly/Ps104:15); [133:2](https://ref.ly/Ps133:2)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 23:5

## Psalms 23:6 (id: 24291)

The Lord expresses his unfailing love through the goodness of his presence and other benefits that he alone provides ([69:16](https://ref.ly/Ps69:16); [86:17](https://ref.ly/Ps86:17); [109:21](https://ref.ly/Ps109:21); see [18:6](https://ref.ly/Ps18:6); [61:4](https://ref.ly/Ps61:4)). He actively bestows care that is greater than the temporary trials imposed by enemies ([7:1](https://ref.ly/Ps7:1)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 23:6

## Psalms 24:1 (id: 24295)

The Lord created and now rules the earth and everything in it (see [1 Cor 10:25–26](https://ref.ly/1Cor10:25-1Cor10:26)). He sees all its people ([Ps 33:14](https://ref.ly/Ps33:14)), regardless of their status ([49:1–2](https://ref.ly/Ps49:1-Ps49:2)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 24:1

## Psalms 24:1–2 (id: 24293)

The kingdom belongs to the Creator, the Great King (cp. [22:27](https://ref.ly/Ps22:27)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 24:1–PSA 24:2

## Psalms 24:1–10 (id: 24292)

The shepherd of [Ps 23](https://ref.ly/Ps23:1-Ps23:6), who is also the King of the whole world, takes possession of Zion.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 24:1–PSA 24:10

## Psalms 24:2 (id: 24296)

God created everything in an orderly and stable manner (see [89:11](https://ref.ly/Ps89:11); [102:25](https://ref.ly/Ps102:25); [104:5](https://ref.ly/Ps104:5)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 24:2

## Psalms 24:3 (id: 24298)

These questions invite readers to look away from their problems with the wicked and to examine themselves (see [15:1](https://ref.ly/Ps15:1)). • God’s holy place is the holy mountain, a reference both to Jerusalem and to heaven.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 24:3

## Psalms 24:3–6 (id: 24297)

The citizens of the King’s realm include all who seek him. The Lord invites them to enter his presence.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 24:3–PSA 24:6

## Psalms 24:4 (id: 24299)

Those with pure hands have not shed blood or injured relationships between people (see [9:12](https://ref.ly/Ps9:12); [15:2–5](https://ref.ly/Ps15:2-Ps15:5)). • Those with pure hearts commit themselves fully to the Lord, as evidenced in strength of character, transparency, and selflessness ([51:10](https://ref.ly/Ps51:10); [73:1](https://ref.ly/Ps73:1); see [Matt 5:8](https://ref.ly/Matt5:8)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 24:4

## Psalms 24:10 (id: 24294)

The Lord of Heaven’s Armies reigns from his home, the Temple in Jerusalem ([84:3–5](https://ref.ly/Ps84:3-Ps84:5)). He excludes sin and sinners ([24:3–6](https://ref.ly/Ps24:3-Ps24:6)) but protects all who dwell in Zion.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 24:10

## Psalms 25:1 (id: 24309)

The psalmist commits himself to the Lord instead of to idols (see [24:3–4](https://ref.ly/Ps24:3-Ps24:4)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 25:1

## Psalms 25:1–3 (id: 24301)

The psalmist expresses confidence that the godly will be vindicated and his enemies will not succeed (see [25:15–22](https://ref.ly/Ps25:15-Ps25:22)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 25:1–PSA 25:3

## Psalms 25:1–22 (id: 24300)

This individual lament includes instruction in wisdom and a community lament; it begins and ends with an affirmation of trust in the Lord ([25:1–3](https://ref.ly/Ps25:1-Ps25:3), [15–22](https://ref.ly/Ps25:15-Ps25:22)). The psalmist prays for guidance ([25:4–7](https://ref.ly/Ps25:4-Ps25:7)) and encourages the godly to practice a lifestyle of wisdom ([25:12–14](https://ref.ly/Ps25:12-Ps25:14)). In addition to the enemies who trouble him, the psalmist confesses his sins ([25:7](https://ref.ly/Ps25:7), [11](https://ref.ly/Ps25:11), [18](https://ref.ly/Ps25:18)) as part of his anguish. Trust develops with understanding God’s character: He is compassionate, faithful, and good ([25:8–10](https://ref.ly/Ps25:8-Ps25:10)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 25:1–PSA 25:22

## Psalms 25:2 (id: 24311)

Enemies would rejoice by singing a victory song.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 25:2

## Psalms 25:4–6 (id: 24312)

The right path*,* the path of wisdom (see [5:8](https://ref.ly/Ps5:8)), means being open to instruction that leads to life ([27:11](https://ref.ly/Ps27:11); [43:3](https://ref.ly/Ps43:3); [73:24](https://ref.ly/Ps73:24); [119:12](https://ref.ly/Ps119:12)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 25:4–PSA 25:6

## Psalms 25:4–7 (id: 24313)

In this prayer for guidance, compassion, and forgiveness, the psalmist turns to the Lord for instruction in wisdom. He confesses his past failures and acknowledges that his hope lies with his merciful Savior.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 25:4–PSA 25:7

## Psalms 25:5 (id: 24314)

Biblical hope does not mean wishing for an event to turn out favorably. Hope trusts the Lord’s will and gives the courage to face disappointments ([33:22](https://ref.ly/Ps33:22); [130:5](https://ref.ly/Ps130:5)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 25:5

## Psalms 25:6 (id: 24315)

compassion: See also [51:1](https://ref.ly/Ps51:1); [57:1](https://ref.ly/Ps57:1); [103:8](https://ref.ly/Ps103:8).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 25:6

## Psalms 25:8–10 (id: 24316)

The Lord keeps his people close to himself.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 25:8–PSA 25:10

## Psalms 25:11 (id: 24302)

The psalmist again asks forgiveness for his many sins ([25:7](https://ref.ly/Ps25:7); [32:1–5](https://ref.ly/Ps32:1-Ps32:5)). The sins of Israel’s kings demonstrated the weaknesses inherent in David’s dynasty and the reasons for its failure in Old Testament Israel (see [Ps 89](https://ref.ly/Ps89:1-Ps89:52)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 25:11

## Psalms 25:12–15 (id: 24303)

Those who fear the Lord will receive further instruction and experience God’s presence ([25:14](https://ref.ly/Ps25:14)) and blessing ([25:13](https://ref.ly/Ps25:13)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 25:12–PSA 25:15

## Psalms 25:13 (id: 24304)

prosperity: See [23:6](https://ref.ly/Ps23:6). • inherit the land: Unlike the wicked, who will perish ([1:6](https://ref.ly/Ps1:6)), the godly have a secure future. In the end, God will bless them, and their blessings will endure (see [37:9](https://ref.ly/Ps37:9), [11](https://ref.ly/Ps37:11), [22](https://ref.ly/Ps37:22), [29](https://ref.ly/Ps37:29), [34](https://ref.ly/Ps37:34); [Isa 57:13](https://ref.ly/Isa57:13); [Matt 5:5](https://ref.ly/Matt5:5)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 25:13

## Psalms 25:15 (id: 24306)

the traps of my enemies: See [5:9–10](https://ref.ly/Ps5:9-Ps5:10); [31:4](https://ref.ly/Ps31:4); [140:5](https://ref.ly/Ps140:5); [Prov 3:26](https://ref.ly/Prov3:26).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 25:15

## Psalms 25:15–22 (id: 24305)

The psalmist expresses confidence in the Lord, commits to a life of integrity, and prays for rescue.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 25:15–PSA 25:22

## Psalms 25:17–18 (id: 24307)

The psalmist can find no relief (see [4:1](https://ref.ly/Ps4:1); [13:1–2](https://ref.ly/Ps13:1-Ps13:2)) as his problems go from bad to worse. He associates his anguish with sin, but he does not elaborate on the nature of his sin (see [25:7](https://ref.ly/Ps25:7), [11](https://ref.ly/Ps25:11)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 25:17–PSA 25:18

## Psalms 25:19–20 (id: 24308)

Knowing that the Lord hates violent people (see [11:5](https://ref.ly/Ps11:5)), the psalmist pleads with God to deal with these enemies.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 25:19–PSA 25:20

## Psalms 25:21 (id: 24310)

Just as it opened, the psalm closes with a commitment of trust and hope (see [9:18](https://ref.ly/Ps9:18); [25:5](https://ref.ly/Ps25:5)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 25:21

## Psalms 26:1–3 (id: 24318)

The psalmist opens himself to divine examination of his life, especially in the areas of his character and devotion.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 26:1–PSA 26:3

## Psalms 26:1–12 (id: 24317)

In this individual lament, the psalmist prays for redemption on the basis of his own innocence and the Lord’s justice.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 26:1–PSA 26:12

## Psalms 26:3 (id: 24320)

For God’s truth to become part of one’s character requires a habitual commitment.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 26:3

## Psalms 26:4–5 (id: 24321)

Because of his devotion to the Lord ([26:1–3](https://ref.ly/Ps26:1-Ps26:3)), the psalmist dissociates himself from evil people (see [1:1](https://ref.ly/Ps1:1)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 26:4–PSA 26:5

## Psalms 26:6 (id: 24323)

Ritual purity required the worshiper to wash their hands*,* symbolic of separation from evil and evildoers (see [73:13](https://ref.ly/Ps73:13)). • The altar symbolizes God’s presence ([43:4](https://ref.ly/Ps43:4)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 26:6

## Psalms 26:6–8 (id: 24322)

The psalmist demonstrates his loyalty to the Lord through pious rituals, praise, and acknowledgment of the Lord’s presence in the Temple.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 26:6–PSA 26:8

## Psalms 26:8 (id: 24324)

The sanctuary symbolized the manifest presence of the Lord (see [18:6](https://ref.ly/Ps18:6)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 26:8

## Psalms 26:9 (id: 24325)

Don’t let me suffer: The end of the godly cannot be the same as that of the wicked.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 26:9

## Psalms 26:12 (id: 24319)

The psalmist’s footing on solid ground represents salvation (cp. [143:10](https://ref.ly/Ps143:10)). • publicly: Or *in the great assembly* at the Temple ([26:6–8](https://ref.ly/Ps26:6-Ps26:8); [22:25](https://ref.ly/Ps22:25)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 26:12

## Psalms 27:1 (id: 24329)

Light expresses the Lord’s goodness ([27:13](https://ref.ly/Ps27:13); see [4:6](https://ref.ly/Ps4:6); [23:6](https://ref.ly/Ps23:6); [31:19](https://ref.ly/Ps31:19); [38:10](https://ref.ly/Ps38:10); [43:3](https://ref.ly/Ps43:3); [56:13](https://ref.ly/Ps56:13)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 27:1

## Psalms 27:1–3 (id: 24327)

The psalmist acknowledges the Lord at the center of his life ([27:1](https://ref.ly/Ps27:1)). Because of God’s presence, he engages his adversaries with confidence. They cannot intimidate him or penetrate his inner security.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 27:1–PSA 27:3

## Psalms 27:1–14 (id: 24326)

This psalm mixes two genres—a psalm of confidence ([27:1–6](https://ref.ly/Ps27:1-Ps27:6)) and an individual lament ([27:7–14](https://ref.ly/Ps27:7-Ps27:14))—held together by the theme of longing for the Lord’s presence. The psalmist focuses on the Lord; his circumstances are secondary. The strength of the psalmist’s faith is expressed in his openness to the Lord’s instruction, timing, and priorities.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 27:1–PSA 27:14

## Psalms 27:2 (id: 24330)

The psalmist’s enemies seek to devour him by living at his expense (see study note on 14:4).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 27:2
* **Associated Articles:** Psalms 14:4 (ID: `24087@TyndaleStudyNotes`)

## Psalms 27:3 (id: 24331)

remain confident: See [25:2](https://ref.ly/Ps25:2); [26:1](https://ref.ly/Ps26:1).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 27:3

## Psalms 27:4–6 (id: 24332)

Searching for and enjoying the Lord’s presence provides the psalmist’s foundation for confidence and security. He lives in the assurance of God’s protection and looks forward to offering sacrifices of thanksgiving and praise (see [18:6](https://ref.ly/Ps18:6)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 27:4–PSA 27:6

## Psalms 27:5 (id: 24333)

sanctuary (or *tabernacle*): This early shrine was the Israelites’ place of worship before the Temple was constructed.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 27:5

## Psalms 27:6 (id: 24334)

hold my head high: A sign of victory. • The granting of the request of [27:4](https://ref.ly/Ps27:4) prompts sacrifices with shouts of joy.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 27:6

## Psalms 27:7–8 (id: 24336)

Unlike the wicked ([10:4](https://ref.ly/Ps10:4)), who only want a temporary advantage ([78:34–36](https://ref.ly/Ps78:34-Ps78:36)), the godly search for the Lord as a thirsty person searches for water in the desert ([63:1](https://ref.ly/Ps63:1); [105:4](https://ref.ly/Ps105:4); [119:2](https://ref.ly/Ps119:2), [10](https://ref.ly/Ps119:10); [Matt 6:33](https://ref.ly/Matt6:33)). They act wisely ([Ps 34:10](https://ref.ly/Ps34:10), [14](https://ref.ly/Ps34:14)) while waiting for the Lord to resolve their crisis ([34:4](https://ref.ly/Ps34:4); [69:6](https://ref.ly/Ps69:6); [77:2](https://ref.ly/Ps77:2); [119:58](https://ref.ly/Ps119:58)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 27:7–PSA 27:8

## Psalms 27:7–12 (id: 24335)

The psalmist requests the Lord’s mercy, presence, and instruction. God is the psalmist’s greatest good; enemies and other circumstances are peripheral.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 27:7–PSA 27:12

## Psalms 27:13–14 (id: 24328)

The psalmist expresses confidence and hope in the Lord’s presence. To live in faith means to wait patiently in recognition of the Lord’s goodness. Such a life is not always pleasant for the godly ([42:2–3](https://ref.ly/Ps42:2-Ps42:3); [43:5](https://ref.ly/Ps43:5)), but their future is secure ([37:9](https://ref.ly/Ps37:9); [130:7](https://ref.ly/Ps130:7); see [9:18](https://ref.ly/Ps9:18)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 27:13–PSA 27:14

## Psalms 28:1 (id: 24339)

if you are silent: The psalmist appeals to the Lord to take action ([35:22](https://ref.ly/Ps35:22); [50:3](https://ref.ly/Ps50:3); [83:1](https://ref.ly/Ps83:1); [109:1](https://ref.ly/Ps109:1)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 28:1

## Psalms 28:1–2 (id: 24337)

The psalmist urges the Lord to listen; his urgency flows out of the tension between his deep relationship with the Lord and the adversity he faces.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 28:1–PSA 28:2

## Psalms 28:1–9 (id: 24338)

In this individual lament, the psalmist pleads for justice and mercy. He expresses confidence in the Lord’s strength and faithfulness, and he intercedes for the Lord’s people.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 28:1–PSA 28:9

## Psalms 28:2 (id: 24340)

It was common to lift up one’s hands in a gesture of devoted prayer ([63:4](https://ref.ly/Ps63:4); [134:2](https://ref.ly/Ps134:2)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 28:2

## Psalms 28:3–5 (id: 24341)

The psalmist curses his enemies, asking God for retribution and vindication.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 28:3–PSA 28:5

## Psalms 28:5 (id: 24342)

The wicked do not acknowledge the difference between the sacred and the common, so they have no respect for the Lord’s creation, redemption, or revelation.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 28:5

## Psalms 28:6–8 (id: 24343)

The psalmist anticipates rescue because of his confidence in the Lord’s justice.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 28:6–PSA 28:8

## Psalms 28:7 (id: 24344)

my strength and shield: The Lord protects the psalmist (see [59:9](https://ref.ly/Ps59:9), [17](https://ref.ly/Ps59:17)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 28:7

## Psalms 28:9 (id: 24345)

The poem closes with intercession for the Lord’s people. • Bless Israel, your special possession: See [29:11](https://ref.ly/Ps29:11); [133:3](https://ref.ly/Ps133:3).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 28:9

## Psalms 29:1–2 (id: 24347)

The psalmist issues a call to honor the Lord for his power (cp. [96:7–8](https://ref.ly/Ps96:7-Ps96:8)). • you heavenly beings: Angels or deities who, some believed, held special powers. The psalmist did not believe in other deities but called on people who thought they were real to look to the Lord as the only God.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 29:1–PSA 29:2

## Psalms 29:1–11 (id: 24346)

This nature hymn in praise of the Creator declares that the Lord holds all power over nature. God uses the same unsurpassed strength to care for his people.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 29:1–PSA 29:11

## Psalms 29:3–9 (id: 24350)

The word translated voice (Hebrew qol) can also mean “noise” ([1 Kgs 1:45](https://ref.ly/1Kgs1:45)) or “thunder” ([Joel 3:16](https://ref.ly/Joel3:16)). The Lord’s voice is awe\-inspiring, and it dominates whatever rumblings people might attribute to other deities.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 29:3–PSA 29:9

## Psalms 29:5 (id: 24351)

The cedars of Lebanon were known for their size and quality (see [Isa 2:13](https://ref.ly/Isa2:13)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 29:5

## Psalms 29:6 (id: 24352)

Lebanon’s mountains and Hermon are high mountains to the north of Israel. • The Lord can cause even immense mountains to shake at his command (see [114:4](https://ref.ly/Ps114:4)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 29:6

## Psalms 29:8 (id: 24353)

The wilderness of Kadesh was located south of Judah. God’s voice can be heard throughout the land, from the north ([29:6](https://ref.ly/Ps29:6)) to the south.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 29:8

## Psalms 29:10 (id: 24348)

The image of powerful floodwaters connects with the Genesis flood ([Gen 6:17](https://ref.ly/Gen6:17)). The Lord reigns as king over the whole created order; no one contests his kingdom.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 29:10

## Psalms 29:11 (id: 24349)

The ruler of nature blesses his people with peace (see [28:8–9](https://ref.ly/Ps28:8-Ps28:9); [37:11](https://ref.ly/Ps37:11); [133:3](https://ref.ly/Ps133:3)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 29:11

## Psalms 30:1 (id: 24365)

I will exalt you is a call to lift up the Lord’s name in praise and thanksgiving ([34:3](https://ref.ly/Ps34:3); [81:1](https://ref.ly/Ps81:1); [99:5](https://ref.ly/Ps99:5), [9](https://ref.ly/Ps99:9); [107:32](https://ref.ly/Ps107:32); [118:28](https://ref.ly/Ps118:28); [145:1](https://ref.ly/Ps145:1); see [Exod 15:1](https://ref.ly/Exod15:1); [Isa 25:1](https://ref.ly/Isa25:1)). • you rescued me: God pulled the psalmist from death ([Ps 30:3](https://ref.ly/Ps30:3)). • In his justice and care, God refused to let the psalmist’s enemies triumph (see [26:9](https://ref.ly/Ps26:9); [27:12](https://ref.ly/Ps27:12); [28:3](https://ref.ly/Ps28:3); [31:8](https://ref.ly/Ps31:8)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 30:1

## Psalms 30:1–3 (id: 24364)

The psalmist praises God for his triumph over adversity, which he likens to salvation from the grave.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 30:1–PSA 30:3

## Psalms 30:1–12 (id: 24363)

This individual thanksgiving psalm opens in praise to the Lord for his salvation ([30:1–3](https://ref.ly/Ps30:1-Ps30:3)), then contrasts God’s favor with his anger ([30:4–7](https://ref.ly/Ps30:4-Ps30:7)), and ends with a transformation from mourning to dancing ([30:8–12](https://ref.ly/Ps30:8-Ps30:12)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 30:1–PSA 30:12

## Psalms 30:title (id: 24369)

wrote this psalm in advance for the dedication of the Temple*,* making his own experience representative of the nation’s.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 30:1

## Psalms 30:4 (id: 24366)

The godly should celebrate the Lord’s acts of rescue with song and praise ([33:21](https://ref.ly/Ps33:21); [97:12](https://ref.ly/Ps97:12); [103:1](https://ref.ly/Ps103:1); [105:3](https://ref.ly/Ps105:3); [145:21](https://ref.ly/Ps145:21)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 30:4

## Psalms 30:6–7 (id: 24367)

Nothing can stop me now! The psalmist confesses his presumptuous attitude (cp. [32:3–4](https://ref.ly/Ps32:3-Ps32:4)). • secure as a mountain: In the psalms, this phrase creates a powerful image of stability and of God’s control (see [11:1](https://ref.ly/Ps11:1); [18:7](https://ref.ly/Ps18:7); [36:6](https://ref.ly/Ps36:6); [46:2](https://ref.ly/Ps46:2); [72:3](https://ref.ly/Ps72:3); [76:4](https://ref.ly/Ps76:4); [83:14](https://ref.ly/Ps83:14); [97:5](https://ref.ly/Ps97:5); [114:4](https://ref.ly/Ps114:4), [6](https://ref.ly/Ps114:6); [125:2](https://ref.ly/Ps125:2)). • I was shattered: The absence of God’s favor destroys the security of the proud (cp. [104:27–30](https://ref.ly/Ps104:27-Ps104:30)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 30:6–PSA 30:7

## Psalms 30:8–12 (id: 24368)

The psalmist faced death (also in [30:1–3](https://ref.ly/Ps30:1-Ps30:3))—perhaps literally, perhaps figuratively. But when he turned to the Lord, the Lord rescued him and turned his mourning into joyful dancing. Only God’s favor can permanently and powerfully overcome human failure and the depths of despair.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 30:8–PSA 30:12

## Psalms 31:1–5 (id: 24371)

The Lord offers refuge to anyone who comes to him for protection. The psalmist trusts in and submits to the Lord. See also [71:1–3](https://ref.ly/Ps71:1-Ps71:3).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 31:1–PSA 31:5

## Psalms 31:1–24 (id: 24370)

The psalmist encourages the godly to find refuge in the Lord and wait for his salvation. Despite having had a death\-like experience, he testifies to the Lord’s faithfulness. This psalm foreshadows the suffering of Jesus ([Luke 23:46](https://ref.ly/Luke23:46)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 31:1–PSA 31:24

## Psalms 31:2 (id: 24380)

The psalmist issues an urgent call for the Lord to pay attention to his desperate situation ([71:2](https://ref.ly/Ps71:2); [88:2](https://ref.ly/Ps88:2); [102:2](https://ref.ly/Ps102:2)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 31:2

## Psalms 31:5 (id: 24381)

I entrust my spirit into your hand: Whether he lives or dies, the psalmist will trust his Lord. Jesus uttered these words on the cross just before he died ([Luke 23:46](https://ref.ly/Luke23:46)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 31:5

## Psalms 31:6–8 (id: 24382)

Trust in the Lord requires confidence that he has our best interests at heart.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 31:6–PSA 31:8

## Psalms 31:8 (id: 24383)

A safe place literally means a broad place, in contrast to a “narrow” or constricted place of distress (see [18:19](https://ref.ly/Ps18:19)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 31:8

## Psalms 31:9–13 (id: 24384)

In this prayer for mercy, the psalmist wedges a description of the intensity of suffering and the pain of rejection between two affirmations of trust ([31:6](https://ref.ly/Ps31:6), [14](https://ref.ly/Ps31:14)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 31:9–PSA 31:13

## Psalms 31:10 (id: 24372)

wasting away from within: This is a powerful description of how despair takes a toll on our physical well\-being.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 31:10

## Psalms 31:14–18 (id: 24373)

Hope does not confide in frail and changeable human beings but only in the Lord. The sufferer entrusts himself to God while waiting for the Lord’s justice.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 31:14–PSA 31:18

## Psalms 31:15 (id: 24374)

My future is in your hands: To relinquish control of timing is one way to express submission.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 31:15

## Psalms 31:17 (id: 24375)

The psalmist, who did not deserve to be disgraced*,* invokes the principle of retribution (see study note on 1:6; see also “Prayers for Vengeance” Theme Note).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 31:17
* **Associated Articles:** Psalms 1:6 (ID: `23658@TyndaleStudyNotes`); Prayers for Vengeance (ID: `500274@TyndaleStudyNotesThemes`)

## Psalms 31:19–20 (id: 24376)

Since the godly are under the Lord’s protection and shelter, evil has no power over them.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 31:19–PSA 31:20

## Psalms 31:19–24 (id: 24377)

The psalmist thanks the Lord for answering his prayer ([31:1–18](https://ref.ly/Ps31:1-Ps31:18)) and rescuing him.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 31:19–PSA 31:24

## Psalms 31:21–22 (id: 24378)

Praise the Lord: The psalmist expresses his joy at the experience of God’s goodness and love. Throughout his ordeal, the Lord has cared for him.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 31:21–PSA 31:22

## Psalms 31:23–24 (id: 24379)

Out of his own pain and renewed awareness of the Lord’s goodness, the psalmist turns to others who suffer. He holds out the promise of God’s loving care for those who persevere in hoping for the Lord.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 31:23–PSA 31:24

## Psalms 32:1–2 (id: 24386)

The Lord’s forgiveness restores people to fellowship with him, clears them of guilt*,* and gives them great joy. Paul quoted this text when explaining justification by faith alone ([Rom 4:4–8](https://ref.ly/Rom4:4-Rom4:8)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 32:1–PSA 32:2

## Psalms 32:1–11 (id: 24385)

This wisdom psalm of confession and thanksgiving encourages and exhorts the godly to learn from the psalmist’s experience of sin, denial, confession, and forgiveness. This psalm was one of the seven psalms of penitence used in the early church (also [Pss 6](https://ref.ly/Ps6:1-Ps6:10), [38](https://ref.ly/Ps38:1-Ps38:22), [51](https://ref.ly/Ps51:1-Ps51:19), [102](https://ref.ly/Ps102:1-Ps102:28), [130](https://ref.ly/Ps130:1-Ps130:8), [143](https://ref.ly/Ps143:1-Ps143:12)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 32:1–PSA 32:11

## Psalms 32:3–5 (id: 24388)

The psalmist acknowledges his own sin (see [19:12–13](https://ref.ly/Ps19:12-Ps19:13); [25:7](https://ref.ly/Ps25:7), [11](https://ref.ly/Ps25:11), [15–22](https://ref.ly/Ps25:15-Ps25:22)) and his resistance to confessing sin. The Lord pressed him hard until he confessed his guilt.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 32:3–PSA 32:5

## Psalms 32:4 (id: 24389)

The psalmist attributes his suffering directly to the Lord’s hand of discipline (cp. [38:2](https://ref.ly/Ps38:2); [39:10](https://ref.ly/Ps39:10)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 32:4

## Psalms 32:5 (id: 24390)

God has forgiven the guilt and rebellion of [32:1](https://ref.ly/Ps32:1). The Lord’s nature is to reconcile and forgive ([78:38](https://ref.ly/Ps78:38); [85:2](https://ref.ly/Ps85:2); [130:4](https://ref.ly/Ps130:4)), but he requires confession and repentance.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 32:5

## Psalms 32:6 (id: 24391)

The godly will learn from the psalmist’s experience to pray for forgiveness before it is too late.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 32:6

## Psalms 32:7 (id: 24392)

The Lord promises to be his people’s hiding place ([31:20](https://ref.ly/Ps31:20)). Instead of being overwhelmed by terror ([31:13](https://ref.ly/Ps31:13)), the psalmist is surrounded by songs of victory.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 32:7

## Psalms 32:8 (id: 24393)

God interrupts the psalmist’s teaching with a message that invites the godly to receive the Lord’s wisdom (see [5:8](https://ref.ly/Ps5:8); [23:3](https://ref.ly/Ps23:3); [25:4–6](https://ref.ly/Ps25:4-Ps25:6)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 32:8

## Psalms 32:9 (id: 24394)

The senseless person is not wise. Rejecting the Lord’s counsel ruins life and makes one like an animal (see [Isa 1:3](https://ref.ly/Isa1:3); [Jas 3:3](https://ref.ly/Jas3:3)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 32:9

## Psalms 32:10 (id: 24387)

Difficulties common to all of life will ensnare the wicked, whereas the Lord promises to protect the godly with his care.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 32:10

## Psalms 33:1–3 (id: 24396)

The psalmist exhorts the godly to praise the Lord with melodies*,* with a new song*,* and with skillfully\-played music.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 33:1–PSA 33:3

## Psalms 33:1–22 (id: 24395)

This hymn of creation (see also [Pss 8](https://ref.ly/Ps8:1-Ps8:9), [19](https://ref.ly/Ps19:1-Ps19:14), [104](https://ref.ly/Ps104:1-Ps104:35), [145](https://ref.ly/Ps145:1-Ps145:21)) might be a continuation of [Ps 32](https://ref.ly/Ps32:1-Ps32:11). It exhorts readers to praise God ([33:1–3](https://ref.ly/Ps33:1-Ps33:3)), to recognize the power of his word in creation ([33:4–7](https://ref.ly/Ps33:4-Ps33:7)), and to fear the Creator ([33:8–11](https://ref.ly/Ps33:8-Ps33:11)). It offers hope to forgiven sinners ([Ps 32](https://ref.ly/Ps32:1-Ps32:11)) that they can live a new life in the fear of the Lord and under divine protection.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 33:1–PSA 33:22

## Psalms 33:4–7 (id: 24405)

God’s word displays his character and his power.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 33:4–PSA 33:7

## Psalms 33:7 (id: 24406)

The nations surrounding Israel thought that the sea had divine power, but it is under God’s control, within boundaries that he set (see [104:8–10](https://ref.ly/Ps104:8-Ps104:10)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 33:7

## Psalms 33:8 (id: 24408)

The power of the Lord extends to all the nations (see 2; [96:1–3](https://ref.ly/Ps96:1-Ps96:3)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 33:8

## Psalms 33:8–11 (id: 24407)

Fear of the Lord begins with awe for God and for his powerful word. His word created everything and continues to order and sustain creation. He frustrates the plans of people who oppose his will.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 33:8–PSA 33:11

## Psalms 33:10 (id: 24397)

The plans and schemes of the mighty will not prevail, except by God’s will (see [Isa 8:9–10](https://ref.ly/Isa8:9-Isa8:10)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 33:10

## Psalms 33:11 (id: 24398)

God’s word still orders creation and will do so forever. • God’s intentions are marvelous ([40:5](https://ref.ly/Ps40:5); [92:5](https://ref.ly/Ps92:5)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 33:11

## Psalms 33:12 (id: 24399)

People who fear God are chosen as his inheritance (see [33:13–19](https://ref.ly/Ps33:13-Ps33:19)); this excludes rebellious people ([78:62](https://ref.ly/Ps78:62)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 33:12

## Psalms 33:13–19 (id: 24400)

From the heavens, the Lord searches out and cares for anyone who fears him (see [14:2–3](https://ref.ly/Ps14:2-Ps14:3)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 33:13–PSA 33:19

## Psalms 33:16–17 (id: 24401)

army . . . great strength . . . warhorse: Even military might is under God’s control (see [33:10–11](https://ref.ly/Ps33:10-Ps33:11); [Eccl 9:11](https://ref.ly/Eccl9:11)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 33:16–PSA 33:17

## Psalms 33:18 (id: 24402)

God watches over all who live by his counsel ([32:8](https://ref.ly/Ps32:8)). He protects, rescues, and remains close to them ([34:15–22](https://ref.ly/Ps34:15-Ps34:22)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 33:18

## Psalms 33:20–22 (id: 24403)

The godly respond to this magnificent vision of God’s power in creation and in the affairs of the world with an affirmation of trust, commitment, joy, and hope as they pray and wait for God’s rescue.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 33:20–PSA 33:22

## Psalms 33:22 (id: 24404)

Using a play on words, the psalmist contrasts his people’s sure hope (Hebrew yakhal) in the Lord with the supposed strength ([33:17](https://ref.ly/Ps33:17); Hebrew khayil) of the horses of the wicked.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 33:22

## Psalms 34:1 (id: 24419)

is another name for Achish (see [1 Sam 21:10–15](https://ref.ly/1Sam21:10-1Sam21:15)). The body of the psalm makes no explicit connection to this event.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 34:1

## Psalms 34:1–3 (id: 24410)

The psalmist exhorts the helpless to join him in praise.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 34:1–PSA 34:3

## Psalms 34:1–22 (id: 24409)

This wisdom psalm includes a thanksgiving hymn ([34:1–7](https://ref.ly/Ps34:1-Ps34:7)) that celebrates the Lord’s care for and protection of godly sufferers. It also includes an invitation to wisdom ([34:8–14](https://ref.ly/Ps34:8-Ps34:14)) and an exposition of wisdom concerning the Lord’s care for the needy and the suffering of the wicked ([34:15–22](https://ref.ly/Ps34:15-Ps34:22)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 34:1–PSA 34:22

## Psalms 34:5–6 (id: 24421)

The psalmist narrates his experiences of answered prayer.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 34:5–PSA 34:6

## Psalms 34:7 (id: 24422)

The angel of the Lord represented the Lord’s presence during the wilderness journey. He protected Israel from the forces of Egypt ([Exod 14:19–20](https://ref.ly/Exod14:19-Exod14:20)), and he will guard all the godly ([Ps 91:11](https://ref.ly/Ps91:11)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 34:7

## Psalms 34:8–14 (id: 24423)

The godly encourage everyone to seek wisdom, to fear the Lord, and to place themselves under the protection of the Lord’s angel.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 34:8–PSA 34:14

## Psalms 34:9–10 (id: 24424)

Fear of the Lord includes reverence and respect, and it motivates a life of wisdom (see [Prov 1:7](https://ref.ly/Prov1:7); [9:10](https://ref.ly/Prov9:10)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 34:9–PSA 34:10

## Psalms 34:11 (id: 24412)

Anyone who listens, even children*,* can become wise followers of God.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 34:11

## Psalms 34:11–13 (id: 24411)

Wisdom contains three components: fearing the Lord ([34:11](https://ref.ly/Ps34:11)), doing good ([34:14](https://ref.ly/Ps34:14)), and rejecting evil ([34:13](https://ref.ly/Ps34:13)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 34:11–PSA 34:13

## Psalms 34:12–16 (id: 24413)

Peter quotes this passage in his instructions for peaceful living ([1 Pet 3:10–12](https://ref.ly/1Pet3:10-1Pet3:12)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 34:12–PSA 34:16

## Psalms 34:13 (id: 24414)

Godly people control their words; speaking evil and telling lies are foolish (see [10:7](https://ref.ly/Ps10:7); cp. [17:1](https://ref.ly/Ps17:1)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 34:13

## Psalms 34:14 (id: 24415)

The way of peace leads to harmony and order, whereas evil destroys them (see [37:11](https://ref.ly/Ps37:11)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 34:14

## Psalms 34:15–16 (id: 24416)

The Lord distinguishes between wise and foolish people; he shows his concern for the wise by rescuing them from trouble ([34:15](https://ref.ly/Ps34:15), [17–20](https://ref.ly/Ps34:17-Ps34:20)), but he destroys the foolish ([34:16](https://ref.ly/Ps34:16), [21](https://ref.ly/Ps34:21)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 34:15–PSA 34:16

## Psalms 34:18 (id: 24417)

Those who are brokenhearted possess a spirit of deep contrition and dependence on the Lord. God accepts this spirit as a proper sacrifice ([51:17](https://ref.ly/Ps51:17)). The wicked hate the brokenhearted ([109:16](https://ref.ly/Ps109:16)), but the Lord heals them ([147:3](https://ref.ly/Ps147:3); see [Isa 57:15](https://ref.ly/Isa57:15); [61:1](https://ref.ly/Isa61:1)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 34:18

## Psalms 34:19–22 (id: 24418)

The godly might suffer, but the Lord will reward them in the end. Similarly, the wicked might prosper for a time, but ultimately they will perish ([1:6](https://ref.ly/Ps1:6); [34:15–16](https://ref.ly/Ps34:15-Ps34:16)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 34:19–PSA 34:22

## Psalms 34:20 (id: 24420)

Bones represent a person’s entire being (see [6:2](https://ref.ly/Ps6:2)). • not one of them is broken: John applied this statement to Jesus at the crucifixion ([John 19:36](https://ref.ly/John19:36)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 34:20

## Psalms 35:1–28 (id: 24425)

In this lament, the Lord’s troubled servant calls for God to see his circumstances and vindicate him.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 35:1–PSA 35:28

## Psalms 35:4–10 (id: 24434)

The psalmist longs for the Lord’s salvation. The language seems vindictive, but it arises from a desire for justice and for the Lord to care for the needy and oppressed.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 35:4–PSA 35:10

## Psalms 35:6 (id: 24435)

A path that is dark and slippery suggests instability and untimely doom under the Lord’s judgment (see [69:23](https://ref.ly/Ps69:23); [73:18](https://ref.ly/Ps73:18); [82:5](https://ref.ly/Ps82:5); [107:10](https://ref.ly/Ps107:10); [143:3](https://ref.ly/Ps143:3)). • The angel of the Lord is an agent of judgment as well as salvation.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 35:6

## Psalms 35:10 (id: 24426)

Nothing in the universe can compare with the Lord (see [86:8](https://ref.ly/Ps86:8); [89:6](https://ref.ly/Ps89:6), [8](https://ref.ly/Ps89:8); [Isa 40:18](https://ref.ly/Isa40:18), [25](https://ref.ly/Isa40:25)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 35:10

## Psalms 35:11 (id: 24428)

Malicious witnesses want nothing but violence (see [11:4–6](https://ref.ly/Ps11:4-Ps11:6); [54:3](https://ref.ly/Ps54:3)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 35:11

## Psalms 35:11–18 (id: 24427)

The psalmist presents the Lord with the reasons for his suffering. Evil has many faces. He is tired and worn out, and he knows that only the Lord can help him.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 35:11–PSA 35:18

## Psalms 35:16 (id: 24429)

The psalmist’s attackers snarl to express their bitter envy.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 35:16

## Psalms 35:19 (id: 24431)

John applied this claim of innocence (see also [69:4](https://ref.ly/Ps69:4)) to Jesus ([John 15:25](https://ref.ly/John15:25)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 35:19

## Psalms 35:19–25 (id: 24430)

In this prayer for vindication, the psalmist’s crisis looms so large that a resolution must be found in the Lord. The psalmist has taken the high road, believing that vengeance belongs to the Lord. God’s patience hardens the hearts of the wicked and gives them reasons to justify their evil lifestyle.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 35:19–PSA 35:25

## Psalms 35:21 (id: 24432)

Aha! . . . Look: Both words translate the same expression of glee (Hebrew he’akh).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 35:21

## Psalms 35:26–28 (id: 24433)

The psalmist calls on the Lord to judge the wicked and to rescue the godly and bring them joy.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 35:26–PSA 35:28

## Psalms 36:1 (id: 24440)

no fear of God: Paul includes this phrase in his description of the depravity of all people ([Rom 3:18](https://ref.ly/Rom3:18)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 36:1

## Psalms 36:1–4 (id: 24437)

Fools despise what is wise and good as they pursue evil.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 36:1–PSA 36:4

## Psalms 36:1–12 (id: 24436)

This lament contrasts the world of folly devised by the wicked with the world of wisdom created and sustained by the Lord. The wicked care only about themselves, whereas the Lord cares for all of creation. He will intervene to bring about justice in his world. The righteous will enjoy his protection, but the wicked will perish.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 36:1–PSA 36:12

## Psalms 36:5–6 (id: 24441)

God’s all\-encompassing goodness surpasses that of the created order. God graciously meets his people’s practical needs.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 36:5–PSA 36:6

## Psalms 36:5–9 (id: 24442)

As the source of wisdom, the Lord is reliable and incomparable. His faithful care extends to all parts of the created order.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 36:5–PSA 36:9

## Psalms 36:6–9 (id: 24443)

All creatures live by God’s grace ([1 Tim 4:10](https://ref.ly/1Tim4:10)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 36:6–PSA 36:9

## Psalms 36:7–8 (id: 24444)

God invites all humanity to the banquet in his house (cp. [Prov 9:1–6](https://ref.ly/Prov9:1-Prov9:6)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 36:7–PSA 36:8

## Psalms 36:9 (id: 24445)

Light represents salvation and celebration ([18:25–29](https://ref.ly/Ps18:25-Ps18:29); [27:1](https://ref.ly/Ps27:1); cp. [35:6](https://ref.ly/Ps35:6)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 36:9

## Psalms 36:10–11 (id: 24438)

Since God’s wisdom extends to all of creation, it protects the godly.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 36:10–PSA 36:11

## Psalms 36:12 (id: 24439)

The psalmist remains confident that the disorder caused by the wicked ([36:1–4](https://ref.ly/Ps36:1-Ps36:4)) will end when they meet their demise.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 36:12

## Psalms 37:1 (id: 24454)

envy: The jealous desire to have what others enjoy leads to further sin ([73:3](https://ref.ly/Ps73:3); [Prov 3:31](https://ref.ly/Prov3:31); [Jas 1:14–15](https://ref.ly/Jas1:14-Jas1:15); [4:1–2](https://ref.ly/Jas4:1-Jas4:2)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 37:1

## Psalms 37:1–9 (id: 24447)

The wise respond to evil by trusting in the Lord. Trust includes five dimensions: (1\) renouncing irritability and envy ([37:1–2](https://ref.ly/Ps37:1-Ps37:2)); (2\) delighting in the Lord ([37:3–4](https://ref.ly/Ps37:3-Ps37:4)); (3\) submitting to the Lord ([37:5–6](https://ref.ly/Ps37:5-Ps37:6)); (4\) practicing patience in hope ([37:7](https://ref.ly/Ps37:7)); and (5\) avoiding anger ([37:8–9](https://ref.ly/Ps37:8-Ps37:9)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 37:1–PSA 37:9

## Psalms 37:1–40 (id: 24446)

This psalm elaborates on the problems posed in [Ps 36](https://ref.ly/Ps36:1-Ps36:12): How should the godly respond to the reality of evil? When will the Lord bring justice? Why does he permit the wicked to destroy his created order? [Psalm 37](https://ref.ly/Ps37:1-Ps37:40) offers clear responses that reduce the tensions of life ([37:1–9](https://ref.ly/Ps37:1-Ps37:9), [34](https://ref.ly/Ps37:34)) and promise that the meek will have a future ([37:10–11](https://ref.ly/Ps37:10-Ps37:11), [39–40](https://ref.ly/Ps37:39-Ps37:40)). The alternating contrast between the godly and the wicked emphasizes the futility of folly ([37:12–24](https://ref.ly/Ps37:12-Ps37:24), [27–33](https://ref.ly/Ps37:27-Ps37:33)). The personal observations of the psalmist add a human touch ([37:25–26](https://ref.ly/Ps37:25-Ps37:26), [35–38](https://ref.ly/Ps37:35-Ps37:38)). He encourages viewing the inheritance of the land from a long\-range perspective: The earth belongs to the Lord, who will give it to those he blesses—the lowly and godly who trust in him, put their hope in him, and follow him (see [37:9](https://ref.ly/Ps37:9), [11](https://ref.ly/Ps37:11), [22](https://ref.ly/Ps37:22), [29](https://ref.ly/Ps37:29), [34](https://ref.ly/Ps37:34); see also [Isa 57:13](https://ref.ly/Isa57:13); [Matt 5:5](https://ref.ly/Matt5:5)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 37:1–PSA 37:40

## Psalms 37:2 (id: 24460)

Finite existence is part of the human condition (see [90:5–6](https://ref.ly/Ps90:5-Ps90:6); [92:7](https://ref.ly/Ps92:7); [102:4](https://ref.ly/Ps102:4), [11](https://ref.ly/Ps102:11); [103:15](https://ref.ly/Ps103:15); [129:6](https://ref.ly/Ps129:6); [Isa 40:7–8](https://ref.ly/Isa40:7-Isa40:8)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 37:2

## Psalms 37:3 (id: 24466)

To do good means cultivating a devotion to wisdom (see [34:14](https://ref.ly/Ps34:14); [Prov 3:5–7](https://ref.ly/Prov3:5-Prov3:7)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 37:3

## Psalms 37:3–4 (id: 24461)

The antidote to irritability and envy ([37:1](https://ref.ly/Ps37:1)) is trust in the Lord.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 37:3–PSA 37:4

## Psalms 37:4 (id: 24467)

To take delight in the Lord means aligning with the Lord’s way in order to enjoy him.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 37:4

## Psalms 37:6 (id: 24468)

Justice occurs when the Lord’s will triumphs and the godly experience his rescue ([Isa 45:8](https://ref.ly/Isa45:8); [51:5–6](https://ref.ly/Isa51:5-Isa51:6); [58:8](https://ref.ly/Isa58:8), [10–11](https://ref.ly/Isa58:10-Isa58:11)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 37:6

## Psalms 37:7 (id: 24469)

Be still: We should let the Lord be God rather than taking matters into our own hands.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 37:7

## Psalms 37:8 (id: 24470)

Irritability and anger quickly corrode character.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 37:8

## Psalms 37:9–11 (id: 24471)

The wicked will not possess the land*;* those who trust in the Lord will. The Lord promises an inheritance because he is committed to caring for his people.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 37:9–PSA 37:11

## Psalms 37:11 (id: 24448)

The Lord is the author of peace ([85:10](https://ref.ly/Ps85:10))—he brings peace to a chaotic world ([29:11](https://ref.ly/Ps29:11); [37:11](https://ref.ly/Ps37:11); [85:8](https://ref.ly/Ps85:8); [147:14](https://ref.ly/Ps147:14)). His wisdom guides the lowly into the way of peace ([119:165](https://ref.ly/Ps119:165); [Matt 5:5](https://ref.ly/Matt5:5)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 37:11

## Psalms 37:12–13 (id: 24449)

The wicked snarl to express their bitter envy. They plot to bring an end to the godly, but the Lord derides them because they cannot succeed ([2:4](https://ref.ly/Ps2:4)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 37:12–PSA 37:13

## Psalms 37:12–17 (id: 24450)

The wicked seek to destroy the Lord’s order, but he defeats them.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 37:12–PSA 37:17

## Psalms 37:14–15 (id: 24451)

The weapons of the wicked will turn against them (cp. [7:12–13](https://ref.ly/Ps7:12-Ps7:13)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 37:14–PSA 37:15

## Psalms 37:16 (id: 24452)

Being wise with modest means is better than having prosperity and power and being wicked ([Prov 15:16](https://ref.ly/Prov15:16); [16:8](https://ref.ly/Prov16:8), [19](https://ref.ly/Prov16:19); [17:1](https://ref.ly/Prov17:1); [28:6](https://ref.ly/Prov28:6)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 37:16

## Psalms 37:18–20 (id: 24453)

The Lord cares for the blameless in this life and for eternity, but the wicked will perish.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 37:18–PSA 37:20

## Psalms 37:20 (id: 24455)

Smoke depicts the temporary nature of life ([68:2](https://ref.ly/Ps68:2); [102:3](https://ref.ly/Ps102:3)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 37:20

## Psalms 37:21 (id: 24456)

To borrow and never repay is a behavior of a crooked lifestyle. • Generous givers freely share what they freely receive from the Lord (see [111:5](https://ref.ly/Ps111:5); [112:5](https://ref.ly/Ps112:5)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 37:21

## Psalms 37:23–24 (id: 24457)

The rectitude and strength of a godly person’s life comes from the Lord (see [Prov 4:12](https://ref.ly/Prov4:12); [14:15](https://ref.ly/Prov14:15); [16:9](https://ref.ly/Prov16:9); [20:24](https://ref.ly/Prov20:24)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 37:23–PSA 37:24

## Psalms 37:25–26 (id: 24458)

The Lord does not abandon his children or their descendants.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 37:25–PSA 37:26

## Psalms 37:27–33 (id: 24459)

The godly are wise; they do good and reject evil. The Lord cares for them, protecting them and ensuring that they receive their rightful portion of the land as their inheritance. The wicked might try to ambush the godly*,* but they will not succeed.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 37:27–PSA 37:33

## Psalms 37:30 (id: 24462)

The godly base their counsel on the Lord’s wisdom.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 37:30

## Psalms 37:31 (id: 24463)

They have made God’s law their own: The godly internalize God’s wisdom and instructions (see [119:11](https://ref.ly/Ps119:11); [Jer 24:7](https://ref.ly/Jer24:7); [31:31–34](https://ref.ly/Jer31:31-Jer31:34)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 37:31

## Psalms 37:35–36 (id: 24464)

The wicked might appear to be flourishing like a tree (cp. [52:8](https://ref.ly/Ps52:8); [92:12–13](https://ref.ly/Ps92:12-Ps92:13)), but they eventually die and are forgotten ([37:2](https://ref.ly/Ps37:2)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 37:35–PSA 37:36

## Psalms 37:39–40 (id: 24465)

The Lord provides strength for his people.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 37:39–PSA 37:40

## Psalms 38:1 (id: 24479)

The meaning of this phrase is uncertain (also in [70:title](https://ref.ly/Ps70:1)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 38:1

## Psalms 38:1–4 (id: 24474)

The psalmist’s sins had triggered the Lord’s anger and rage*,* resulting in the arrows and blows of discipline and rebuke*;* as a result, his whole body is sick.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 38:1–PSA 38:4

## Psalms 38:1–17 (id: 24472)

These verses form a prelude to the psalmist’s confession ([38:18](https://ref.ly/Ps38:18)) and describe his woeful condition.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 38:1–PSA 38:17

## Psalms 38:1–22 (id: 24473)

This psalm is a lament and prayer for healing. The psalmist’s suffering is associated with his unconfessed sin. He confesses his sin and entrusts his case to the Lord.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 38:1–PSA 38:22

## Psalms 38:3 (id: 24481)

Sin can lead to sickness and even death ([1 Cor 11:30](https://ref.ly/1Cor11:30)). Whether the psalmist actually felt physically ill or his sickness was a metaphor for emotional turmoil, he knew that it came from God and threatened his life (see [Pss 32:3](https://ref.ly/Ps32:3); [39:10](https://ref.ly/Ps39:10)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 38:3

## Psalms 38:4 (id: 24482)

The psalmist’s burden results from sin (see [40:12](https://ref.ly/Ps40:12); [41:4](https://ref.ly/Ps41:4); cp. [Gen 4:13](https://ref.ly/Gen4:13)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 38:4

## Psalms 38:5–8 (id: 24483)

The severity of God’s punishment brings anguish that affects every part of the psalmist’s being.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 38:5–PSA 38:8

## Psalms 38:9–12 (id: 24484)

The psalmist longs for a restored relationship with God, but he feels alienated. He finds himself lost and alone as his friends disappear.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 38:9–PSA 38:12

## Psalms 38:13 (id: 24475)

The psalmist suffers quietly before his opponents (see [Isa 53:7](https://ref.ly/Isa53:7)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 38:13

## Psalms 38:15 (id: 24476)

The Lord alone will resolve the conflict ([9:18](https://ref.ly/Ps9:18); [27:14](https://ref.ly/Ps27:14); [37:9](https://ref.ly/Ps37:9), [34](https://ref.ly/Ps37:34)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 38:15

## Psalms 38:17–20 (id: 24477)

No longer able to endure his suffering and teetering on the verge of collapse (cp. [15:5](https://ref.ly/Ps15:5)), the psalmist confesses his sin (see [32:5](https://ref.ly/Ps32:5)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 38:17–PSA 38:20

## Psalms 38:19 (id: 24478)

That the psalmist’s enemies hate him without reason compounds his pain.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 38:19

## Psalms 38:22 (id: 24480)

Asking the Lord to act quickly in times of great need is common in the Psalter ([22:19](https://ref.ly/Ps22:19); [31:2](https://ref.ly/Ps31:2); [40:13](https://ref.ly/Ps40:13); [69:17](https://ref.ly/Ps69:17); [70:1](https://ref.ly/Ps70:1); [71:12](https://ref.ly/Ps71:12); [79:8](https://ref.ly/Ps79:8); [102:2](https://ref.ly/Ps102:2); [141:1](https://ref.ly/Ps141:1); [143:7](https://ref.ly/Ps143:7)). However, wisdom and experience teach that God’s people must often wait for him to act ([27:14](https://ref.ly/Ps27:14); [37:7](https://ref.ly/Ps37:7); [Isa 8:17](https://ref.ly/Isa8:17); [40:31](https://ref.ly/Isa40:31)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 38:22

## Psalms 39:1 (id: 24490)

was a levitical singer appointed by David along with Asaph ([1 Chr 9:16](https://ref.ly/1Chr9:16); [16:38](https://ref.ly/1Chr16:38); [25:1](https://ref.ly/1Chr25:1)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 39:1

## Psalms 39:1–3 (id: 24486)

Suffering in silence only intensifies the psalmist’s anguish, pain, and inner turmoil.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 39:1–PSA 39:3

## Psalms 39:1–13 (id: 24485)

This prayer for rescue reflects the psalmist’s discouragement, which comes from having a limited perspective on his situation.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 39:1–PSA 39:13

## Psalms 39:4–5 (id: 24491)

how fleeting my life is: This perspective comes out of suffering (see [78:39](https://ref.ly/Ps78:39); [89:47–48](https://ref.ly/Ps89:47-Ps89:48); [90:3–10](https://ref.ly/Ps90:3-Ps90:10)). The human lifetime is but a moment to God ([90:4](https://ref.ly/Ps90:4)), as temporary as a breath (see [39:11](https://ref.ly/Ps39:11); [144:4](https://ref.ly/Ps144:4)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 39:4–PSA 39:5

## Psalms 39:4–6 (id: 24492)

Because of his suffering and sin, the psalmist concludes that life is meaningless and fleeting (see [Job 7:7–10](https://ref.ly/Job7:7-Job7:10); [Isa 40:6–8](https://ref.ly/Isa40:6-Isa40:8)). He had expected a wicked life to have those qualities (see [Pss 37:2](https://ref.ly/Ps37:2), [20](https://ref.ly/Ps37:20); [103:15–16](https://ref.ly/Ps103:15-Ps103:16)), but now whether a person is godly or not seems to be irrelevant.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 39:4–PSA 39:6

## Psalms 39:8 (id: 24493)

The idea that rebellion brings on suffering is a common thread in [Pss 32](https://ref.ly/Ps32:1-Ps32:11), [38–41](https://ref.ly/Ps38:1-Ps41:13).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 39:8

## Psalms 39:9–11 (id: 24494)

The psalmist links suffering with God’s discipline, assuming that it is punishment for his sin.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 39:9–PSA 39:11

## Psalms 39:11 (id: 24487)

The Lord uses discipline to correct his children ([38:1](https://ref.ly/Ps38:1), [3](https://ref.ly/Ps38:3), [7](https://ref.ly/Ps38:7); [40:12](https://ref.ly/Ps40:12); see [Prov 3:11–12](https://ref.ly/Prov3:11-Prov3:12); [Heb 12:5–6](https://ref.ly/Heb12:5-Heb12:6)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 39:11

## Psalms 39:12 (id: 24488)

A guest (or *foreigner*) had no rights of land ownership (see [Lev 25:23](https://ref.ly/Lev25:23)). The patriarchs had lived as guests in Canaan ([Ps 105:23](https://ref.ly/Ps105:23)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 39:12

## Psalms 39:13 (id: 24489)

Unlike the psalmist’s earlier request that God stay close to him ([38:21–22](https://ref.ly/Ps38:21-Ps38:22)), his present desire for God to leave him alone echoes Job’s disposition ([Job 7:17–19](https://ref.ly/Job7:17-Job7:19)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 39:13

## Psalms 40:1–5 (id: 24503)

The psalmist thanks the Lord for his rescue and testifies that God can be trusted.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 40:1–PSA 40:5

## Psalms 40:1–17 (id: 24502)

This psalm includes a thanksgiving song ([40:1–10](https://ref.ly/Ps40:1-Ps40:10)) followed by a lament ([40:11–17](https://ref.ly/Ps40:11-Ps40:17)). The thanksgiving song includes the reason for the thanksgiving ([40:1–5](https://ref.ly/Ps40:1-Ps40:5)), an affirmation of commitment ([40:6–8](https://ref.ly/Ps40:6-Ps40:8)), and a public testimony of God’s character ([40:7–10](https://ref.ly/Ps40:7-Ps40:10)). The lament concerns the psalmist’s troubles because of his sins ([40:11–12](https://ref.ly/Ps40:11-Ps40:12)) and is followed by two prayers for vindication ([40:13–15](https://ref.ly/Ps40:13-Ps40:15), [17](https://ref.ly/Ps40:17)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 40:1–PSA 40:17

## Psalms 40:6 (id: 24506)

The Lord delights in the attitude and character of the person making an offering more than in the offering itself. • Now that you have made me listen, I finally understand: Greek text reads *You have given me a body.* In [Heb 10:5–7](https://ref.ly/Heb10:5-Heb10:7), the writer quotes from the Greek version of [Ps 40:6–8](https://ref.ly/Ps40:6-Ps40:8). He casts the words as something Jesus said as he left heaven and came into the world.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 40:6

## Psalms 40:7 (id: 24507)

As is written about me in the Scriptures: Moses had recorded God’s requirements for Israel’s kings in [Deut 17:14–15](https://ref.ly/Deut17:14-Deut17:15).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 40:7

## Psalms 40:11 (id: 24504)

The psalmist prays that the Lord will be true to his character when answering this plea for mercy.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 40:11

## Psalms 40:12–17 (id: 24505)

The psalmist is troubled by both his adversities and his own sins and prays for rescue. • This passage is repeated almost verbatim as [Ps 70](https://ref.ly/Ps70:1-Ps70:5).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 40:12–PSA 40:17

## Psalms 41:1 (id: 24511)

The poor who suffer hardship have special protection under God’s law ([Lev 14:21](https://ref.ly/Lev14:21); [19:10](https://ref.ly/Lev19:10)); they receive God’s justice and godly rule ([Pss 72:13](https://ref.ly/Ps72:13); [82:3–4](https://ref.ly/Ps82:3-Ps82:4)). The word translated *poor* is often a synonym for the godly ([113:7](https://ref.ly/Ps113:7); see [Zeph 3:12](https://ref.ly/Zeph3:12)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 41:1

## Psalms 41:1–13 (id: 24508)

In this wisdom psalm, the psalmist prays for healing ([41:4](https://ref.ly/Ps41:4), [10](https://ref.ly/Ps41:10)), laments his distress ([41:5–9](https://ref.ly/Ps41:5-Ps41:9)), and expresses confidence in the Lord’s blessing ([41:1–3](https://ref.ly/Ps41:1-Ps41:3), [11–12](https://ref.ly/Ps41:11-Ps41:12)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 41:1–PSA 41:13

## Psalms 41:3 (id: 24512)

when they are sick: This illness might be physical or spiritual (see [6:2](https://ref.ly/Ps6:2); [Ps 38](https://ref.ly/Ps38:1-Ps38:22)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 41:3

## Psalms 41:4 (id: 24513)

The psalmist applies the blessing to himself ([41:12](https://ref.ly/Ps41:12)). Apparently he has taken care of the poor ([41:1](https://ref.ly/Ps41:1)), but he has sinned against the Lord in other ways. Out of his pain, he cries for healing while confessing his sin. The Lord alone can grant the restoration that brings true joy ([30:2](https://ref.ly/Ps30:2); [107:20–21](https://ref.ly/Ps107:20-Ps107:21)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 41:4

## Psalms 41:5 (id: 24515)

How soon will he die? The psalmist’s opponents regard his suffering as a divine judgment (cp. [1:6](https://ref.ly/Ps1:6)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 41:5

## Psalms 41:5–9 (id: 24514)

The psalmist’s enemies disguise themselves as friends, while his friends openly become his enemies.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 41:5–PSA 41:9

## Psalms 41:9 (id: 24516)

the one who shared my food: Eating together was a sign of unity ([Acts 2:42](https://ref.ly/Acts2:42)). Refusing to eat with someone indicated hostility ([1 Cor 5:11](https://ref.ly/1Cor5:11)). Jesus experienced the same kind of betrayal ([John 13:1](https://ref.ly/John13:1), [18](https://ref.ly/John13:18)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 41:9

## Psalms 41:11–12 (id: 24509)

The psalmist knows that the Lord has forgiven him and will bless him.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 41:11–PSA 41:12

## Psalms 41:13 (id: 24510)

This doxology closes Book One ([Pss 1–41](https://ref.ly/Ps1:1-Ps41:13)). Cp. [106:48](https://ref.ly/Ps106:48).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 41:13

## Psalms 42:1 (id: 24519)

were members of a Levitical choir appointed by David to serve as Temple singers (see [1 Chr 6:22–38](https://ref.ly/1Chr6:22-1Chr6:38); [9:19–34](https://ref.ly/1Chr9:19-1Chr9:34); [2 Chr 20:19](https://ref.ly/2Chr20:19)). Their ancestor Korah was the apostate who had rebelled against Moses and whom the earth swallowed up ([Exod 6:24](https://ref.ly/Exod6:24); [Num 16](https://ref.ly/Num16:1-Num16:50)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 42:1

## Psalms 42:1–4 (id: 24518)

The psalmist’s longing for God comes from being geographically distant from the Temple as he remembers the past. • The verb translated longs is found only here and in [Joel 1:20](https://ref.ly/Joel1:20) (“cry out”); in both cases it refers to extreme thirst in a waterless desert (see [Pss 63:1](https://ref.ly/Ps63:1); [143:6](https://ref.ly/Ps143:6); see also [84:2](https://ref.ly/Ps84:2)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 42:1–PSA 42:4

## Psalms 42:1–43.5 (id: 24517)

These psalms, like [Pss 9](https://ref.ly/Ps9:1-Ps9:20) and[10](https://ref.ly/Ps10:1-Ps10:18), form a unit comprising a lament with a bittersweet refrain of hope ([42:5](https://ref.ly/Ps42:5), [11](https://ref.ly/Ps42:11); [43:5](https://ref.ly/Ps43:5)). In many Hebrew manuscripts these two psalms are combined as one. The historical context is uncertain; these psalms might be the voice of God’s people in exile, confessing their loyalty to God as he punishes them for their prevailing apostasy. The psalmist longs for fellowship with God such as he enjoyed in Jerusalem ([42:4](https://ref.ly/Ps42:4)); his memories only make him more discouraged. As the psalmist cries out to God, he recalls God’s love and faithfulness ([42:8](https://ref.ly/Ps42:8)), which moves him to plead for vindication ([43:1–4](https://ref.ly/Ps43:1-Ps43:4)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 42:1–PSA 43:5

## Psalms 42:3 (id: 24520)

Having tears for food speaks of great grief ([80:5](https://ref.ly/Ps80:5); [102:9](https://ref.ly/Ps102:9); see [6:6](https://ref.ly/Ps6:6); [56:8](https://ref.ly/Ps56:8); [119:136](https://ref.ly/Ps119:136); [126:5](https://ref.ly/Ps126:5)). • The wicked try to hold God to their timetable and deny his power to intervene.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 42:3

## Psalms 42:4 (id: 24521)

The psalmist recalls leading a great procession as a member of the Levitical choir, possibly during the high holy days.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 42:4

## Psalms 42:5 (id: 24523)

The psalmist feels depressed, but it does not incapacitate him. He remembers that the living God is his Savior. This verse is repeated in [42:11](https://ref.ly/Ps42:11) and [43:5](https://ref.ly/Ps43:5).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 42:5

## Psalms 42:5–6 (id: 24522)

The psalmist encourages himself with questions and answers.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 42:5–PSA 42:6

## Psalms 42:6 (id: 24524)

Mount Hermon is a high mountain range northeast of Israel. The source of the Jordan is by Dan at the foot of Mount Hermon. • Mount Mizar might be a peak in the Mount Hermon range.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 42:6

## Psalms 42:7 (id: 24525)

The raging seas*,* waves*,* and surging tides conjure images of God’s wrath (see [88:7](https://ref.ly/Ps88:7)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 42:7

## Psalms 42:8 (id: 24526)

The psalmist sees rays of hope. A life oriented to God includes songs of joy and praying for justice and vindication ([42:9–10](https://ref.ly/Ps42:9-Ps42:10); [43:1–4](https://ref.ly/Ps43:1-Ps43:4)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 42:8

## Psalms 42:9–10 (id: 24527)

The psalmist brings his many doubts, discouragements, and questions directly to God.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 42:9–PSA 42:10

## Psalms 43:1–4 (id: 24528)

The psalmist turns to the Lord for rescue from his troubles, for guidance, for restoration, and for vindication.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 43:1–PSA 43:4

## Psalms 43:2 (id: 24529)

tossed me aside: Other psalms similarly ask whether God has rejected his people ([44:9](https://ref.ly/Ps44:9), [23](https://ref.ly/Ps44:23); [60:1](https://ref.ly/Ps60:1), [10](https://ref.ly/Ps60:10); [74:1](https://ref.ly/Ps74:1); [77:7](https://ref.ly/Ps77:7); [88:14](https://ref.ly/Ps88:14); [89:38](https://ref.ly/Ps89:38); [108:11](https://ref.ly/Ps108:11)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 43:2

## Psalms 43:3 (id: 24530)

In this prayer for God’s redemption, light and truth are viewed as guides (see [18:25–29](https://ref.ly/Ps18:25-Ps18:29); [27:1](https://ref.ly/Ps27:1); [85:10–13](https://ref.ly/Ps85:10-Ps85:13); [89:14–18](https://ref.ly/Ps89:14-Ps89:18); see also [119:105](https://ref.ly/Ps119:105); [John 3:19](https://ref.ly/John3:19); [Eph 5:8](https://ref.ly/Eph5:8); [1 Thes 5:5–7](https://ref.ly/1Thess5:5-1Thess5:7)). • The Temple on the mountain in Jerusalem symbolized God’s holy presence among his people ([Pss 15:1](https://ref.ly/Ps15:1); [43:3](https://ref.ly/Ps43:3); [99:5](https://ref.ly/Ps99:5), [9](https://ref.ly/Ps99:9); [132:7](https://ref.ly/Ps132:7)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 43:3

## Psalms 43:5 (id: 24531)

This verse is repeated in [42:5](https://ref.ly/Ps42:5), [11](https://ref.ly/Ps42:11).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 43:5

## Psalms 44:1 (id: 24534)

we have heard . . . of all you did: The story of redemption encompasses the story of God’s favor and power in his past acts of rescue (see [78:1–4](https://ref.ly/Ps78:1-Ps78:4); see also [Pss 105–106](https://ref.ly/Ps105:1-Ps106:48)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 44:1

## Psalms 44:1–26 (id: 24532)

This national lament after defeat in battle continues the tone of the previous two psalms, including reflecting on an unspecified moment in Israel’s history and calling on God for salvation. The people recite God’s past acts of rescue ([44:1–3](https://ref.ly/Ps44:1-Ps44:3)), acknowledge God’s power to save ([44:4–8](https://ref.ly/Ps44:4-Ps44:8)), describe their humiliation in exile ([44:9–16](https://ref.ly/Ps44:9-Ps44:16)), claim their innocence and lament the injustice of their current situation ([44:17–22](https://ref.ly/Ps44:17-Ps44:22)), and cry for vindication ([44:23–26](https://ref.ly/Ps44:23-Ps44:26)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 44:1–PSA 44:26

## Psalms 44:2 (id: 24538)

God drove out the pagan nations during the conquests recorded in Joshua.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 44:2

## Psalms 44:3 (id: 24539)

Though the Israelites used swords and other weapons ([44:6](https://ref.ly/Ps44:6)), they would have lost their battles without the light of the Lord’s favor (see [18:25–29](https://ref.ly/Ps18:25-Ps18:29); [27:1](https://ref.ly/Ps27:1); [89:15](https://ref.ly/Ps89:15)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 44:3

## Psalms 44:4–8 (id: 24540)

God’s people feel confident about his mighty acts; he was with them in the past, and he is their king in the present.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 44:4–PSA 44:8

## Psalms 44:9–16 (id: 24541)

The people have experienced defeat ([44:9–12](https://ref.ly/Ps44:9-Ps44:12)), so they understand suffering and disgrace ([44:13–16](https://ref.ly/Ps44:13-Ps44:16)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 44:9–PSA 44:16

## Psalms 44:11 (id: 24533)

scattered us among the nations: This probably refers to the Exile (see [51:18–19](https://ref.ly/Ps51:18-Ps51:19); [89:38–51](https://ref.ly/Ps89:38-Ps89:51); [106:40–47](https://ref.ly/Ps106:40-Ps106:47); [137](https://ref.ly/Ps137:1-Ps137:9)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 44:11

## Psalms 44:22 (id: 24535)

Paul quotes this verse as a parenthetical aside in his list of things that cannot separate us from Christ’s love ([Rom 8:36](https://ref.ly/Rom8:36)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 44:22

## Psalms 44:23 (id: 24537)

Wake up: Biblical authors often call for God’s attention in a crisis ([35:23](https://ref.ly/Ps35:23); [44:23](https://ref.ly/Ps44:23); [73:20](https://ref.ly/Ps73:20); [80:2](https://ref.ly/Ps80:2); [Mark 4:38](https://ref.ly/Mark4:38)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 44:23

## Psalms 44:23–26 (id: 24536)

In the end, God’s people can turn to the Lord and trust him for rescue. Their petition for God to remedy their situation is as strong as their lament about God’s rejection.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 44:23–PSA 44:26

## Psalms 45:1 (id: 24545)

is no longer known (see also [Ps 69](https://ref.ly/Ps69:1-Ps69:36)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 45:1

## Psalms 45:1–17 (id: 24542)

This psalm celebrates a royal wedding; it might have been sung on many occasions and not just at one wedding. As God’s representative, the king carried the responsibility of dispensing justice and maintaining order in God’s world (see [Ps 2](https://ref.ly/Ps2:1-Ps2:12)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 45:1–PSA 45:17

## Psalms 45:2 (id: 24546)

This general description of the king’s symbolic status anticipates his permanent legacy ([45:16](https://ref.ly/Ps45:16)). That the Lord has blessed him and charged him to bear God’s attributes is symbolized by his handsome appearance and gracious words.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 45:2

## Psalms 45:3 (id: 24548)

Glory and majesty belong to the Lord ([96:6](https://ref.ly/Ps96:6); [111:3](https://ref.ly/Ps111:3)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 45:3

## Psalms 45:3–5 (id: 24547)
