[Exod 15:13](https://ref.ly/Exod15:13)). • your own special possession: This is another expression for “your people” ([Pss 28:9](https://ref.ly/Ps28:9); [78:62](https://ref.ly/Ps78:62); [94:14](https://ref.ly/Ps94:14); [106:40](https://ref.ly/Ps106:40)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 74:2

## Psalms 74:3–8 (id: 24876)

Like a guide, the psalmist points out to the Lord what took place during the destruction of Jerusalem in 586 BC.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 74:3–PSA 74:8

## Psalms 74:12 (id: 24870)

my king from ages past: The psalmist acknowledges God’s power and his historical bond with Israel ([5:2](https://ref.ly/Ps5:2); [44:4](https://ref.ly/Ps44:4); [84:3](https://ref.ly/Ps84:3)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 74:12

## Psalms 74:14 (id: 24871)

Leviathan: See [104:26](https://ref.ly/Ps104:26); [Job 3:8](https://ref.ly/Job3:8); [41:1](https://ref.ly/Job41:1), [12](https://ref.ly/Job41:12), [22](https://ref.ly/Job41:22), [31](https://ref.ly/Job41:31); [Isa 27:1](https://ref.ly/Isa27:1). Here, the creature’s multiple heads suggest a mythical monster.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 74:14

## Psalms 74:15 (id: 24872)

springs and streams to gush forth: God provided water in the desert for his people (see [68:8–9](https://ref.ly/Ps68:8-Ps68:9); [Exod 17:6](https://ref.ly/Exod17:6)); he dried up the Red Sea ([Exod 14:21](https://ref.ly/Exod14:21)) and the Jordan River ([Josh 3:17](https://ref.ly/Josh3:17)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 74:15

## Psalms 74:19–23 (id: 24873)

The poet urges God to act.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 74:19–PSA 74:23

## Psalms 75:1–10 (id: 24877)

This hymn of thanksgiving includes two direct messages from God that provide assurance of his justice ([75:2–3](https://ref.ly/Ps75:2-Ps75:3), [10](https://ref.ly/Ps75:10)). The Lord rebukes arrogant people who defy him, promising to forcibly humble them ([75:4–8](https://ref.ly/Ps75:4-Ps75:8)). Together, the community and the psalmist respond with thanksgiving for God’s character ([75:1](https://ref.ly/Ps75:1), [9](https://ref.ly/Ps75:9)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 75:1–PSA 75:10

## Psalms 75:2–8 (id: 24878)

The Lord will bring justice in his own time.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 75:2–PSA 75:8

## Psalms 75:4–5 (id: 24879)

The wicked arrogantly defy the heavens—the dwelling place of God. Through their boasting they insist that they are wiser than God.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 75:4–PSA 75:5

## Psalms 75:6 (id: 24880)

No creature has the right to rebel against its Creator.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 75:6

## Psalms 75:7–8 (id: 24881)

The Lord alone is the Judge, with the power to exalt and humble (see [1 Sam 2:7](https://ref.ly/1Sam2:7); [Luke 1:52](https://ref.ly/Luke1:52)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 75:7–PSA 75:8

## Psalms 76:1 (id: 24884)

The Greek version reads *for the Assyrian.*

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 76:1

## Psalms 76:1–3 (id: 24883)

God’s victory over Zion’s enemies foreshadows his worldwide victory over all his enemies.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 76:1–PSA 76:3

## Psalms 76:1–12 (id: 24882)

This psalm appears to celebrate a victory. The victory might have been recent, such as over the Assyrians (see note on [76:title](https://ref.ly/Ps76:1); see also [Isa 37](https://ref.ly/Isa37:1-Isa37:38)); or the psalm might be recalling God’s great acts of rescue in the past.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 76:1–PSA 76:12

## Psalms 76:3 (id: 24885)

God brings an end to the attacks of his enemies (see [46:9](https://ref.ly/Ps46:9)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 76:3

## Psalms 76:4 (id: 24887)

The victorious king’s splendor, glory, and majesty are greater than anything in the created order ([8:1](https://ref.ly/Ps8:1); [29:4](https://ref.ly/Ps29:4); [111:3](https://ref.ly/Ps111:3)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 76:4

## Psalms 76:4–6 (id: 24886)

The psalmist praises God for his achievement and for his glorious majesty.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 76:4–PSA 76:6

## Psalms 76:7 (id: 24889)

The word translated feared (Hebrew nora’) is a wordplay on the word translated “glorious” in [76:4](https://ref.ly/Ps76:4) (Hebrew na’or).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 76:7

## Psalms 76:7–9 (id: 24888)

The needy await their victorious God, while the wicked stand in fear of him.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 76:7–PSA 76:9

## Psalms 77:1–3 (id: 24891)

The night provides a special opportunity for prayer and meditation ([77:6](https://ref.ly/Ps77:6), [11](https://ref.ly/Ps77:11); see [6:6](https://ref.ly/Ps6:6); [16:7](https://ref.ly/Ps16:7); [17:3](https://ref.ly/Ps17:3); [30:5](https://ref.ly/Ps30:5); [63:6](https://ref.ly/Ps63:6); [119:55](https://ref.ly/Ps119:55), [62](https://ref.ly/Ps119:62), [148](https://ref.ly/Ps119:148)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 77:1–PSA 77:3

## Psalms 77:1–20 (id: 24890)

The psalmist laments that God has turned away from him, even though he feels innocent. He reflects on his situation ([77:3](https://ref.ly/Ps77:3), [6](https://ref.ly/Ps77:6), [12](https://ref.ly/Ps77:12)) and finds hope (see [25:5](https://ref.ly/Ps25:5)) in remembering God’s past deeds ([77:11](https://ref.ly/Ps77:11)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 77:1–PSA 77:20

## Psalms 77:3 (id: 24896)

I think of God: God’s people inevitably face difficult times, but recalling his mighty acts at the beginning of their relationship assures them of God’s commitment. • Feeling overwhelmed*,* the psalmist is unable to deal with the crisis ([142:3](https://ref.ly/Ps142:3); [143:4](https://ref.ly/Ps143:4)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 77:3

## Psalms 77:4–6 (id: 24897)

As the psalmist meditates at night, he feels so disturbed that he cannot sleep or speak. He has pleasant memories of the past, but he cannot look beyond the present moment into the future.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 77:4–PSA 77:6

## Psalms 77:7 (id: 24899)

Feeling rejected (see [43:2](https://ref.ly/Ps43:2)), the psalmist asks if the situation is permanent.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 77:7

## Psalms 77:7–9 (id: 24898)

The psalmist questions his status before God.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 77:7–PSA 77:9

## Psalms 77:10 (id: 24893)

The psalmist fears that God’s hand of protection ([44:3](https://ref.ly/Ps44:3); [77:15](https://ref.ly/Ps77:15); [Exod 6:6](https://ref.ly/Exod6:6)) and favor ([Pss 16:7–8](https://ref.ly/Ps16:7-Ps16:8); [110:1](https://ref.ly/Ps110:1)) is now against him for no apparent reason.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 77:10

## Psalms 77:10–12 (id: 24892)

The memories of God’s mighty works in the past fill the psalmist’s mind.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 77:10–PSA 77:12

## Psalms 77:13–15 (id: 24894)

This central section of the poem reflects on God as the holy and powerful redeemer.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 77:13–PSA 77:15

## Psalms 77:16 (id: 24895)

the Red Sea: The Canaanites attributed divine power to the sea, but God is the one who made the sea and uses it for his own purposes.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 77:16

## Psalms 78:1–8 (id: 24901)

The prologue is an invitation to learn wisdom.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 78:1–PSA 78:8

## Psalms 78:1–72 (id: 24900)

This wisdom psalm exhorts the people to learn wisdom and faithfully pass it on.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 78:1–PSA 78:72

## Psalms 78:2 (id: 24909)

The psalmist recites Israel’s story ([78:5–72](https://ref.ly/Ps78:5-Ps78:72)) in a parable in order to teach wisdom and insight. • Jesus quoted this verse to explain why he taught in parables ([Matt 13:35](https://ref.ly/Matt13:35)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 78:2

## Psalms 78:3–4 (id: 24910)

This story of what God has done should be told from generation to generation (see [Deut 6:20–25](https://ref.ly/Deut6:20-Deut6:25); [Prov 4:1–4](https://ref.ly/Prov4:1-Prov4:4)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 78:3–PSA 78:4

## Psalms 78:5–6 (id: 24917)

The telling of the story should motivate God’s people to obey what he commanded ([Deut 6:4–9](https://ref.ly/Deut6:4-Deut6:9)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 78:5–PSA 78:6

## Psalms 78:7–8 (id: 24922)

God holds each generation responsible for its own response, which should be to maintain faith and hope (see [9:18](https://ref.ly/Ps9:18); [27:14](https://ref.ly/Ps27:14)) and avoid being stubborn, rebellious, and unfaithful (see [Deut 9:6–7](https://ref.ly/Deut9:6-Deut9:7); [10:16](https://ref.ly/Deut10:16); [30:6](https://ref.ly/Deut30:6); [31:27](https://ref.ly/Deut31:27)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 78:7–PSA 78:8

## Psalms 78:9–11 (id: 24924)

Ephraim*,* the second son of Joseph, received a special blessing from Jacob ([Gen 48:15–20](https://ref.ly/Gen48:15-Gen48:20); [49:22–26](https://ref.ly/Gen49:22-Gen49:26); [Deut 33:13–17](https://ref.ly/Deut33:13-Deut33:17)). The land that his descendants received included fertile valleys and strategic roads ([Judg 8:2](https://ref.ly/Judg8:2)). However, the people of Ephraim did not live in obedience to God’s gracious covenant.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 78:9–PSA 78:11

## Psalms 78:12 (id: 24903)

The miracles are the ten plagues against Egypt that God performed during Israel’s captivity ([Exod 7–12](https://ref.ly/Exod7:1-Exod12:51)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 78:12

## Psalms 78:12–16 (id: 24902)

The focus shifts from Ephraim ([78:9–11](https://ref.ly/Ps78:9-Ps78:11)) to Israel as a whole as the psalmist reflects on God’s power in Egypt (see [81:4–7](https://ref.ly/Ps81:4-Ps81:7)) and in the wilderness.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 78:12–PSA 78:16

## Psalms 78:13 (id: 24904)

God divided the sea when Israel crossed through the Red Sea (see [Exod 14–15](https://ref.ly/Exod14:1-Exod15:27)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 78:13

## Psalms 78:14 (id: 24905)

God used a cloud and a pillar of fire to guide and protect Israel in the wilderness ([Exod 13:21–22](https://ref.ly/Exod13:21-Exod13:22)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 78:14

## Psalms 78:17–31 (id: 24906)

Israel rebelled in the wilderness despite God’s abundant provision.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 78:17–PSA 78:31

## Psalms 78:23–25 (id: 24907)

Abundance comes through the doors of heaven ([Gen 8:2](https://ref.ly/Gen8:2); [2 Kgs 7:2](https://ref.ly/2Kgs7:2); [Mal 3:10](https://ref.ly/Mal3:10)). • Israel ate manna for forty years in the wilderness ([Exod 16:31–36](https://ref.ly/Exod16:31-Exod16:36); [John 6:31](https://ref.ly/John6:31)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 78:23–PSA 78:25

## Psalms 78:26–31 (id: 24908)

God powerfully satisfied the people’s desires, but they did not respond with gratitude or faith. Therefore, God exercised his justice.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 78:26–PSA 78:31

## Psalms 78:32–39 (id: 24911)

Israel’s rebellion resulted in God’s judgment, but even their short\-lived and insincere repentance motivated God to exercise forbearance.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 78:32–PSA 78:39

## Psalms 78:33 (id: 24912)

An entire generation died in the wilderness ([Num 14:22–23](https://ref.ly/Num14:22-Num14:23), [28–35](https://ref.ly/Num14:28-Num14:35)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 78:33

## Psalms 78:34 (id: 24914)

They repented: This demonstration of zeal was not sincere.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 78:34

## Psalms 78:34–39 (id: 24913)

Israel’s continued existence, in spite of the people’s rebellion and unbelief ([78:7–8](https://ref.ly/Ps78:7-Ps78:8)), was due to God’s compassion.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 78:34–PSA 78:39

## Psalms 78:35–39 (id: 24915)

The Israelites remembered the right doctrine ([9:9](https://ref.ly/Ps9:9); [91:1](https://ref.ly/Ps91:1)), but they did not allow God to change their hearts ([Lev 26:41](https://ref.ly/Lev26:41)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 78:35–PSA 78:39

## Psalms 78:40–55 (id: 24916)

The Israelites rebelled even though the Lord had rescued them from powerful plagues.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 78:40–PSA 78:55

## Psalms 78:56–64 (id: 24918)

Israel’s rebellion desecrated the Promised Land. The people built shrines to false gods and worshiped idols ([78:58](https://ref.ly/Ps78:58)) during the period of the judges (e.g., [Judg 2:11](https://ref.ly/Judg2:11); [3:7](https://ref.ly/Judg3:7), [17–18](https://ref.ly/Judg3:17-Judg3:18)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 78:56–PSA 78:64

## Psalms 78:60 (id: 24919)

God abandoned his dwelling at Shiloh because of the people’s idol worship ([1 Sam 4:11](https://ref.ly/1Sam4:11); [Jer 7:12](https://ref.ly/Jer7:12)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 78:60

## Psalms 78:67 (id: 24920)

The tribe of Ephraim was not completely rejected*,* but God favored Judah ([78:68](https://ref.ly/Ps78:68)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 78:67

## Psalms 78:68–69 (id: 24921)

In the choice of Mount Zion instead of Shiloh as God’s sanctuary on earth, God moved from the north to the south (see [Ps 69](https://ref.ly/Ps69:1-Ps69:36)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 78:68–PSA 78:69

## Psalms 78:70–72 (id: 24923)

The God who had turned against his own people ([78:62](https://ref.ly/Ps78:62)) chose David*,* a shepherd ([Gen 46:34](https://ref.ly/Gen46:34); [1 Sam 16:10–11](https://ref.ly/1Sam16:10-1Sam16:11)), to become their shepherd ([Ps 78:52](https://ref.ly/Ps78:52); cp. [23:1](https://ref.ly/Ps23:1)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 78:70–PSA 78:72

## Psalms 79:1 (id: 24928)

your special possession: This phrase might refer to the land, the Temple (see [61:5](https://ref.ly/Ps61:5)), or the people (see [79:2](https://ref.ly/Ps79:2); [78:71](https://ref.ly/Ps78:71)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 79:1

## Psalms 79:1–4 (id: 24926)

The poet laments the desecration of the Temple and the success of the enemy.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 79:1–PSA 79:4

## Psalms 79:1–13 (id: 24925)

This lament describes the occasion of Jerusalem’s fall in 586 BC. The early history of Israel’s rebellions described in [Ps 78](https://ref.ly/Ps78:1-Ps78:72) provoked God’s wrath, resulting in the desolation of Zion described here as the defilement of the Temple and the disgraced bodies that littered the landscape. The psalmist then prays for forgiveness and rescue ([79:8–9](https://ref.ly/Ps79:8-Ps79:9)), as well as for God to pay back the nation’s enemies ([79:12–13](https://ref.ly/Ps79:12-Ps79:13)). Other psalms lamenting the Exile include [Pss 42–44](https://ref.ly/Ps42:1-Ps44:26), [102](https://ref.ly/Ps102:1-Ps102:28), [107](https://ref.ly/Ps107:1-Ps107:43), [126](https://ref.ly/Ps126:1-Ps126:6), [137](https://ref.ly/Ps137:1-Ps137:9).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 79:1–PSA 79:13

## Psalms 79:5–8 (id: 24929)

The intensity of God’s judgment surprises the people; they cry out in despair for compassion, forgiveness, and relief. Verses [6–7](https://ref.ly/Ps6:1-Ps7:17) are repeated almost verbatim in [Jer 10:25](https://ref.ly/Jer10:25).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 79:5–PSA 79:8

## Psalms 79:6 (id: 24930)

The repentant among God’s people ask him to vent his anger not on them but on their wicked and unrepentant enemies.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 79:6

## Psalms 79:8 (id: 24931)

The people’s accumulation of past sins contributed to the Exile ([2 Kgs 17:7–23](https://ref.ly/2Kgs17:7-2Kgs17:23); [24:3–4](https://ref.ly/2Kgs24:3-2Kgs24:4)); however, the people perished because of their own sins ([Jer 31:30](https://ref.ly/Jer31:30); [Ezek 18:20](https://ref.ly/Ezek18:20)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 79:8

## Psalms 79:9–11 (id: 24932)

The people ask God to rescue them. Although Israel’s sins caused the tragedy, the pagan nations must also be held responsible for the bloodshed.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 79:9–PSA 79:11

## Psalms 79:12 (id: 24927)

The Exile resulted in national suffering and in individual searching for the Lord. • pay back: See [1:6](https://ref.ly/Ps1:6); [94:2](https://ref.ly/Ps94:2); [Jer 32:18](https://ref.ly/Jer32:18). • The expression seven times signifies something complete. • Israel’s neighbors included Edom, Moab, and Ammon (see [Ps 137:7](https://ref.ly/Ps137:7); [2 Kgs 24:2](https://ref.ly/2Kgs24:2); [Obad 1](https://ref.ly/Obad1:1-Obad1:21)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 79:12

## Psalms 80:1 (id: 24951)

is unknown today.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 80:1

## Psalms 80:1–2 (id: 24943)

God is the Shepherd of Israel: See also [23:1](https://ref.ly/Ps23:1); [28:9](https://ref.ly/Ps28:9); [78:52–53](https://ref.ly/Ps78:52-Ps78:53). • radiant glory . . . power: These expressions ([145:11](https://ref.ly/Ps145:11)) refer to God’s manifest presence.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 80:1–PSA 80:2

## Psalms 80:1–3 (id: 24944)

The psalmist urgently calls upon the Lord to act.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 80:1–PSA 80:3

## Psalms 80:1–19 (id: 24942)

This psalm of lament might originate with the remnant of the northern kingdom after its fall in 722 BC. The people call on God as their Shepherd and as the God of Heaven’s Armies in the hope that he will return to them and restore them. They remember the Exodus and their special relationship with the Lord and conclude with an expression of renewed commitment to him ([80:18](https://ref.ly/Ps80:18)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 80:1–PSA 80:19

## Psalms 80:3 (id: 24952)

This verse is repeated (with an increasing crescendo) in [80:7](https://ref.ly/Ps80:7), [19](https://ref.ly/Ps80:19).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 80:3

## Psalms 80:4–7 (id: 24953)

The people cry out for rescue from the shame of their recent defeat. The enemy’s victory is less devastating, however, than the knowledge that they themselves are objects of God’s wrath.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 80:4–PSA 80:7

## Psalms 80:8–9 (id: 24955)

Israel had been a prosperous grapevine ([Gen 1:28](https://ref.ly/Gen1:28); [Gal 5:22–23](https://ref.ly/Gal5:22-Gal5:23)) that God transplanted into the land of Canaan at the time of the conquest. However, the people forgot the source of their prosperity and chose to do evil ([Isa 5:1–7](https://ref.ly/Isa5:1-Isa5:7); [Hos 10:1](https://ref.ly/Hos10:1)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 80:8–PSA 80:9

## Psalms 80:8–11 (id: 24954)

Israel has a glorious past, beginning with its redemption from Egypt.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 80:8–PSA 80:11

## Psalms 80:10–11 (id: 24945)

Solomon’s kingdom had extended west to the Mediterranean Sea and east to the Euphrates River (see[72:8–9](https://ref.ly/Ps72:8-Ps72:9); [89:25](https://ref.ly/Ps89:25); [1 Kgs 4:21](https://ref.ly/1Kgs4:21)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 80:10–PSA 80:11

## Psalms 80:12 (id: 24946)

broken down our walls: God no longer defended Israel ([Isa 5:5](https://ref.ly/Isa5:5)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 80:12

## Psalms 80:13 (id: 24947)

The surrounding nations were ceremonially unclean, like a wild boar or vicious wild animals.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 80:13

## Psalms 80:15 (id: 24948)

Israel was the son that God had brought out of Egypt (see [Hos 11:1](https://ref.ly/Hos11:1)) and planted in the Holy Land.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 80:15

## Psalms 80:16–19 (id: 24949)

The community prays for God to change their desperate situation and restore them. They are still the Lord’s chosen people.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 80:16–PSA 80:19

## Psalms 80:17 (id: 24950)

The son of your choice was probably the northern kingdom of Israel, although it might allude to the king of David’s dynasty ([110:1](https://ref.ly/Ps110:1)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 80:17

## Psalms 81:1–3 (id: 24957)

As a prelude to the message of warning, the psalmist invites Israel to contemplate their God in song and dance.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 81:1–PSA 81:3

## Psalms 81:1–16 (id: 24956)

This warning message invites Israel to worship only the Lord and to enjoy the fullness of his blessing.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 81:1–PSA 81:16

## Psalms 81:2 (id: 24961)

An Israelite tambourine was a hand drum—a round frame covered with a skin, used as a percussion instrument during festivities, often to accompany dancing ([68:25](https://ref.ly/Ps68:25); [149:3](https://ref.ly/Ps149:3); [150:4](https://ref.ly/Ps150:4)). • The sweet lyre and the harp*,* both stringed instruments, are the instruments most frequently mentioned in the psalms (e.g., [33:2](https://ref.ly/Ps33:2); [57:8](https://ref.ly/Ps57:8); [71:22](https://ref.ly/Ps71:22); [150:3](https://ref.ly/Ps150:3)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 81:2

## Psalms 81:3 (id: 24962)

The ram’s horn mustered armies and announced special holy days ([47:5](https://ref.ly/Ps47:5); [98:6](https://ref.ly/Ps98:6)). • new moon: The first day of the lunar month marked a festival.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 81:3

## Psalms 81:4–5 (id: 24963)

The festival, a time to celebrate and listen to the Lord, took place at God’s appointed time.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 81:4–PSA 81:5

## Psalms 81:5 (id: 24964)

for Israel: Literally *for Joseph.* The tribes of Ephraim and Manasseh (the sons of Joseph) are used here to refer to the entire nation of Israel.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 81:5

## Psalms 81:6–7 (id: 24965)

The Lord heard Israel’s cry in Egypt and rescued them from oppressive slavery.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 81:6–PSA 81:7

## Psalms 81:8–10 (id: 24966)

God pleads with his people to remember the covenant and the Ten Commandments.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 81:8–PSA 81:10

## Psalms 81:10 (id: 24958)

God emphasizes that he and no one else rescued Israel. • The nation should open its mouth wide to take in God’s word (cp. [Deut 8:3](https://ref.ly/Deut8:3); [Ezek 3:1](https://ref.ly/Ezek3:1)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 81:10

## Psalms 81:11–16 (id: 24959)

The Lord helps Israel to understand that their failure was not because of his weakness.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 81:11–PSA 81:16

## Psalms 81:13–14 (id: 24960)

God wants to give his children his goodness, but only if they listen ([Isa 1:18–19](https://ref.ly/Isa1:18-Isa1:19); [28:12](https://ref.ly/Isa28:12); [48:18–19](https://ref.ly/Isa48:18-Isa48:19); see [Deut 6:3](https://ref.ly/Deut6:3)). • God promises to subdue the enemies ([Deut 9:3](https://ref.ly/Deut9:3)) of those who walk the paths of obedience and loyalty. He will also richly feed his people ([Isa 1:19](https://ref.ly/Isa1:19)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 81:13–PSA 81:14

## Psalms 82:1 (id: 24968)

God presides and stands ready to render judgment (see [Isa 3:13](https://ref.ly/Isa3:13)). • heaven’s court: See [Job 1:6](https://ref.ly/Job1:6).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 82:1

## Psalms 82:1–8 (id: 24967)

God condemns those who mistreat the helpless.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 82:1–PSA 82:8

## Psalms 82:2 (id: 24969)

Since justice marks God’s reign ([89:4](https://ref.ly/Ps89:4)), he opposes favoring the wicked. So the psalmist is perplexed and cries out to God for justice ([82:3–4](https://ref.ly/Ps82:3-Ps82:4), [8](https://ref.ly/Ps82:8)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 82:2

## Psalms 82:5 (id: 24970)

The unjust oppressors cannot bring or restore order. They wander about in darkness*,* unmoved by circumstances even when the whole world order falls apart around them (cp. [11:3](https://ref.ly/Ps11:3)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 82:5

## Psalms 82:6–7 (id: 24971)

The gods (see study notes on 29:1–2; 58:1), like mere mortals*,* cannot escape the judgment common to human rulers. Jesus quoted from this passage in [John 10:34](https://ref.ly/John10:34).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 82:6–PSA 82:7
* **Associated Articles:** Psalms 29:1-2 (ID: `24347@TyndaleStudyNotes`); Psalms 58:1 (ID: `24670@TyndaleStudyNotes`)

## Psalms 82:8 (id: 24972)

The nations belong to God; he will take over the realms formerly ruled by local deities and give them to his people, just as he did with the Promised Land.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 82:8

## Psalms 83:1–4 (id: 24974)

The enemy has successfully intimidated God’s people, so the poet prays that the Lord will hear and act.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 83:1–PSA 83:4

## Psalms 83:1–18 (id: 24973)

This community lament asks God for rescue and victory. The terse poetry suggests difficult times. A powerful coalition desires to destroy Israel ([83:1–4](https://ref.ly/Ps83:1-Ps83:4)) and allies itself against God ([83:5–8](https://ref.ly/Ps83:5-Ps83:8)). Recalling the fate of others who came against Israel ([83:9–12](https://ref.ly/Ps83:9-Ps83:12)), the psalmist prays that the same will happen to these enemies ([83:13–16](https://ref.ly/Ps83:13-Ps83:16)) so that God will receive honor among them ([83:17–18](https://ref.ly/Ps83:17-Ps83:18)). It is unclear whether this psalm arose out of a specific historical instance of opposition by these nations, or if it is a poetic collage of nations representing Israel’s enemies.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 83:1–PSA 83:18

## Psalms 83:5–8 (id: 24978)

signed a treaty: The allies agreed to fight against God and his people. The nations that are named in the alliance were situated around Israel and Judah.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 83:5–PSA 83:8

## Psalms 83:6–7 (id: 24979)

The Edomites*,* descendants of Esau, were located to the southeast of Judah (see [Gen 25:30](https://ref.ly/Gen25:30); [32:3](https://ref.ly/Gen32:3); [36:1–8](https://ref.ly/Gen36:1-Gen36:8)). • Ishmaelites were desert\-dwelling descendants of Hagar. • Moabites and Ammonites descended from Lot; both were located to the east of Israel and Judah. • The Hagrites were possibly located north of the Ammonites ([1 Chr 5:10](https://ref.ly/1Chr5:10)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 83:6–PSA 83:7

## Psalms 83:7 (id: 24980)

The Gebalites probably came from Gebal/Byblos on the coast of Lebanon. • The Amalekites were located south of Israel in the Negev. • Philistia was southwest of Judah, by the Mediterranean Sea. • Tyre was a port city on the Mediterranean, northwest of Israel.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 83:7

## Psalms 83:8 (id: 24981)

Assyria was northeast of Israel and north of the Persian Gulf. • The descendants of Lot were the Moabites and the Ammonites ([83:6–7](https://ref.ly/Ps83:6-Ps83:7)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 83:8

## Psalms 83:9–11 (id: 24982)

The Midianites*,* ruled by Zebah and Zalmunna and led by Oreb and Zeeb*,* were Israel’s enemy in the days of Gideon ([Judg 7:1–8:5](https://ref.ly/Judg7:1-Judg8:5)). Barak’s coalition defeated Sisera and Jabin ([Judg 4](https://ref.ly/Judg4:1-Judg4:24)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 83:9–PSA 83:11

## Psalms 83:9–18 (id: 24983)

The psalmist prays that God will miraculously destroy the new coalition as he did three other enemies; doing so would bring him glory.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 83:9–PSA 83:18

## Psalms 83:12 (id: 24975)

The coalition’s motivation for wiping out Israel was to acquire the land (see [Jer 3:19](https://ref.ly/Jer3:19)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 83:12

## Psalms 83:13 (id: 24976)

tumbleweed . . . chaff: This dry plant material easily blows away (see [Isa 17:13](https://ref.ly/Isa17:13)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 83:13

## Psalms 83:14–15 (id: 24977)

fire . . . fierce storm . . . tempest: These are images of God’s manifestation in judgment (see [Isa 29:6](https://ref.ly/Isa29:6)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 83:14–PSA 83:15

## Psalms 84:1–4 (id: 24985)

The psalmist is far from the Temple. He turns toward it in hopeful reflection.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 84:1–PSA 84:4

## Psalms 84:1–12 (id: 24984)

The psalmist expresses his deep spiritual longing for God’s presence. He faints with longing as he reflects on the Temple and on pilgrims making the journey to Jerusalem ([84:1–7](https://ref.ly/Ps84:1-Ps84:7)). He prays for himself and for the community ([84:8–9](https://ref.ly/Ps84:8-Ps84:9)). The conclusion of the psalm ([84:10–12](https://ref.ly/Ps84:10-Ps84:12)) clarifies that the Temple represents God—the psalmist truly longs for God’s presence. He knows that God’s goodness is greater than life and that only God can give his people favor and honor ([84:10–11](https://ref.ly/Ps84:10-Ps84:11)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 84:1–PSA 84:12

## Psalms 84:3 (id: 24988)

The poet envies the birds that have nesting places in and around the Temple.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 84:3

## Psalms 84:4 (id: 24989)

The priests and Temple personnel lived in the Temple.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 84:4

## Psalms 84:5 (id: 24991)

Travelers needed strength to meet the challenges of pilgrimage by foot along unpaved paths, in all kinds of weather and with the possibility of assaults.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 84:5

## Psalms 84:5–7 (id: 24990)

The pilgrimage to Jerusalem reenacted the Exodus, when God marvelously provided for his people (see [78:15–16](https://ref.ly/Ps78:15-Ps78:16); [105:41](https://ref.ly/Ps105:41)). The psalmist imagines the pains of travel turning to the joy of arrival.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 84:5–PSA 84:7

## Psalms 84:6 (id: 24992)

The Valley of Weeping probably refers to the anguish that lonely pilgrims endured (see [23:4](https://ref.ly/Ps23:4)), rather than to an actual location. • refreshing springs . . . autumn rains: Even when pilgrims feel totally exhausted, the prospect of drawing near to the Lord renews their spirits (cp. [Isa 35:6–10](https://ref.ly/Isa35:6-Isa35:10); [41:18–20](https://ref.ly/Isa41:18-Isa41:20); [43:17–20](https://ref.ly/Isa43:17-Isa43:20); [49:10](https://ref.ly/Isa49:10)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 84:6

## Psalms 84:9 (id: 24993)

Both kings and priests were anointed to dedicate them for service (see [132:17](https://ref.ly/Ps132:17); [Exod 28:41](https://ref.ly/Exod28:41); [1 Sam 9:16](https://ref.ly/1Sam9:16); [16:1–13](https://ref.ly/1Sam16:1-1Sam16:13); cp. [Isa 61:1](https://ref.ly/Isa61:1); [Acts 10:38](https://ref.ly/Acts10:38)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 84:9

## Psalms 84:10 (id: 24986)

The psalmist viewed being in God’s presence as much better than being anywhere else.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 84:10

## Psalms 84:11 (id: 24987)

Some people worshiped the sun as a god, but the true God provides all that anyone needs.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 84:11

## Psalms 85:1 (id: 24998)

God restored the fortunes of Israel by bringing the nation back from exile (see [14:7](https://ref.ly/Ps14:7); [126:1](https://ref.ly/Ps126:1)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 85:1

## Psalms 85:1–5 (id: 24995)

Though the psalmist gratefully acknowledges God’s goodness, he also asks God whether his wrath will last forever.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 85:1–PSA 85:5

## Psalms 85:1–13 (id: 24994)

The psalmist leads the postexilic community in lament and prayer for full redemption. He ponders God’s past rescue of Israel from exile ([85:1–3](https://ref.ly/Ps85:1-Ps85:3)), longs for greater evidence of God’s goodness, and leads the community in prayer for full restoration ([85:4–7](https://ref.ly/Ps85:4-Ps85:7)). God responds with a message of peace ([85:8–9](https://ref.ly/Ps85:8-Ps85:9)), and the psalm concludes with a lyrical outburst at the grandeur of God’s salvation ([85:10–13](https://ref.ly/Ps85:10-Ps85:13)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 85:1–PSA 85:13

## Psalms 85:2 (id: 24999)

When God forgave the guilt of their sins*,* he gave the people the possibility of fellowship with him (see [32:5](https://ref.ly/Ps32:5)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 85:2

## Psalms 85:6–7 (id: 25000)

This prayer for renewal is based on God’s unfailing love for his people.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 85:6–PSA 85:7

## Psalms 85:8–9 (id: 25001)

When God the Lord speaks, his faithful people listen. He promises them peace*,* meaning wholeness and well\-being (see [37:11](https://ref.ly/Ps37:11)). They fear the Lord and know that he and his salvation are near to them. • The Lord does not tolerate foolish ways*,* such as those that resulted in the Exile.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 85:8–PSA 85:9

## Psalms 85:10–13 (id: 24996)

In the glorious world of renewal and salvation, all the qualities of God’s care—love*,* truth*,* righteousness*,* and peace—come together and transform the created order into something new (see [Isa 32:15–20](https://ref.ly/Isa32:15-Isa32:20)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 85:10–PSA 85:13

## Psalms 85:13 (id: 24997)

Righteousness is like a messenger preparing the world for God’s coming in response to the prayers of his people ([85:4–7](https://ref.ly/Ps85:4-Ps85:7); [89:14](https://ref.ly/Ps89:14)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 85:13

## Psalms 86:1 (id: 25008)

This is the only Psalm connected to David in the third book.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 86:1

## Psalms 86:1–4 (id: 25003)

God’s devoted servant prays for mercy. The psalmist sees himself as a member of the covenant community and as a citizen of the world.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 86:1–PSA 86:4

## Psalms 86:1–17 (id: 25002)

The psalmist invokes God’s help and praises his character in a lament prompted by the presence of evil ([86:14](https://ref.ly/Ps86:14), [17](https://ref.ly/Ps86:17)). All people will worship the gracious and almighty God ([86:8–10](https://ref.ly/Ps86:8-Ps86:10)). To this end, the poet commits himself to a lifestyle of ethical integrity ([86:11](https://ref.ly/Ps86:11)) and praising the Lord ([86:12–13](https://ref.ly/Ps86:12-Ps86:13)). The last stanza contrasts the qualities of evil people with those of the Lord ([86:14–17](https://ref.ly/Ps86:14-Ps86:17)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 86:1–PSA 86:17

## Psalms 86:5 (id: 25010)

The psalmist recounts the catalog of divine perfections ([Exod 34:6–7](https://ref.ly/Exod34:6-Exod34:7)), especially God’s willingness to forgive sin (see[Pss 32:5](https://ref.ly/Ps32:5); [85:2](https://ref.ly/Ps85:2); [145:7–10](https://ref.ly/Ps145:7-Ps145:10)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 86:5

## Psalms 86:5–7 (id: 25009)

The psalmist appeals to God to remain true to his character, which is the basis for hope.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 86:5–PSA 86:7

## Psalms 86:8–10 (id: 25011)

All the nations must submit themselves to the Lord and worship him ([45:17](https://ref.ly/Ps45:17); [117:1](https://ref.ly/Ps117:1); [148:7–11](https://ref.ly/Ps148:7-Ps148:11)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 86:8–PSA 86:10

## Psalms 86:11 (id: 25004)

The poet responds to the Lord by seeking faithful instruction in the truth. • An individual with purity of heart has integrity and wholeness (see[73:1](https://ref.ly/Ps73:1)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 86:11

## Psalms 86:12–13 (id: 25005)

In anticipation of God’s rescue, the psalmist praises him and trusts in his goodness.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 86:12–PSA 86:13

## Psalms 86:14–17 (id: 25006)

The arrogant exist both inside and outside the community. The psalmist asks for a vision of God’s character; God is so great that just a glimpse of his goodness will shut the mouths of the wicked.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 86:14–PSA 86:17

## Psalms 86:15 (id: 25007)

God has mercy on his people ([51:1](https://ref.ly/Ps51:1)); he is gracious ([25:6](https://ref.ly/Ps25:6)), slow to get angry ([103:8](https://ref.ly/Ps103:8); [145:8](https://ref.ly/Ps145:8)), and filled with unfailing love and faithfulness (Hebrew khesed and ’emeth; [143:1](https://ref.ly/Ps143:1)). This verse repeats a theme first expressed in [Exod 34:7](https://ref.ly/Exod34:7); [Num 14:18](https://ref.ly/Num14:18) (cp.[Pss 103:8](https://ref.ly/Ps103:8); [145:8](https://ref.ly/Ps145:8); [Neh 9:17](https://ref.ly/Neh9:17); [Joel 2:13](https://ref.ly/Joel2:13); [Jon 4:2](https://ref.ly/Jonah4:2)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 86:15

## Psalms 87:1 (id: 25013)

Jerusalem was Israel’s capital and the location of the Temple, God’s earthly palace (see [Ps 84](https://ref.ly/Ps84:1-Ps84:12)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 87:1

## Psalms 87:1–7 (id: 25012)

This psalm envisions Jerusalem as the city of God where all the nations are citizens.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 87:1–PSA 87:7

## Psalms 87:4 (id: 25014)

As great as Zion is, it will be even greater when it becomes an international city where believers from all the nations have citizenship. • God keeps a record of all who confess him as their Lord ([Dan 7:10](https://ref.ly/Dan7:10); [Rev 13:8](https://ref.ly/Rev13:8)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 87:4

## Psalms 87:5–6 (id: 25015)

Jerusalem becomes the international city where all God’s children are citizens.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 87:5–PSA 87:6

## Psalms 88:1 (id: 25020)

might be a sage from Solomon’s time ([1 Kgs 4:31](https://ref.ly/1Kgs4:31)), a descendant of Judah ([1 Chr 2:6](https://ref.ly/1Chr2:6)), or a member of the Levitical family charged with singing at the Temple ([1 Chr 15:17](https://ref.ly/1Chr15:17); [2 Chr 5:12](https://ref.ly/2Chr5:12)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 88:1

## Psalms 88:1–5 (id: 25017)

The psalmist calls on the Lord for salvation.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 88:1–PSA 88:5

## Psalms 88:1–18 (id: 25016)

In this lament, the psalmist sees himself as cast out from God’s presence. At first, he calls on the Lord. When he finds no relief from his suffering, he presents three charges against God ([88:6–7](https://ref.ly/Ps88:6-Ps88:7), [8–12](https://ref.ly/Ps88:8-Ps88:12), [13–17](https://ref.ly/Ps88:13-Ps88:17)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 88:1–PSA 88:18

## Psalms 88:6–7 (id: 25021)

In his first charge, the psalmist blames the Lord for his demise. God’s overpowering anger did not make sense. • The phrase the darkest depths implies the place of the dead ([143:3](https://ref.ly/Ps143:3); see [Lam 3:6](https://ref.ly/Lam3:6)) or the depths of the sea ([Pss 68:22](https://ref.ly/Ps68:22); [69:1–2](https://ref.ly/Ps69:1-Ps69:2)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 88:6–PSA 88:7

## Psalms 88:8–12 (id: 25022)

In his second charge, the psalmist claims that God has isolated him and caused his loneliness (cp. [31:11](https://ref.ly/Ps31:11); [38:11](https://ref.ly/Ps38:11)). Loneliness was a curse in a culture where relationships were more important than personal achievement.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 88:8–PSA 88:12

## Psalms 88:13–17 (id: 25018)

In his third charge, the psalmist accuses the Lord of rejecting him. The force and apparent cruelty of the psalmist’s suffering overwhelm him.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 88:13–PSA 88:17

## Psalms 88:18 (id: 25019)

The psalmist restates his second and first charges.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 88:18

## Psalms 89:1 (id: 25029)

God’s unfailing love gives reason to celebrate forever.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 89:1

## Psalms 89:1–52 (id: 25023)

Book Three ([Pss 73–89](https://ref.ly/Ps73:1-Ps89:52)) begins and ends with weighty questions. Though [Ps 89](https://ref.ly/Ps89:1-Ps89:52) begins with a praise\-filled account of how the Lord exalted the throne of David ([89:1–37](https://ref.ly/Ps89:1-Ps89:37)), the psalmist protests the Lord’s apparent rejection of his covenant with David ([89:38–51](https://ref.ly/Ps89:38-Ps89:51); see [2 Sam 7:8–16](https://ref.ly/2Sam7:8-2Sam7:16)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 89:1–PSA 89:52

## Psalms 89:title (id: 25049)

was a wise man ([1 Kgs 4:31](https://ref.ly/1Kgs4:31); cp. [Ps 88:title](https://ref.ly/Ps88:1)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 89:1

## Psalms 89:3 (id: 25038)

The Lord has sworn by his own holiness ([89:35](https://ref.ly/Ps89:35); see [110:4](https://ref.ly/Ps110:4)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 89:3

## Psalms 89:3–4 (id: 25034)

The psalmist restates God’s covenant with David (see also [89:19–37](https://ref.ly/Ps89:19-Ps89:37)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 89:3–PSA 89:4

## Psalms 89:5 (id: 25045)

Praise for God’s greatness (see [8:1](https://ref.ly/Ps8:1)) comes from the inhabitants of heaven who witness his faithfulness.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 89:5

## Psalms 89:5–8 (id: 25042)

God is the absolute standard of faithfulness, commitment, and order. The angelic beings and the heavens testify to his constancy.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 89:5–PSA 89:8

## Psalms 89:6 (id: 25046)

mightiest angel: Literally *son of God* (see study note on 29:1–2).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 89:6
* **Associated Articles:** Psalms 29:1-2 (ID: `24347@TyndaleStudyNotes`)

## Psalms 89:9–10 (id: 25047)

The Lord rules over all parts of the created order, including evil. • You scattered your enemies: The Lord will crush ([Luke 1:51](https://ref.ly/Luke1:51)) evil powers that oppose him ([Ps 2:1–3](https://ref.ly/Ps2:1-Ps2:3)). • with your mighty arm: This phrase represents God’s strength ([89:13](https://ref.ly/Ps89:13)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 89:9–PSA 89:10

## Psalms 89:9–13 (id: 25048)

In this hymn, the psalmist celebrates God’s comprehensive and powerful sovereignty over nature.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 89:9–PSA 89:13

## Psalms 89:12 (id: 25024)

Mount Tabor was in northern Israel. Mount Hermon formed the extreme northern border of the nation.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 89:12

## Psalms 89:14–18 (id: 25025)

God rules wisely over creation. The qualities of righteousness, justice, and faithfulness fit the profile of a wise ruler. The happy people who live under his rule enjoy his protection.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 89:14–PSA 89:18

## Psalms 89:15–16 (id: 25026)

Those who are wise worship God, walk in his light*,* rejoice in their relationship with him, and exult in his character.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 89:15–PSA 89:16

## Psalms 89:17–18 (id: 25027)

The Lord protects his people with the same power by which he established the created order.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 89:17–PSA 89:18

## Psalms 89:19–37 (id: 25028)

The Lord chose David as his son and as king of Israel (see [2:4–6](https://ref.ly/Ps2:4-Ps2:6); [2 Sam 7:8–16](https://ref.ly/2Sam7:8-2Sam7:16)) to provide protection for his people.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 89:19–PSA 89:37

## Psalms 89:20 (id: 25030)

I have anointed him: This is the verb from which *anointed one* (Hebrew mashiakh, “messiah”) is derived.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 89:20

## Psalms 89:26–29 (id: 25031)

The Lord adopted David as his son, appointed him as his commander over the nations, and promised to support him forever. Verse 26 recalls a verse from David’s song of praise ([2 Sam 22:47](https://ref.ly/2Sam22:47)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 89:26–PSA 89:29

## Psalms 89:27 (id: 25032)

David would be the most eminent of earthly kings. The Hebrew word translated mightiest is the same as the designation for God as “Most High” (‘elyon).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 89:27

## Psalms 89:29 (id: 25033)

The Lord writes his faithfulness in heaven*,* on the canvas of his universe (see [89:2](https://ref.ly/Ps89:2)). He records his commitment to the dynasty of David in the same way.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 89:29

## Psalms 89:30–37 (id: 25035)

The Lord disciplines but does not reject his erring children. He foresees violation of trust and subsequent punishment, but he commits himself to uphold the covenant. His fidelity to David corresponds to his faithfulness to the created order.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 89:30–PSA 89:37

## Psalms 89:35 (id: 25036)

holiness: The Lord is wholly distinct from the created order ([22:3](https://ref.ly/Ps22:3)); his character is totally pure. He does as he pleases ([115:3](https://ref.ly/Ps115:3)), and he chooses to be faithful ([89:1](https://ref.ly/Ps89:1); [115:1](https://ref.ly/Ps115:1)); therefore, he cannot lie.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 89:35

## Psalms 89:38 (id: 25037)

You are angry: The harshness of God’s wrath perplexes the psalmist.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 89:38

## Psalms 89:40 (id: 25039)

broken down the walls: The Lord’s people are completely vulnerable.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 89:40

## Psalms 89:42 (id: 25040)

Although the Lord promised to strengthen David, he secretly strengthened David’s enemies.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 89:42

## Psalms 89:46–47 (id: 25041)

The psalmist wonders if he will live to see the end of the Lord’s anger. Our lifetimes are short*,* like a day in the Lord’s sight ([90:4](https://ref.ly/Ps90:4), [10](https://ref.ly/Ps90:10)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 89:46–PSA 89:47

## Psalms 89:50 (id: 25043)

The phrase your servants refers to the community loyal to the Lord.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 89:50

## Psalms 89:52 (id: 25044)

This doxology concludes all of Book Three ([Pss 73–89](https://ref.ly/Ps73:1-Ps89:52)); it is not intended to be read as part of [Ps 89](https://ref.ly/Ps89:1-Ps89:52). It stands in stark contrast to the anguish and questioning of [Ps 89](https://ref.ly/Ps89:1-Ps89:52). Cp. [41:13](https://ref.ly/Ps41:13); [106:48](https://ref.ly/Ps106:48).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 89:52

## Psalms 90:1 (id: 25075)

led God’s people from slavery in Egypt to Mount Sinai, where he received the law and established God’s covenant with Israel. • the man of God: Moses enjoyed a special relationship with God ([Deut 33:1](https://ref.ly/Deut33:1)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 90:1

## Psalms 90:1–2 (id: 25068)

The Lord becomes the home of the godly; he has provided shelter for countless generations. The word translated *home* is not used frequently in the Psalter. It describes a place of safety where the Lord meets his needy people and cares for them ([68:5](https://ref.ly/Ps68:5); [71:3](https://ref.ly/Ps71:3)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 90:1–PSA 90:2

## Psalms 90:1–17 (id: 25067)

Although the Lord’s people have made their home in him for generations, their sin widens the gap between them and their infinite Lord. The Lord’s wrath against a person’s sin might last a lifetime and yet be only a taste of his displeasure with sin. This lamentable situation calls the community to seek the Lord’s light. Taking the first step means seeking restoration with the Lord on the basis of his compassion and love ([90:13–14](https://ref.ly/Ps90:13-Ps90:14)). He alone makes his servants glad and blesses their future generations ([90:16–17](https://ref.ly/Ps90:16-Ps90:17)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 90:1–PSA 90:17

## Psalms 90:2 (id: 25076)

The Lord is the eternal God. • The Lord gave birth to the earth by creating it.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 90:2

## Psalms 90:3–6 (id: 25077)

Unlike God, humans are mortal and transitory.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 90:3–PSA 90:6

## Psalms 90:7–10 (id: 25078)

Sinners cannot escape God’s wrath because the Lord sees their sins. Their fleeting lives are filled with afflictions.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 90:7–PSA 90:10

## Psalms 90:9–10 (id: 25079)

A groan of sorrow ([Ezek 2:10](https://ref.ly/Ezek2:10)) sums up a life spent in facing the consequences of sin. • Humans cause trouble (see [Ps 10:6](https://ref.ly/Ps10:6)) and receive pain in return.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 90:9–PSA 90:10

## Psalms 90:11–12 (id: 25069)

In the search for wisdom, no one can comprehend the Lord (see [Isa 40:13](https://ref.ly/Isa40:13)). The appropriate human response to the Lord is godly fear (see [Ps 60:4](https://ref.ly/Ps60:4)). The Lord alone can teach humans to follow the path of wisdom ([25:4–6](https://ref.ly/Ps25:4-Ps25:6)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 90:11–PSA 90:12

## Psalms 90:13 (id: 25071)

The phrase your servants refers to the community of those loyal to the Lord.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 90:13

## Psalms 90:13–17 (id: 25070)

The psalmist prays for the Lord’s favor and restoration.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 90:13–PSA 90:17

## Psalms 90:15 (id: 25072)

The psalmist calls upon the Lord to give the people gladness to replace their mourning (see [92:4–5](https://ref.ly/Ps92:4-Ps92:5)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 90:15

## Psalms 90:16 (id: 25073)

The children represent future generations in contrast to the generations past ([90:1](https://ref.ly/Ps90:1)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 90:16

## Psalms 90:17 (id: 25074)

Humans waste their efforts unless the Lord makes them successful ([44:3](https://ref.ly/Ps44:3)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 90:17

## Psalms 91:1 (id: 25087)

The Most High is an ancient title that expresses the Lord’s exalted status as the ruler and protector of the godly (see [Gen 14:19](https://ref.ly/Gen14:19)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 91:1

## Psalms 91:1–2 (id: 25081)

The Lord is an ancient shelter (see [90:1](https://ref.ly/Ps90:1)), open to those who seek refuge in him.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 91:1–PSA 91:2

## Psalms 91:1–16 (id: 25080)

This wisdom psalm expresses confidence in the Almighty God, who provides a shelter for those who take refuge in him. They receive redemption, life, and glory from the Lord, who loves and cares for those who seek him.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 91:1–PSA 91:16

## Psalms 91:3 (id: 25089)

God protects the godly from deadly disease and even a destructive word.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 91:3

## Psalms 91:3–4 (id: 25088)

The psalmist invites the godly to trust in the Lord and find protection in him.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 91:3–PSA 91:4

## Psalms 91:4 (id: 25090)

The armor might refer to a body shield, while protection refers to a small shield worn on the arm.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 91:4

## Psalms 91:5–8 (id: 25091)

The godly should not be afraid*,* because the Lord watches over them. These promises do not guarantee an escape from trouble, but they create an expectation of the Lord’s goodness.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 91:5–PSA 91:8

## Psalms 91:6 (id: 25092)

The reference to disease represents any kind of affliction.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 91:6

## Psalms 91:9–13 (id: 25093)

The poet again invites the godly to seek refuge in the Lord and enjoy the benefits of divine protection.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 91:9–PSA 91:13

## Psalms 91:11 (id: 25082)

he will order his angels: Satan cited these words when he tempted Jesus ([Matt 4:6](https://ref.ly/Matt4:6); [Luke 4:10–11](https://ref.ly/Luke4:10-Luke4:11)), but God makes this promise for those who obey him ([Ps 91:14](https://ref.ly/Ps91:14)), not for those who arrogantly test him ([Matt 4:4](https://ref.ly/Matt4:4), [7](https://ref.ly/Matt4:7)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 91:11

## Psalms 91:14 (id: 25084)

Those who love the Lord will obey him ([Deut 30:20](https://ref.ly/Deut30:20); [1 Jn 5:3](https://ref.ly/1John5:3)) and seek his protection ([Pss 91:1](https://ref.ly/Ps91:1); [145:18](https://ref.ly/Ps145:18)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 91:14

## Psalms 91:14–16 (id: 25083)

The godly can trust the Lord’s protection and provision.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 91:14–PSA 91:16

## Psalms 91:15 (id: 25085)

The Lord promises to answer the prayers of his people. • The Psalter often speaks of people honoring the Lord ([50:15](https://ref.ly/Ps50:15)); here, God promises to honor the godly who risk everything for his sake ([62:7](https://ref.ly/Ps62:7); [71:21](https://ref.ly/Ps71:21); [84:11](https://ref.ly/Ps84:11)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 91:15

## Psalms 91:16 (id: 25086)

A long life on earth represents just a small part of the Lord’s goodness and eternal friendship ([23:6](https://ref.ly/Ps23:6)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 91:16

## Psalms 92:1 (id: 25101)

Jewish tradition assigned one psalm to each day of the week: Sunday ([Ps 24](https://ref.ly/Ps24:1-Ps24:10)), Monday ([Ps 48](https://ref.ly/Ps48:1-Ps48:14)), Tuesday ([Ps 82](https://ref.ly/Ps82:1-Ps82:8)), Wednesday ([Ps 94](https://ref.ly/Ps94:1-Ps94:23)), Thursday ([Ps 81](https://ref.ly/Ps81:1-Ps81:16)), Friday ([Ps 93](https://ref.ly/Ps93:1-Ps93:5)), and the Sabbath ([Ps 92](https://ref.ly/Ps92:1-Ps92:15)). This is the only psalm that indicates this use in its title.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 92:1

## Psalms 92:1–3 (id: 25095)

The psalmist offers praise and thanksgiving for God’s unfailing love and faithfulness.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 92:1–PSA 92:3

## Psalms 92:1–15 (id: 25094)

Thanksgiving and praise open this psalm. The Lord—the Most High—is faithful and just in discerning between the godly and the wicked. The godly will enjoy a glorious, vigorous future, while the wicked will perish. The wise see and understand the Lord’s works as they reveal his justice ([92:6–7](https://ref.ly/Ps92:6-Ps92:7), [11](https://ref.ly/Ps92:11), [15](https://ref.ly/Ps92:15)). The wicked, like grass, are quickly destroyed ([92:7–10](https://ref.ly/Ps92:7-Ps92:10)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 92:1–PSA 92:15

## Psalms 92:4–5 (id: 25102)

The Lord acts and the psalmist responds in praise ([92:4](https://ref.ly/Ps92:4)). God’s actions spring from his thoughts ([92:5](https://ref.ly/Ps92:5)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 92:4–PSA 92:5

## Psalms 92:4–7 (id: 25103)

Fools perish because they do not understand the Lord’s marvelous works and eternal plans.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 92:4–PSA 92:7

## Psalms 92:5–6 (id: 25104)

The Lord’s thoughts do not make sense to the simpleton or the fool*,* the immoral person who desires no wisdom ([Prov 1:22](https://ref.ly/Prov1:22); [10:23](https://ref.ly/Prov10:23)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 92:5–PSA 92:6

## Psalms 92:7 (id: 25105)

Even when the ungodly seem to grow luxuriantly ([73:3–5](https://ref.ly/Ps73:3-Ps73:5)), they have no future ([92:9](https://ref.ly/Ps92:9); see [1:6](https://ref.ly/Ps1:6); [90:5–6](https://ref.ly/Ps90:5-Ps90:6); [Isa 40:6–8](https://ref.ly/Isa40:6-Isa40:8)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 92:7

## Psalms 92:8 (id: 25107)

The transcendent Lord stays above the world of human experience. From this exalted place, he rules and judges ([7:7](https://ref.ly/Ps7:7)), celebrates his victories ([68:18](https://ref.ly/Ps68:18); see [Ps 47](https://ref.ly/Ps47:1-Ps47:9)), comes to rescue the needy ([102:19](https://ref.ly/Ps102:19)), brings an end to the wicked ([92:7–8](https://ref.ly/Ps92:7-Ps92:8)), and receives praise ([148:1](https://ref.ly/Ps148:1)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 92:8

## Psalms 92:8–10 (id: 25106)

The glory of the Lord provides the reason for the poet’s renewed strength and glory, and for the imminent defeat of the enemy.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 92:8–PSA 92:10

## Psalms 92:10 (id: 25096)

as strong as a wild ox: The Lord allows the psalmist to share his exaltation ([92:8](https://ref.ly/Ps92:8)), thus ensuring victory.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 92:10

## Psalms 92:11–15 (id: 25097)

The psalmist understands the Lord’s mighty acts. He shares in the glory of the wise of heart.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 92:11–PSA 92:15

## Psalms 92:12 (id: 25098)

Carvings of palm trees ([1 Kgs 6:29](https://ref.ly/1Kgs6:29), [32](https://ref.ly/1Kgs6:32), [35](https://ref.ly/1Kgs6:35); [7:36](https://ref.ly/1Kgs7:36)) adorned the Temple, and builders made rich use of cedars ([1 Kgs 5:6](https://ref.ly/1Kgs5:6)). The trees represent the godly, who are planted in the very courts of the Temple.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 92:12

## Psalms 92:13 (id: 25099)

The Temple area consisted of the Lord’s own house and the courts that surrounded it.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 92:13

## Psalms 92:15 (id: 25100)

There is no evil in him! The Lord is consistently just; he rightly judges everyone (see [Zeph 3:5](https://ref.ly/Zeph3:5)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 92:15

## Psalms 93:1 (id: 25110)

robed in majesty: The Lord stands victorious both before and after battle (see [45:3](https://ref.ly/Ps45:3)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 93:1

## Psalms 93:1–5 (id: 25109)

The everlasting Lord gloriously establishes his kingship (cp. [Pss 47](https://ref.ly/Ps47:1-Ps47:9), [99–100](https://ref.ly/Ps99:1-Ps100:5)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 93:1–PSA 93:5

## Psalms 93:1–100.5 (id: 25108)

These psalms challenge the doubts created by the Exile (see [Ps 89](https://ref.ly/Ps89:1-Ps89:52)) and answer the questions asked in [90:11](https://ref.ly/Ps90:11), [13](https://ref.ly/Ps90:13). The Lord has established a kingdom ([Ps 93](https://ref.ly/Ps93:1-Ps93:5)) that is characterized by the punishment of the wicked ([Ps 94](https://ref.ly/Ps94:1-Ps94:23)), reverent obedience among his people ([Ps 95](https://ref.ly/Ps95:1-Ps95:11)), justice for the poor ([Ps 96](https://ref.ly/Ps96:1-Ps96:13)), celebration in Zion ([Ps 97](https://ref.ly/Ps97:1-Ps97:12)), salvation for Israel ([Ps 98](https://ref.ly/Ps98:1-Ps98:9)), holiness ([Ps 99](https://ref.ly/Ps99:1-Ps99:9)), and praise ([Ps 100](https://ref.ly/Ps100:1-Ps100:5)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 93:1–PSA 100:5

## Psalms 93:3–4 (id: 25111)

God’s victory over natural chaos gives the psalmist confidence that the Lord will also defeat his present enemies (cp. [Jer 46:8](https://ref.ly/Jer46:8); [47:2](https://ref.ly/Jer47:2)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 93:3–PSA 93:4

## Psalms 93:5 (id: 25112)

Through his stable rule and royal laws*,* the Lord orders the world. • Your reign (literally *your house*): The *house* from which God reigns might be the Lord’s heavenly palace or the earthly Temple.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 93:5

## Psalms 94:1–7 (id: 25114)

After the community falls victim to the wicked ([94:5–7](https://ref.ly/Ps94:5-Ps94:7)), they pray that the Lord will render justice (see [7:11](https://ref.ly/Ps7:11); [9:12](https://ref.ly/Ps9:12)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 94:1–PSA 94:7

## Psalms 94:1–23 (id: 25113)

This plea for the Lord’s justice includes both communal and individual expressions of lament ([94:1–7](https://ref.ly/Ps94:1-Ps94:7), [16–23](https://ref.ly/Ps94:16-Ps94:23)). The psalmist gives voice to the pain and suffering caused by the wicked, but he also depicts the comfort and stability of the Lord’s protection. He calls on the Lord to avenge the needy against the arrogant and foolish, he rebukes such people for their folly ([94:8–11](https://ref.ly/Ps94:8-Ps94:11)), and he pronounces a blessing on the wise ([94:12–15](https://ref.ly/Ps94:12-Ps94:15)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 94:1–PSA 94:23

## Psalms 94:2 (id: 25123)

Just as the Lord’s enemies rise up against him and his people ([3:7](https://ref.ly/Ps3:7); [93:3](https://ref.ly/Ps93:3)), he must arise and make retribution against the enemy (see [79:12](https://ref.ly/Ps79:12); [Isa 65:6](https://ref.ly/Isa65:6)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 94:2

## Psalms 94:6 (id: 25124)

widows . . . foreigners . . . orphans: The Lord’s law protects needy people ([Deut 24:17](https://ref.ly/Deut24:17); [27:19](https://ref.ly/Deut27:19)), but they remain vulnerable in society.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 94:6

## Psalms 94:7 (id: 25125)

The wicked think that they can get away with their vile acts and speech, foolishly assuming that God isn’t looking or doesn’t care.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 94:7

## Psalms 94:8–11 (id: 25126)

The psalmist rebukes human folly.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 94:8–PSA 94:11

## Psalms 94:9 (id: 25127)

It is preposterous that those with ears and eyes would imagine their Creator to be deaf and blind.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 94:9

## Psalms 94:10 (id: 25115)

punishes: This word also carries the idea of “warns” ([2:10](https://ref.ly/Ps2:10)), “disciplines” ([6:1](https://ref.ly/Ps6:1); [94:12](https://ref.ly/Ps94:12)), or “instructs” ([16:7](https://ref.ly/Ps16:7)). The Lord disciplines his people to purify their character ([Prov 3:11–12](https://ref.ly/Prov3:11-Prov3:12); [Heb 12:6–11](https://ref.ly/Heb12:6-Heb12:11)). He punishes his enemies by giving them what they deserve ([Ps 1:6](https://ref.ly/Ps1:6); [Rom 6:23](https://ref.ly/Rom6:23)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 94:10

## Psalms 94:11 (id: 25116)

While the Lord’s thoughts are deep, people’s thoughts are worthless (cp. [92:5](https://ref.ly/Ps92:5); [1 Cor 3:20](https://ref.ly/1Cor3:20)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 94:11

## Psalms 94:12–15 (id: 25117)

True to his nature, the Lord rewards those who live by his wise instruction and makes them happy according to his promises.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 94:12–PSA 94:15

## Psalms 94:13 (id: 25118)

God’s relief includes his comfort and rescue.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 94:13

## Psalms 94:14 (id: 25119)

Even when it seems that he has, the Lord will not reject his people.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 94:14

## Psalms 94:16 (id: 25121)

Only God has the power to stand up to the wicked (see [2:2](https://ref.ly/Ps2:2)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 94:16

## Psalms 94:16–23 (id: 25120)

The psalmist’s prayer resumes (see [94:1–7](https://ref.ly/Ps94:1-Ps94:7)) with a desperate cry for the Lord’s justice; it concludes with the hopeful expectation that evil will end.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 94:16–PSA 94:23

## Psalms 94:18–19 (id: 25122)

The psalmist’s experience of slipping contrasts with God’s promise to stand with him ([94:12–13](https://ref.ly/Ps94:12-Ps94:13); see [15:5](https://ref.ly/Ps15:5); [93:1](https://ref.ly/Ps93:1)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 94:18–PSA 94:19

## Psalms 95:1–11 (id: 25128)

This call to worship urges the people to respond to the Lord, the Shepherd, and to follow him faithfully. The previous generation, who refused to obey, did not receive the blessings of the Promised Land.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 95:1–PSA 95:11

## Psalms 95:3 (id: 25131)

above all gods: The psalmist refutes idolatry and paganism ([96:4–6](https://ref.ly/Ps96:4-Ps96:6); [135:15–18](https://ref.ly/Ps135:15-Ps135:18); see also [Isa 46:5–7](https://ref.ly/Isa46:5-Isa46:7)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 95:3

## Psalms 95:3–5 (id: 25130)

The Lord is the great King over the whole universe.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 95:3–PSA 95:5

## Psalms 95:4–5 (id: 25132)

The whole created order owes its existence to the sovereign Lord alone—not to various gods.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 95:4–PSA 95:5

## Psalms 95:6–7 (id: 25133)

The great King cares for his people as a shepherd cares for his flock ([Isa 40:11](https://ref.ly/Isa40:11)). • The Lord our maker*,* the Creator of heaven and earth, also made a people for himself ([Isa 45:9–12](https://ref.ly/Isa45:9-Isa45:12); [51:12–16](https://ref.ly/Isa51:12-Isa51:16)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 95:6–PSA 95:7

## Psalms 95:8 (id: 25135)

To harden your hearts means to be stubborn and resist the Lord’s grace (see [Num 20:2–13](https://ref.ly/Num20:2-Num20:13); see also [Matt 13:3–23](https://ref.ly/Matt13:3-Matt13:23); [John 12:37–43](https://ref.ly/John12:37-John12:43); [Eph 4:17–32](https://ref.ly/Eph4:17-Eph4:32); [Heb 3:6–19](https://ref.ly/Heb3:6-Heb3:19); [4:6–11](https://ref.ly/Heb4:6-Heb4:11)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 95:8

## Psalms 95:8–11 (id: 25134)

If people want to enter into the Lord’s rest, they need to respond immediately (see [Heb 3:7–4:11](https://ref.ly/Heb3:7-Heb4:11)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 95:8–PSA 95:11

## Psalms 95:9 (id: 25136)

Israel’s ancestors . . . saw the wonders of the Lord, but they foolishly did not try to grasp their significance (see [92:5–6](https://ref.ly/Ps92:5-Ps92:6)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 95:9

## Psalms 95:11 (id: 25129)

The generation of Israel that wandered in the wilderness for forty years failed to enter the place of rest that Israel enjoyed after the conquest of the land ([1 Kgs 8:56](https://ref.ly/1Kgs8:56); see [Deut 12:9](https://ref.ly/Deut12:9)). The Lord promised them the land and gave it to them ([Isa 28:12](https://ref.ly/Isa28:12)), but they did not obey him ([Isa 28:1](https://ref.ly/Isa28:1)). The warning reminds every generation of the need to obey in faith. • The rest that God provides includes peace, provision, and protection ([Ps 132:14–18](https://ref.ly/Ps132:14-Ps132:18)). The author of Hebrews challenged a new generation to enter the rest provided by Jesus Christ ([Heb 3:7–4:13](https://ref.ly/Heb3:7-Heb4:13)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 95:11

## Psalms 96:1 (id: 25141)

Three psalms open with the exhortation to sing a new song ([Pss 96](https://ref.ly/Ps96:1-Ps96:13), [98](https://ref.ly/Ps98:1-Ps98:9), [149](https://ref.ly/Ps149:1-Ps149:9)); the song celebrates the Lord’s universal kingship (see [33:3](https://ref.ly/Ps33:3)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 96:1

## Psalms 96:1–13 (id: 25137)

This psalm establishes the Lord’s universal kingship (see [Ps 93](https://ref.ly/Ps93:1-Ps93:5)) and prepares for the coming of the Lord to bring justice and righteousness into the world. The psalmist invites everyone to worship the Lord ([96:1–3](https://ref.ly/Ps96:1-Ps96:3)), the glorious Creator of all the earth ([96:4–6](https://ref.ly/Ps96:4-Ps96:6)), because worship is due to him alone ([96:7–9](https://ref.ly/Ps96:7-Ps96:9)). The universe joins in praise as the righteous Judge establishes a new order ([96:10–13](https://ref.ly/Ps96:10-Ps96:13)). • This psalm (along with [105:1–15](https://ref.ly/Ps105:1-Ps105:15); [106:1](https://ref.ly/Ps106:1), [47–48](https://ref.ly/Ps106:47-Ps106:48)) is included in David’s song of praise recorded in [1 Chr 16:1–43](https://ref.ly/1Chr16:1-1Chr16:43).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 96:1–PSA 96:13

## Psalms 96:4 (id: 25143)

Great is the Lord! . . . most worthy of praise: With this refrain, the poet exalts the Lord over all the gods ([95:3](https://ref.ly/Ps95:3)) and nations ([99:2](https://ref.ly/Ps99:2)). He inspires awe more than anyone or anything else ([76:7](https://ref.ly/Ps76:7), [12](https://ref.ly/Ps76:12); [89:7](https://ref.ly/Ps89:7); [99:3](https://ref.ly/Ps99:3); [111:9](https://ref.ly/Ps111:9)). He is beyond human possession or comprehension. The story of what he does to redeem his people causes them to praise him.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 96:4

## Psalms 96:4–6 (id: 25142)

The gods of the nations are as nothing before the glorious and majestic Creator of the earth.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 96:4–PSA 96:6

## Psalms 96:5 (id: 25144)

The Lord made the heavens*,* an even greater task than creating the earth. The idols*,* made by human hands ([115:4](https://ref.ly/Ps115:4)), created nothing.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 96:5

## Psalms 96:6 (id: 25145)

Honor and majesty: The Lord is glorious ([96:6](https://ref.ly/Ps96:6); [104:1](https://ref.ly/Ps104:1); [148:13](https://ref.ly/Ps148:13)), and so are his works in nature ([8:1](https://ref.ly/Ps8:1)) and in redemption ([111:3](https://ref.ly/Ps111:3); [145:5](https://ref.ly/Ps145:5)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 96:6

## Psalms 96:7 (id: 25146)

nations of the world (literally *families of the nations*): Families and clans represent subdivisions of the nations (see [Gen 12:3](https://ref.ly/Gen12:3)). • The nations must respond to the Lord’s glory ([Pss 8:1](https://ref.ly/Ps8:1); [19:1–4](https://ref.ly/Ps19:1-Ps19:4); [24:7](https://ref.ly/Ps24:7)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 96:7

## Psalms 96:8 (id: 25147)

The courts of God’s sanctuary were usually off\-limits to non\-Jewish people. In this psalm the nations of the world—the non\-Jews—are invited in ([65:4](https://ref.ly/Ps65:4); [84:2](https://ref.ly/Ps84:2), [10](https://ref.ly/Ps84:10); [100:4](https://ref.ly/Ps100:4); [116:19](https://ref.ly/Ps116:19); [135:2](https://ref.ly/Ps135:2); [Isa 1:12](https://ref.ly/Isa1:12)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 96:8

## Psalms 96:9 (id: 25148)

Worshipers should tremble in awe ([96:4](https://ref.ly/Ps96:4); see [18:7–15](https://ref.ly/Ps18:7-Ps18:15); [97:4](https://ref.ly/Ps97:4)) at the splendor of the Lord’s majesty and holiness ([Heb 12:25](https://ref.ly/Heb12:25)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 96:9

## Psalms 96:10 (id: 25138)

The Lord’s coming means the end of injustice. He rules fairly ([9:8](https://ref.ly/Ps9:8); [96:13](https://ref.ly/Ps96:13); [98:9](https://ref.ly/Ps98:9)) and inaugurates an era of harmony and order not experienced since Eden. • The Lord’s reign over the world is founded on the strong pillars of “righteousness and justice” ([89:14](https://ref.ly/Ps89:14)), so it cannot be shaken (cp. [11:3](https://ref.ly/Ps11:3)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 96:10

## Psalms 96:11–13 (id: 25139)

The psalmist exhorts the created order to respond with joy to the news of the Lord’s coming. Cp. a similar theme in [98:7–9](https://ref.ly/Ps98:7-Ps98:9).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 96:11–PSA 96:13

## Psalms 96:12 (id: 25140)

All of nature will experience renewal in God’s presence ([65:13](https://ref.ly/Ps65:13); [72:6](https://ref.ly/Ps72:6),[16](https://ref.ly/Ps72:16); [Isa 44:23](https://ref.ly/Isa44:23); [55:12](https://ref.ly/Isa55:12); [Rom 8:21–22](https://ref.ly/Rom8:21-Rom8:22)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 96:12

## Psalms 97:1 (id: 25151)

The farthest coastlands represent the most remote parts of the world.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 97:1

## Psalms 97:1–12 (id: 25149)

God is greatly exalted over the gods and over all the earth. Awe\-inspiring phenomena accompany his coming. Even the created order is visibly affected and the wicked perish, but the people of Zion love his coming and rejoice.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 97:1–PSA 97:12

## Psalms 97:2–4 (id: 25152)

Dark clouds . . . Fire . . . lightning: This language shows that the Lord is coming in judgment.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 97:2–PSA 97:4

## Psalms 97:5–7 (id: 25153)

The created order stirs at the coming of its King. He alone deserves worship.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 97:5–PSA 97:7

## Psalms 97:6 (id: 25154)

As the Lord enters the world, the testimony of his righteousness resounds from above ([50:6](https://ref.ly/Ps50:6)). • Every nation will view the open display of the Lord’s glory (see [8:1](https://ref.ly/Ps8:1); [19:1–4a](https://ref.ly/Ps19:1-Ps19:4); [24:7](https://ref.ly/Ps24:7); [Isa 40:5](https://ref.ly/Isa40:5)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 97:6

## Psalms 97:7 (id: 25155)

At the Lord’s coming, when every god must bow to him, those who worship other gods will face their own folly (see [95:3–5](https://ref.ly/Ps95:3-Ps95:5)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 97:7

## Psalms 97:8–12 (id: 25156)

Jerusalem rejoices at the news of the Lord’s coming, for he brings justice and rescues the upright of heart.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 97:8–PSA 97:12

## Psalms 97:11 (id: 25150)

The godly people of integrity (see [Prov 2:7](https://ref.ly/Prov2:7), [21](https://ref.ly/Prov2:21); [3:32](https://ref.ly/Prov3:32); [11:6](https://ref.ly/Prov11:6), [11](https://ref.ly/Prov11:11); [14:2](https://ref.ly/Prov14:2)), whose hearts are right*,* maintain a relationship with the Lord and with others ([Pss 94:15](https://ref.ly/Ps94:15); [125:4](https://ref.ly/Ps125:4)). The wicked plan the downfall of the godly ([11:2](https://ref.ly/Ps11:2)), but the Lord rescues them ([11:1](https://ref.ly/Ps11:1); [36:10](https://ref.ly/Ps36:10)). Then the sorrows of the godly turn to joy and praise ([32:11](https://ref.ly/Ps32:11); [64:10](https://ref.ly/Ps64:10); [111:1](https://ref.ly/Ps111:1); [119:7](https://ref.ly/Ps119:7)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 97:11

## Psalms 98:1–9 (id: 25157)

This psalm celebrates the Lord’s kingship. The Lord is Israel’s true King, its champion and savior. His people sing a new song celebrating his victorious power and faithfulness to them. The Lord displays his righteous rule to all the nations throughout the earth, which will culminate in a worldwide kingdom of justice ([98:2](https://ref.ly/Ps98:2), [9](https://ref.ly/Ps98:9)). Consequently, all the earth must worship and rejoice together because the Lord is coming ([98:4–6](https://ref.ly/Ps98:4-Ps98:6)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 98:1–PSA 98:9

## Psalms 98:2–3 (id: 25158)

The Lord makes known his righteousness and faithfulness (see also [Isa 52:10](https://ref.ly/Isa52:10)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 98:2–PSA 98:3

## Psalms 98:4–6 (id: 25159)

The psalmist invites the whole earth to worship the King (see [96:1](https://ref.ly/Ps96:1)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 98:4–PSA 98:6

## Psalms 98:6 (id: 25160)

The Temple musicians used trumpets to call people together for meetings (cp. [81:3](https://ref.ly/Ps81:3)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 98:6

## Psalms 98:7–9 (id: 25161)

The created order is personified as rejoicing at the coming of the righteous Judge (see [93:3–4](https://ref.ly/Ps93:3-Ps93:4); [96:11–13](https://ref.ly/Ps96:11-Ps96:13)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 98:7–PSA 98:9

## Psalms 99:1 (id: 25164)

It is fitting to tremble and quake in response to the Lord’s holiness (see [96:9](https://ref.ly/Ps96:9)). • The throne between the cherubim refers to the cover of the Ark of the Covenant ([Exod 25:17–22](https://ref.ly/Exod25:17-Exod25:22)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 99:1

## Psalms 99:1–5 (id: 25162)

The Lord is the holy and righteous King ([Isa 6:1–5](https://ref.ly/Isa6:1-Isa6:5)). Mount Zion, the location of the Lord’s Temple, metaphorically stands as the highest point on earth ([Ps 113:4](https://ref.ly/Ps113:4); [Isa 2:2](https://ref.ly/Isa2:2); [6:1](https://ref.ly/Isa6:1)). From this summit, the Great King ([Ps 47:2](https://ref.ly/Ps47:2)) can see, rule over, and receive praise from all nations and peoples.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 99:1–PSA 99:5

## Psalms 99:1–9 (id: 25163)

The psalmist calls the nations to worship the Lord, the king of the earth who rules from Zion.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 99:1–PSA 99:9

## Psalms 99:4 (id: 25165)

The qualities of the Lord’s rule include strength, justice*,* love, fairness*,* and righteousness (see [93:4](https://ref.ly/Ps93:4); [97:2](https://ref.ly/Ps97:2), [6–7](https://ref.ly/Ps97:6-Ps97:7), [12](https://ref.ly/Ps97:12); [98:2–3](https://ref.ly/Ps98:2-Ps98:3), [9](https://ref.ly/Ps98:9); [138:6](https://ref.ly/Ps138:6)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 99:4

## Psalms 99:6 (id: 25167)

Moses and Samuel were great models and leaders who had prayed on behalf of the Lord’s people ([Exod 32:31–32](https://ref.ly/Exod32:31-Exod32:32); [1 Sam 12:23](https://ref.ly/1Sam12:23)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 99:6

## Psalms 99:6–8 (id: 25166)

God showed favor by responding to his people in the past, while holding sinners accountable.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 99:6–PSA 99:8

## Psalms 99:7 (id: 25168)

The Lord spoke to Moses and Aaron from the pillar of cloud ([Exod 33:9](https://ref.ly/Exod33:9); [Num 12:5–6](https://ref.ly/Num12:5-Num12:6)), and for a time, the people responded to the revelation.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 99:7

## Psalms 100:1–5 (id: 23673)

This psalm calls all nations to come to Jerusalem to worship the Lord and acknowledge his goodness to Israel.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 100:1–PSA 100:5

## Psalms 100:3 (id: 23674)

The Lord is the one who determines who his people are. • the sheep of his pasture: God will guide and protect his people ([23:1](https://ref.ly/Ps23:1), [4](https://ref.ly/Ps23:4)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 100:3

## Psalms 100:4 (id: 23675)

Gates and courts were part of the Temple in Jerusalem.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 100:4

## Psalms 101:1–8 (id: 23676)

This hymn expresses a commitment to live with integrity and to avoid evil. Jesus meets this ideal.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 101:1–PSA 101:8

## Psalms 101:2 (id: 23677)

in my own home (literally *in my house*): This commitment to integrity might refer to private life at home. Some interpreters view *my house* as referring to the king’s palace; the commitment would then refer to the policies of his administration. • Leading a life of integrity means choosing a wise lifestyle.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 101:2

## Psalms 101:4–5 (id: 23678)

The psalmist hates what the Lord hates ([Prov 6:16–19](https://ref.ly/Prov6:16-Prov6:19); see [Pss 5:5](https://ref.ly/Ps5:5); [11:4–5](https://ref.ly/Ps11:4-Ps11:5)). • Perverse ideas come from corrupt human hearts (cp. [18:26](https://ref.ly/Ps18:26)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 101:4–PSA 101:5

## Psalms 101:6 (id: 23679)

The psalmist surrounds himself with people who are also committed to integrity ([101:2](https://ref.ly/Ps101:2)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 101:6

## Psalms 101:7–8 (id: 23680)

The psalmist commits himself to ridding his house and the city of the Lord—representing the entire kingdom—of all evil.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 101:7–PSA 101:8

## Psalms 102:1–2 (id: 23682)

The psalmist appeals to the Lord not to turn away (or *hide your face*). Israel experienced his turning his face away during their exile.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 102:1–PSA 102:2

## Psalms 102:1–28 (id: 23681)

A frail and afflicted human being prays for the Lord’s compassion on Jerusalem and for his presence with its inhabitants.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 102:1–PSA 102:28

## Psalms 102:3 (id: 23698)

Smoke is an image of transitory life ([37:20](https://ref.ly/Ps37:20); [68:2](https://ref.ly/Ps68:2)). • The psalmist’s bones represent his whole being (see [6:2](https://ref.ly/Ps6:2); [34:19–22](https://ref.ly/Ps34:19-Ps34:22)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 102:3

## Psalms 102:4 (id: 23699)

Like dried grass*,* the psalmist senses his life ebbing away.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 102:4

## Psalms 102:5 (id: 23700)

skin and bones: The psalmist has wasted away because of his anguish (see [102:9](https://ref.ly/Ps102:9); [109:24](https://ref.ly/Ps109:24)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 102:5

## Psalms 102:6 (id: 23701)

The owl was associated with ruin and desolation ([Isa 34:11](https://ref.ly/Isa34:11), [15](https://ref.ly/Isa34:15)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 102:6

## Psalms 102:7–8 (id: 23702)

The psalmist cannot sleep (see [63:6–8](https://ref.ly/Ps63:6-Ps63:8)). Like a bird on the roof*,* he feels isolated from both friends (see [88:8](https://ref.ly/Ps88:8)) and enemies.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 102:7–PSA 102:8

## Psalms 102:10 (id: 23683)

The psalmist blames the Lord for his troubles.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 102:10

## Psalms 102:11 (id: 23684)

The psalmist’s existence seems empty and transitory ([102:4](https://ref.ly/Ps102:4); [109:23](https://ref.ly/Ps109:23); [144:4](https://ref.ly/Ps144:4)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 102:11

## Psalms 102:12 (id: 23686)

forever . . . to every generation: The frailty of humans ([102:3–11](https://ref.ly/Ps102:3-Ps102:11)) contrasts with the permanence of the Lord.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 102:12

## Psalms 102:12–17 (id: 23685)

The topic changes from the psalmist’s miseries to the Lord’s glory. A vision of the Lord’s compassionate kingship gives him confidence in Zion’s future.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 102:12–PSA 102:17

## Psalms 102:13 (id: 23687)

Now is the time for the Lord to restore Jerusalem from exile (see [75:2](https://ref.ly/Ps75:2); [Jer 29:10](https://ref.ly/Jer29:10); [Dan 9:1–19](https://ref.ly/Dan9:1-Dan9:19)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 102:13

## Psalms 102:15–16 (id: 23688)

When the Lord arises ([102:13](https://ref.ly/Ps102:13)), the nations will tremble with fear because they will see his glory (see [8:1](https://ref.ly/Ps8:1); [19:1–4a](https://ref.ly/Ps19:1-Ps19:4); [24:7](https://ref.ly/Ps24:7)). The rebuilding of Zion and the Temple portray God’s glory and fulfill this promise. An even greater fulfillment will come with the New Jerusalem ([Rev 21](https://ref.ly/Rev21:1-Rev21:27)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 102:15–PSA 102:16

## Psalms 102:17 (id: 23689)

The people of Israel were destitute (or *naked*) during the Exile.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 102:17

## Psalms 102:18 (id: 23691)

Let this be recorded: The written record stands as a memorial to the Lord’s goodness.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 102:18

## Psalms 102:18–22 (id: 23690)

The Lord will have mercy; Jews and Gentiles alike will worship him.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 102:18–PSA 102:22

## Psalms 102:19 (id: 23692)

The heavenly sanctuary refers to God’s holy place on high (see [92:8–10](https://ref.ly/Ps92:8-Ps92:10)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 102:19

## Psalms 102:22 (id: 23693)
