The multitudes—both Jews and Gentiles—will join in the worship of the Lord (see [96:7](https://ref.ly/Ps96:7), [9](https://ref.ly/Ps96:9); [106:48](https://ref.ly/Ps106:48); [Isa 2:2–4](https://ref.ly/Isa2:2-Isa2:4); [43:10–13](https://ref.ly/Isa43:10-Isa43:13); [57:15](https://ref.ly/Isa57:15); [60:3–7](https://ref.ly/Isa60:3-Isa60:7)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 102:22

## Psalms 102:23–28 (id: 23694)

Although the psalmist suffers in the present, he bases his hope for the future on the Lord’s past faithfulness.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 102:23–PSA 102:28

## Psalms 102:24 (id: 23695)

The psalmist draws a contrast between his days ([102:23](https://ref.ly/Ps102:23)) and God’s years (cp. [90:4](https://ref.ly/Ps90:4)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 102:24

## Psalms 102:25–27 (id: 23696)

In contrast with the permanence of the Creator, the created order will wear out like a piece of clothing (see [Isa 40:28](https://ref.ly/Isa40:28)). • The writer to the Hebrews describes this passage as having been addressed to Jesus, the Son ([Heb 1:10–12](https://ref.ly/Heb1:10-Heb1:12)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 102:25–PSA 102:27

## Psalms 102:28 (id: 23697)

The Lord’s presence provides the basis for the security and happiness of his people ([23:6](https://ref.ly/Ps23:6)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 102:28

## Psalms 103:1–2 (id: 23704)

Let all that I am praise the Lord: [Pss 103](https://ref.ly/Ps103:1-Ps103:22) and [104](https://ref.ly/Ps104:1-Ps104:35) each open and close with this commitment ([103:1–2](https://ref.ly/Ps103:1-Ps103:2), [22](https://ref.ly/Ps103:22); [104:1](https://ref.ly/Ps104:1), [35](https://ref.ly/Ps104:35); see also [146:1](https://ref.ly/Ps146:1)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 103:1–PSA 103:2

## Psalms 103:1–6 (id: 23705)

The psalmist offers praise for the Lord’s goodness.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 103:1–PSA 103:6

## Psalms 103:1–22 (id: 23703)

This psalm celebrates the Lord’s perfection, compassion, forgiveness, and goodness.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 103:1–PSA 103:22

## Psalms 103:7–8 (id: 23713)

The Lord revealed himself to Moses in distinctive ways that ensured his relationship with his people (see [Exod 34:6–7](https://ref.ly/Exod34:6-Exod34:7); [Num 14:18](https://ref.ly/Num14:18)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 103:7–PSA 103:8

## Psalms 103:9 (id: 23714)

If the Lord were to constantly accuse or remain angry forever*,* no one would be left (see [Isa 54:7–8](https://ref.ly/Isa54:7-Isa54:8); [57:16](https://ref.ly/Isa57:16)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 103:9

## Psalms 103:11–12 (id: 23706)

The Lord’s love and forgiveness are infinite and complete.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 103:11–PSA 103:12

## Psalms 103:13 (id: 23707)

The Lord is like a father to his children: This analogy forms the basis for Jesus’ teaching about God’s fatherhood (see [Matt 5:43–48](https://ref.ly/Matt5:43-Matt5:48); [6:1](https://ref.ly/Matt6:1); [10:19–20](https://ref.ly/Matt10:19-Matt10:20); [12:50](https://ref.ly/Matt12:50); [Luke 6:36](https://ref.ly/Luke6:36); [12:29–32](https://ref.ly/Luke12:29-Luke12:32); [John 8:31–59](https://ref.ly/John8:31-John8:59); [15:1–8](https://ref.ly/John15:1-John15:8); see also [2 Sam 7:14](https://ref.ly/2Sam7:14); [Jer 3:19](https://ref.ly/Jer3:19); [31:9](https://ref.ly/Jer31:9); [Mal 1:6](https://ref.ly/Mal1:6); [2 Cor 6:16–18](https://ref.ly/2Cor6:16-2Cor6:18)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 103:13

## Psalms 103:14–16 (id: 23708)

The Lord compassionately cares for frail humans (see [37:2](https://ref.ly/Ps37:2); [90:5](https://ref.ly/Ps90:5); [92:7](https://ref.ly/Ps92:7); [102:4](https://ref.ly/Ps102:4); [Isa 40:6–8](https://ref.ly/Isa40:6-Isa40:8)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 103:14–PSA 103:16

## Psalms 103:17–19 (id: 23709)

the love of the Lord remains forever: The Lord’s kingdom is everlasting, so he commits himself to his people across many generations.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 103:17–PSA 103:19

## Psalms 103:18 (id: 23710)

To obey God means to be faithful and loyal to him.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 103:18

## Psalms 103:20–21 (id: 23711)

The psalmist exhorts the Lord’s angels, his servants and messengers, to praise the Lord.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 103:20–PSA 103:21

## Psalms 103:22 (id: 23712)

God’s kingdom extends over all things, so all things are called to praise the Lord. • The concluding phrase takes us back to [103:1–2](https://ref.ly/Ps103:1-Ps103:2).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 103:22

## Psalms 104:1 (id: 23722)

Let all that I am praise the Lord: [Pss 103](https://ref.ly/Ps103:1-Ps103:22) and [104](https://ref.ly/Ps104:1-Ps104:35) each open and close with this commitment to praise ([103:1–2](https://ref.ly/Ps103:1-Ps103:2), [22](https://ref.ly/Ps103:22); [104:1](https://ref.ly/Ps104:1), [35](https://ref.ly/Ps104:35)). • how great you are! This acclamation expresses praise for rescue (see also [35:27](https://ref.ly/Ps35:27); [40:16](https://ref.ly/Ps40:16); [70:4](https://ref.ly/Ps70:4)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 104:1

## Psalms 104:1–35 (id: 23715)

This creation hymn (see also [Pss 8](https://ref.ly/Ps8:1-Ps8:9), [33](https://ref.ly/Ps33:1-Ps33:22), [145](https://ref.ly/Ps145:1-Ps145:21)) exalts God’s goodness and majesty. The psalmist reflects on the present world, the original creation, and a future new creation. He sees both creations as marvelously and wisely made (cp. [139:14](https://ref.ly/Ps139:14)), as the work of the Lord’s Spirit ([104:30](https://ref.ly/Ps104:30); [Gen 1:2](https://ref.ly/Gen1:2); [2 Cor 3:6](https://ref.ly/2Cor3:6)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 104:1–PSA 104:35

## Psalms 104:2–4 (id: 23723)

The psalmist interacts with two of the days of creation (see [Gen 1:1–8](https://ref.ly/Gen1:1-Gen1:8)), when God created the heavens and light.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 104:2–PSA 104:4

## Psalms 104:3 (id: 23734)

This poetic portrayal envisions the clouds as beams that support heaven.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 104:3

## Psalms 104:4 (id: 23735)

Wind and lightning are seen as divine messengers. The Lord uses weather phenomena as he desires ([77:17–18](https://ref.ly/Ps77:17-Ps77:18); [78:26](https://ref.ly/Ps78:26); [135:7](https://ref.ly/Ps135:7); [148:5–6](https://ref.ly/Ps148:5-Ps148:6)). • The psalmist interacts with day three of creation ([Gen 1:9–13](https://ref.ly/Gen1:9-Gen1:13)). The Lord is master of water and earth.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 104:4

## Psalms 104:6 (id: 23736)

At first, water covered the earth.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 104:6

## Psalms 104:7 (id: 23737)

The Lord created dry ground on day three of creation ([Gen 1:9–13](https://ref.ly/Gen1:9-Gen1:13)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 104:7

## Psalms 104:8 (id: 23738)

The earth originates in God’s will.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 104:8

## Psalms 104:9 (id: 23740)

The Lord set a firm boundary for the seas to protect the land. God’s sovereignty over sea and land was an argument against the existence of Baal, whom the Canaanites celebrated as victorious over the waters (see [Ps 29](https://ref.ly/Ps29:1-Ps29:11)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 104:9

## Psalms 104:9–10 (id: 23739)

The Lord reigns over all bodies of water, including those on land. He replaced chaotic waters with order and abundance, and the earth became a splendid place for animals and humans, with water refreshing the ground, the birds, and the animals.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 104:9–PSA 104:10

## Psalms 104:11–18 (id: 23716)

The psalmist celebrates animal, plant, and human life, as well as the Lord’s abundant provision for all of it ([Gen 1:9–30](https://ref.ly/Gen1:9-Gen1:30)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 104:11–PSA 104:18

## Psalms 104:14 (id: 23717)

people to use: People are the managers of the created order, and they receive nourishment from the work of their hands.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 104:14

## Psalms 104:15 (id: 23718)

While both can be misused (cp. [Prov 21:17](https://ref.ly/Prov21:17)), the Lord provides wine and olive oil as gifts to enhance life. Life is sustained by basic food, represented by bread.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 104:15

## Psalms 104:17–18 (id: 23719)

The storks migrated from northern Europe and resided in Palestine during the winter. • hyraxes: These animals are about the size of a rabbit and live in rocky places.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 104:17–PSA 104:18

## Psalms 104:19 (id: 23721)

the moon to mark the seasons: Ancient Israel based its calendar on the cycles of the moon. • the sun knows when to set: This is a poetic description from the perspective of normal observation. The sun goes down at a regular time every evening.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 104:19

## Psalms 104:19–23 (id: 23720)

The psalmist rejoices in the order of night and day, marking day four of creation ([Gen 1:14–19](https://ref.ly/Gen1:14-Gen1:19)). This cycle gives all creatures an opportunity to live.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 104:19–PSA 104:23

## Psalms 104:20–23 (id: 23724)

Cycles of darkness and dawn mark the days on earth.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 104:20–PSA 104:23

## Psalms 104:24–26 (id: 23725)

The Lord’s works testify to his wisdom. All parts fit together—land and sea, night and day, land creatures and sea creatures. The Lord’s wisdom makes life orderly and wonderful.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 104:24–PSA 104:26

## Psalms 104:25 (id: 23726)

The ocean, . . . teeming with life of every kind (see [Gen 1:20–21](https://ref.ly/Gen1:20-Gen1:21)), exemplifies the Lord’s creative activities.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 104:25

## Psalms 104:26 (id: 23727)

ships sailing: Commercial vessels engaged in sea trade were one of the wonders of the ancient Near East (see [Isa 2:16](https://ref.ly/Isa2:16); [23:1](https://ref.ly/Isa23:1), [3](https://ref.ly/Isa23:3)). • Leviathan: The psalmist says that this feared creature is nothing but the Lord’s pet.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 104:26

## Psalms 104:27–30 (id: 23728)

All life depends on the gracious sustenance of the Lord of life and death (cp. [Matt 6:11](https://ref.ly/Matt6:11)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 104:27–PSA 104:30

## Psalms 104:29–30 (id: 23729)

When you give them your breath: Life on earth is only possible as the Lord’s gift, symbolized by his breath (Hebrew ruakh, “breath, wind, spirit”). The Lord’s Spirit is the agent of renewal ([Isa 32:15–20](https://ref.ly/Isa32:15-Isa32:20)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 104:29–PSA 104:30

## Psalms 104:31 (id: 23731)

The Lord reveals his presence in the created order (see [8:1](https://ref.ly/Ps8:1); [19:1–4](https://ref.ly/Ps19:1-Ps19:4); [24:7](https://ref.ly/Ps24:7)) and takes pleasure in his new creation (see [Isa 65:19](https://ref.ly/Isa65:19)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 104:31

## Psalms 104:31–35 (id: 23730)

The psalmist moves from describing the known creation to anticipating the new creation, when the Lord will renew the created order into a world without sinners.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 104:31–PSA 104:35

## Psalms 104:32 (id: 23732)

The trembling earth and the smoking mountains represent the Lord’s coming in judgment against sinners and salvation for his faithful people (see[18:7–15](https://ref.ly/Ps18:7-Ps18:15)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 104:32

## Psalms 104:35 (id: 23733)

The Lord will remove all forms of evil that defile his creation. • The concluding phrase takes us back to [104:1](https://ref.ly/Ps104:1) (see also [103:1–2](https://ref.ly/Ps103:1-Ps103:2), [22](https://ref.ly/Ps103:22); [146:1](https://ref.ly/Ps146:1)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 104:35

## Psalms 105:1–5 (id: 23742)

The poet begins with the exhortation Give thanks (see also [106:1](https://ref.ly/Ps106:1); [107:1](https://ref.ly/Ps107:1); [118:1](https://ref.ly/Ps118:1); [136:1](https://ref.ly/Ps136:1)). The other psalms continue with the refrain “for he is good!” The rest of [Ps 105](https://ref.ly/Ps105:1-Ps105:45) tells of God’s goodness.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 105:1–PSA 105:5

## Psalms 105:1–45 (id: 23741)

This hymn praises the Lord’s faithfulness to Abraham and his descendants in all their journeys—from Ur to Canaan ([105:12](https://ref.ly/Ps105:12)), to Egypt ([105:17](https://ref.ly/Ps105:17), [23](https://ref.ly/Ps105:23)), through the wilderness ([105:37](https://ref.ly/Ps105:37), [41](https://ref.ly/Ps105:41)), and back to Canaan ([105:44](https://ref.ly/Ps105:44)). All of this fulfilled the Lord’s promise to Abraham ([105:9](https://ref.ly/Ps105:9), [42](https://ref.ly/Ps105:42)), which was the basis for Israel’s very existence. Joseph, whose suffering was changed into glory, is a paradigm of encouragement for Israel ([105:16–25](https://ref.ly/Ps105:16-Ps105:25)). •[Psalm 105:1–15](https://ref.ly/Ps105:1-Ps105:15) (along with 96; [106:1](https://ref.ly/Ps106:1), [47–48](https://ref.ly/Ps106:47-Ps106:48)) is included in David’s song of praise recorded in [1 Chr 16](https://ref.ly/1Chr16:1-1Chr16:43).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 105:1–PSA 105:45

## Psalms 105:6–11 (id: 23757)

The story of Israel is based on the Lord’s commitment to Abraham. Even when a question arises about the future of God’s covenant with David ([Ps 89](https://ref.ly/Ps89:1-Ps89:52)), God’s covenant with Abraham stands, as does the spiritual bond between God and Israel, Abraham’s descendants.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 105:6–PSA 105:11

## Psalms 105:8 (id: 23758)

The covenant is the Lord’s irrevocable oath to be the Father of Abraham and his descendants (see [Gen 12:1–9](https://ref.ly/Gen12:1-Gen12:9); [15:1–21](https://ref.ly/Gen15:1-Gen15:21)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 105:8

## Psalms 105:11 (id: 23743)

God promised the land of Canaan to Abraham’s descendants as their special possession*,* where they could live as God’s people ([105:44–45](https://ref.ly/Ps105:44-Ps105:45); [Gen 12:7](https://ref.ly/Gen12:7); [15:7–21](https://ref.ly/Gen15:7-Gen15:21)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 105:11

## Psalms 105:12–15 (id: 23744)

The Lord protected Israel’s patriarchs.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 105:12–PSA 105:15

## Psalms 105:15 (id: 23745)

Abraham was one of the nation’s prophets ([Gen 20:7](https://ref.ly/Gen20:7)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 105:15

## Psalms 105:16–22 (id: 23746)

These verses tell the story of Joseph (see [Gen 37–41](https://ref.ly/Gen37:1-Gen41:57)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 105:16–PSA 105:22

## Psalms 105:19 (id: 23747)

tested Joseph’s character: See [Gen 39:6–12](https://ref.ly/Gen39:6-Gen39:12).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 105:19

## Psalms 105:23 (id: 23749)

Egypt (Hebrew mitsrayim) is called the land of Ham.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 105:23

## Psalms 105:23–25 (id: 23748)

These verses tell the story of Israel’s affliction in Egypt (see [Exod 1:1–14](https://ref.ly/Exod1:1-Exod1:14)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 105:23–PSA 105:25

## Psalms 105:26–36 (id: 23750)

The psalmist recounts the story of Moses and the plagues in Egypt ([Exod 7:20–12:30](https://ref.ly/Exod7:20-Exod12:30)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 105:26–PSA 105:36

## Psalms 105:37 (id: 23752)

not one . . . stumbled: The Lord protected all of his people (cp. [9:3](https://ref.ly/Ps9:3)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 105:37

## Psalms 105:37–45 (id: 23751)

The Exodus and the conquest of Canaan fulfilled God’s promise to Abraham, Isaac, and Jacob ([105:9–10](https://ref.ly/Ps105:9-Ps105:10)). Unlike [Ps 78](https://ref.ly/Ps78:1-Ps78:72), the poet recites the Lord’s goodness without commenting on Israel’s history of rebellion (cp. [Ps 106](https://ref.ly/Ps106:1-Ps106:48)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 105:37–PSA 105:45

## Psalms 105:39 (id: 23753)

The Lord’s presence was as evident to all as a fire in the darkness ([Exod 13:22](https://ref.ly/Exod13:22)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 105:39

## Psalms 105:42–45 (id: 23754)

The story of redemption is also the story of the Lord’s faithfulness.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 105:42–PSA 105:45

## Psalms 105:44 (id: 23755)

Canaan was a land of pagan nations (see [111:6](https://ref.ly/Ps111:6)). The psalmist might also be reflecting on God’s promise to Abraham ([Gen 24:60](https://ref.ly/Gen24:60)) regarding the lands given to Isaac ([Gen 26:3](https://ref.ly/Gen26:3)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 105:44

## Psalms 105:45 (id: 23756)

The Lord planned for Israel to testify about him by obeying him; Israel was to be his model people.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 105:45

## Psalms 106:1 (id: 23764)

Praise the Lord! This refrain (Hebrew haleluyah) characterizes four small subgroups in the psalms: [104–106](https://ref.ly/Ps104:1-Ps106:48), [111–113](https://ref.ly/Ps111:1-Ps113:9), [115–117](https://ref.ly/Ps115:1-Ps117:2), [146–150](https://ref.ly/Ps146:1-Ps150:6).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 106:1

## Psalms 106:1–48 (id: 23759)

The Israelite community in exile confessed the Lord’s goodness and justice and their own historic sinfulness. From the humble state of exile, they pleaded for redemption and restoration, asking to be gathered back from all the places the Lord had scattered them in his wrath. The psalm does not end in despair but with the memory of the Lord’s former mercy and the hope that his mercy will be renewed ([106:44–48](https://ref.ly/Ps106:44-Ps106:48)). Israel failed, but the Lord is constant. • Verses 1, [47–48](https://ref.ly/Ps47:1-Ps48:14) (along with [Pss 96](https://ref.ly/Ps96:1-Ps96:13); [105:1–15](https://ref.ly/Ps105:1-Ps105:15)) are included in David’s song of praise recorded in [1 Chr 16:1–43](https://ref.ly/1Chr16:1-1Chr16:43).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 106:1–PSA 106:48

## Psalms 106:2–3 (id: 23765)

Wise people who practice justice and righteousness receive encouragement to proclaim the Lord’s great acts.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 106:2–PSA 106:3

## Psalms 106:4–5 (id: 23775)

The poet prays individually for the Lord’s favor before leading the community confession that follows.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 106:4–PSA 106:5

## Psalms 106:6 (id: 23784)

The story of Israel’s redemption encompasses their sinful response from the days of the ancestors to the present ([106:43](https://ref.ly/Ps106:43)). The themes of sin and divine wrath both open and close Book Four ([90:1–9](https://ref.ly/Ps90:1-Ps90:9); [106:6](https://ref.ly/Ps106:6), [23](https://ref.ly/Ps106:23), [43](https://ref.ly/Ps106:43)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 106:6

## Psalms 106:6–13 (id: 23783)

The community joins together to confess their sins and their ancestors’ many acts of unbelief.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 106:6–PSA 106:13

## Psalms 106:9 (id: 23785)

Red Sea: See [Exod 14:15–31](https://ref.ly/Exod14:15-Exod14:31).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 106:9

## Psalms 106:13 (id: 23760)

They wouldn’t wait: God’s impatient people did not trust him to work according to his will (e.g., see [Exod 15:24](https://ref.ly/Exod15:24); [16:2–3](https://ref.ly/Exod16:2-Exod16:3); [17:1–3](https://ref.ly/Exod17:1-Exod17:3); [Num 14:26–45](https://ref.ly/Num14:26-Num14:45); [21:4–9](https://ref.ly/Num21:4-Num21:9)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 106:13

## Psalms 106:15 (id: 23761)

he sent a plague: See [Exod 32:35](https://ref.ly/Exod32:35); [Num 11:33](https://ref.ly/Num11:33).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 106:15

## Psalms 106:16–18 (id: 23762)

The people became jealous because they presumed to have the same privileges as God’s appointed priests (see [Num 16:1–35](https://ref.ly/Num16:1-Num16:35)). • the earth opened up: See [Num 16:28–33](https://ref.ly/Num16:28-Num16:33).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 106:16–PSA 106:18

## Psalms 106:19–23 (id: 23763)

they bowed before an image: The people forgot their Savior and committed the sin of idolatry (see [Exod 32:1–6](https://ref.ly/Exod32:1-Exod32:6)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 106:19–PSA 106:23

## Psalms 106:22 (id: 23766)

The land of Ham here means Egypt ([106:21](https://ref.ly/Ps106:21)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 106:22

## Psalms 106:24–25 (id: 23767)

The people disobeyed God’s command when they refused to enter the pleasant land (the Promised Land; see [Jer 3:19](https://ref.ly/Jer3:19)). • they wouldn’t believe his promise: See [Num 13:25–14:12](https://ref.ly/Num13:25-Num14:12).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 106:24–PSA 106:25

## Psalms 106:26–27 (id: 23768)

God’s judgment when Israel refused to obey was death and exile ([Num 14:26–30](https://ref.ly/Num14:26-Num14:30)). The occasion for these severe judgments seems to have been disobeying God’s word ([Ps 106:24–25](https://ref.ly/Ps106:24-Ps106:25)) and provoking the Lord’s wrath ([106:28–46](https://ref.ly/Ps106:28-Ps106:46)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 106:26–PSA 106:27

## Psalms 106:28 (id: 23770)

the worship of Baal at Peor: See[Num 25:3](https://ref.ly/Num25:3); [Deut 4:3](https://ref.ly/Deut4:3).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 106:28

## Psalms 106:28–39 (id: 23769)

Israel’s idolatry outside of the land came with them into the land. Their nature did not change; they continued to provoke the Lord to anger by their actions.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 106:28–PSA 106:39

## Psalms 106:30–33 (id: 23771)

Phinehas, who executed a flagrantly apostate Israelite man ([Num 25:3–8](https://ref.ly/Num25:3-Num25:8)), is an even better model of a righteous man than Moses, who failed at Meribah ([Num 20:11–13](https://ref.ly/Num20:11-Num20:13)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 106:30–PSA 106:33

## Psalms 106:34 (id: 23772)

Israel continued to disobey the word of the Lord while living in the Promised Land. Rather than destroying the nations, Israel accepted them and their ways (see [Judg 2:1–3](https://ref.ly/Judg2:1-Judg2:3), [11–15](https://ref.ly/Judg2:11-Judg2:15); [3:5–6](https://ref.ly/Judg3:5-Judg3:6)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 106:34

## Psalms 106:37 (id: 23773)

Pagan gods were demons (see [Deut 32:17](https://ref.ly/Deut32:17)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 106:37

## Psalms 106:39 (id: 23774)

Idolatry, like adultery*,* defiles God’s people (see [Lev 18:24](https://ref.ly/Lev18:24); [Hos 5:3](https://ref.ly/Hos5:3)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 106:39

## Psalms 106:40 (id: 23777)

God abhorred Israel’s sin, as he does all sin.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 106:40

## Psalms 106:40–46 (id: 23776)

The psalmist returns to the Babylonian exile ([106:26–27](https://ref.ly/Ps106:26-Ps106:27)). The Lord judged Israel severely, but he also restrained his wrath, remembering the covenant he had made with Abraham.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 106:40–PSA 106:46

## Psalms 106:43–44 (id: 23778)

When Israel was finally destroyed*,* the destruction was not complete. The Lord pitied them*,* so he left a remnant.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 106:43–PSA 106:44

## Psalms 106:45 (id: 23779)

He remembered . . . and relented: Unlike Israel, the Lord is faithful to his covenant ([105:8](https://ref.ly/Ps105:8)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 106:45

## Psalms 106:46 (id: 23780)

As harsh as the Exile was, the Lord still protected his people (see [2 Kgs 25:27–29](https://ref.ly/2Kgs25:27-2Kgs25:29)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 106:46

## Psalms 106:47 (id: 23781)

Gather us back: The community prays for restoration from exile (see [102:19–22](https://ref.ly/Ps102:19-Ps102:22); [107:3](https://ref.ly/Ps107:3); see also [Isa 11:12](https://ref.ly/Isa11:12); [40:11](https://ref.ly/Isa40:11); [43:5](https://ref.ly/Isa43:5); [54:7](https://ref.ly/Isa54:7); [56:8](https://ref.ly/Isa56:8); [66:18](https://ref.ly/Isa66:18)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 106:47

## Psalms 106:48 (id: 23782)

This doxology concludes Book Four (cp. [41:13](https://ref.ly/Ps41:13); [89:52](https://ref.ly/Ps89:52)). • from everlasting to everlasting! The reference to God’s eternal nature links to the opening of Book Four ([90:1–2](https://ref.ly/Ps90:1-Ps90:2)). • Let all the people say, “Amen!”: The Hebrew word ’amen means “It is true.” The godly accept the Lord’s will in exile and his promise to be their God.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 106:48

## Psalms 107:1–43 (id: 23786)

This psalm is a hymn of praise to God the Redeemer. After an introduction exhorting the redeemed to praise God for his goodness ([107:1–3](https://ref.ly/Ps107:1-Ps107:3)), the psalmist brings together four case studies of people whom the Lord redeemed from adversity ([107:4–32](https://ref.ly/Ps107:4-Ps107:32)). He then sums up the Lord’s sovereignty ([107:33–42](https://ref.ly/Ps107:33-Ps107:42)) and concludes with an invitation to discern God’s unfailing love in all areas of life ([107:43](https://ref.ly/Ps107:43)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 107:1–PSA 107:43

## Psalms 107:2 (id: 23794)

The redeemed might be all who came out of exile.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 107:2

## Psalms 107:3 (id: 23800)

exiles: People came from all nations where the people of Israel and Judah had been scattered.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 107:3

## Psalms 107:4–9 (id: 23801)

Those who were lost in the wilderness thank God for his rescue. The wilderness might be a metaphor for leaving the path of wisdom ([1:1](https://ref.ly/Ps1:1); [Prov 4:10–15](https://ref.ly/Prov4:10-Prov4:15)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 107:4–PSA 107:9

## Psalms 107:6 (id: 23805)

The psalmist does not specify the occasion of his trouble and distress. The generic nature of the adversity permits readers in a variety of circumstances to identify with the laments.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 107:6

## Psalms 107:7–8 (id: 23806)

God led them like a shepherd (see [23:1](https://ref.ly/Ps23:1)). • Verse 8 is a refrain that is repeated in [107:15](https://ref.ly/Ps107:15), [21](https://ref.ly/Ps107:21), [31](https://ref.ly/Ps107:31).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 107:7–PSA 107:8

## Psalms 107:10–16 (id: 23787)

The psalmist calls for thanksgiving and praise from people in despair over the consequences of their rebellion.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 107:10–PSA 107:16

## Psalms 107:11 (id: 23788)

God’s counsel includes his instruction and will.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 107:11

## Psalms 107:12 (id: 23789)

Exhausted by their hard labor ([Lam 5:13](https://ref.ly/Lam5:13)), the people fell. While this might be expected of the wicked ([Pss 9:3](https://ref.ly/Ps9:3); [27:2](https://ref.ly/Ps27:2)), it was unlike the Israelites’ flight from Egypt ([105:37](https://ref.ly/Ps105:37)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 107:12

## Psalms 107:17–22 (id: 23790)

Fools who received what they deserved but were rescued from death offer thanksgiving to the Lord.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 107:17–PSA 107:22

## Psalms 107:20 (id: 23791)

The Lord creates ([Gen 1:3](https://ref.ly/Gen1:3)) and sustains the universe ([Heb 1:3](https://ref.ly/Heb1:3)) simply by speaking ([Ps 147:18](https://ref.ly/Ps147:18)); when he speaks, people are also healed ([Matt 8:8](https://ref.ly/Matt8:8)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 107:20

## Psalms 107:23–32 (id: 23792)

Sailors give thanks to the Lord when he saves them from the chaos and peril of the sea.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 107:23–PSA 107:32

## Psalms 107:25–29 (id: 23793)

The same God who speaks and brings about the sailors’ distress can also calm the storm with just a word (cp. [Jon 1:4](https://ref.ly/Jonah1:4); [Matt 8:26](https://ref.ly/Matt8:26)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 107:25–PSA 107:29

## Psalms 107:32 (id: 23795)

This call for public praise expands the refrains in [107:21–22](https://ref.ly/Ps107:21-Ps107:22) and [107:31](https://ref.ly/Ps107:31).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 107:32

## Psalms 107:33–35 (id: 23796)

The Lord can choose to make the earth fertile or barren ([74:15](https://ref.ly/Ps74:15); [Isa 35:6–7](https://ref.ly/Isa35:6-Isa35:7)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 107:33–PSA 107:35

## Psalms 107:33–42 (id: 23797)

These two sections ([107:33–38](https://ref.ly/Ps107:33-Ps107:38), [39–42](https://ref.ly/Ps107:39-Ps107:42)) expand the theme of the Lord’s sovereignty over things that humans cannot control.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 107:33–PSA 107:42

## Psalms 107:38 (id: 23798)

God’s presence can be seen in the abundance of his people’s families and herds ([127:3](https://ref.ly/Ps127:3); [133:3](https://ref.ly/Ps133:3); cp. [109:8](https://ref.ly/Ps109:8)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 107:38

## Psalms 107:39 (id: 23799)

People often become impoverished when their rulers practice oppression.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 107:39

## Psalms 107:40 (id: 23802)

In his contempt for human rulers, the Lord rectifies their corruption on earth.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 107:40

## Psalms 107:41 (id: 23803)

The large families of the poor are evidence of God’s blessing.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 107:41

## Psalms 107:42–43 (id: 23804)

Justice prevails in God’s world ([1:6](https://ref.ly/Ps1:6)), and Israel’s history demonstrates God’s faithful love.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 107:42–PSA 107:43

## Psalms 108:1–13 (id: 23807)

This psalm combines two excerpts from David’s other psalms (cp. [57:5](https://ref.ly/Ps57:5), [7–11](https://ref.ly/Ps57:7-Ps57:11); [60:5–12](https://ref.ly/Ps60:5-Ps60:12)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 108:1–PSA 108:13

## Psalms 109:1 (id: 23813)

The psalmist sees no evidence that God cares (see [28:1](https://ref.ly/Ps28:1)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 109:1

## Psalms 109:1–31 (id: 23808)

The psalmist begins this lament with a general charge against his accusers: They do evil in return for good ([109:1–5](https://ref.ly/Ps109:1-Ps109:5)). At the end of the psalm, he turns to the Lord in prayer, asking for his protection ([109:21–25](https://ref.ly/Ps109:21-Ps109:25)) and vengeance ([109:26–31](https://ref.ly/Ps109:26-Ps109:31)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 109:1–PSA 109:31

## Psalms 109:4–5 (id: 23821)

The psalmist’s acts of kindness and godliness (see [35:12–14](https://ref.ly/Ps35:12-Ps35:14)) have only met with stubborn opposition and expressions of hatred.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 109:4–PSA 109:5

## Psalms 109:6–19 (id: 23822)

The NLT translates these verses as the words of the psalmist’s accusers; Hebrew lacks They say*,* which makes it unclear who is speaking.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 109:6–PSA 109:19

## Psalms 109:8 (id: 23824)

The wicked person apparently held a position of leadership. Peter referred to this psalm in regard to Judas Iscariot ([Acts 1:20–26](https://ref.ly/Acts1:20-Acts1:26)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 109:8

## Psalms 109:8–11 (id: 23823)

Family members of those guilty of capital crimes often died with the perpetrator ([Num 16:1–33](https://ref.ly/Num16:1-Num16:33); [Josh 7:1–25](https://ref.ly/Josh7:1-Josh7:25)) or had their property confiscated ([1 Kgs 21:13–16](https://ref.ly/1Kgs21:13-1Kgs21:16)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 109:8–PSA 109:11

## Psalms 109:13 (id: 23809)

If one’s family name was blotted out*,* it meant there was no offspring to carry on the family name or remember its history (see [Prov 10:7](https://ref.ly/Prov10:7)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 109:13

## Psalms 109:14 (id: 23810)

Children inherit the sinful nature of their parents ([51:5](https://ref.ly/Ps51:5); [Exod 20:5](https://ref.ly/Exod20:5); [Eph 2:3](https://ref.ly/Eph2:3)). The speaker wants the Lord to punish the perpetrator for the guilt of family members who went before him (cp. [Matt 23:35–36](https://ref.ly/Matt23:35-Matt23:36)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 109:14

## Psalms 109:16 (id: 23811)

The defendant committed capital crimes and did not exercise even basic decency.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 109:16

## Psalms 109:18 (id: 23812)

Cursing is the accused person’s whole way of life.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 109:18

## Psalms 109:20 (id: 23814)

The psalmist appeals to the principle of retribution (see [94:23](https://ref.ly/Ps94:23)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 109:20

## Psalms 109:21 (id: 23816)

The Lord’s reputation is at stake. If the wicked triumph, others could think that the Lord is also wicked and be drawn to that wickedness ([1:1](https://ref.ly/Ps1:1)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 109:21

## Psalms 109:21–25 (id: 23815)

Vulnerable and miserable, the psalmist appeals to his Lord for help. The accusations have killed his inner spirit and even his physical stamina.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 109:21–PSA 109:25

## Psalms 109:23 (id: 23817)

A shadow at dusk suggests a transitory, empty existence ([102:11](https://ref.ly/Ps102:11); [144:4](https://ref.ly/Ps144:4)); a single locust could easily be brushed off one’s clothing.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 109:23

## Psalms 109:26–31 (id: 23818)

These verses form a prayer for God’s presence and for vindication. The psalmist wants everyone to see that he is vindicated by the Lord, not by any human agent.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 109:26–PSA 109:31

## Psalms 109:28 (id: 23819)

The Lord’s servant demonstrates loyalty and obedience.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 109:28

## Psalms 109:29 (id: 23820)

The psalmist had been accused of being clothed with curses ([109:18](https://ref.ly/Ps109:18)); now he asks that his accusers be clothed with disgrace and humiliation.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 109:29

## Psalms 110:1 (id: 23835)

The king of Israel had the great privilege of being the Lord’s adopted son ([Ps 2](https://ref.ly/Ps2:1-Ps2:12); [1 Chr 22:10](https://ref.ly/1Chr22:10)), but he fell ([Ps 89](https://ref.ly/Ps89:1-Ps89:52)). This decree restores and heightens his position. • The Lord: Hebrew *Yahweh,* the name of God (see [Exod 3:6–14](https://ref.ly/Exod3:6-Exod3:14); [6:2–8](https://ref.ly/Exod6:2-Exod6:8); [20:2](https://ref.ly/Exod20:2)). • my Lord (Hebrew ’adoni) means “my master” or “my superior.” The psalmist viewed God’s messianic ruler as his superior. The New Testament frequently cites this psalm to validate Jesus’ claim to be the Messiah ([Matt 22:44–45](https://ref.ly/Matt22:44-Matt22:45); [Mark 12:36–37](https://ref.ly/Mark12:36-Mark12:37); [Luke 20:42–44](https://ref.ly/Luke20:42-Luke20:44); [Acts 2:34–35](https://ref.ly/Acts2:34-Acts2:35); [Heb 1:13](https://ref.ly/Heb1:13)). • The Lord’s right hand represents his authority, strength, presence, and benefits. The Lord chose the descendant of David and raised him up to be close to him ([Ps 80:17](https://ref.ly/Ps80:17)). Jesus claimed this position for himself ([Matt 26:64](https://ref.ly/Matt26:64); [Mark 14:62](https://ref.ly/Mark14:62); [16:19](https://ref.ly/Mark16:19); [Luke 22:69](https://ref.ly/Luke22:69)), and the apostles announced that Jesus, having ascended to heaven, sits at the right hand of the Father ([Acts 2:33](https://ref.ly/Acts2:33); [5:31](https://ref.ly/Acts5:31); [7:55–56](https://ref.ly/Acts7:55-Acts7:56); [Rom 8:34](https://ref.ly/Rom8:34); [Eph 1:20](https://ref.ly/Eph1:20); [Col 3:1](https://ref.ly/Col3:1); [Heb 1:3](https://ref.ly/Heb1:3); [8:1](https://ref.ly/Heb8:1); [10:12](https://ref.ly/Heb10:12); [12:2](https://ref.ly/Heb12:2)). • Ancient Near Eastern kings were sometimes portrayed as placing their feet on the backs of their conquered enemies as on a footstool (see [Heb 10:12–13](https://ref.ly/Heb10:12-Heb10:13)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 110:1

## Psalms 110:1–7 (id: 23834)

Jesus and the apostles cite this psalm to explain Jesus’ unique ministry and status as the Messiah ([Matt 22:43–45](https://ref.ly/Matt22:43-Matt22:45); [Acts 2:32–36](https://ref.ly/Acts2:32-Acts2:36)). It reaffirms God’s covenant with David and gives hope for the future (see [2 Sam 7:8–16](https://ref.ly/2Sam7:8-2Sam7:16)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 110:1–PSA 110:7

## Psalms 110:2–3 (id: 23836)

The kingdom will expand and increase, beginning from Jerusalem, until all enemies are conquered.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 110:2–PSA 110:3

## Psalms 110:4 (id: 23837)

The Lord had made an unbreakable oath and covenant, so his apparent rejection of David’s dynasty ([89:38](https://ref.ly/Ps89:38)) in the Exile had led to a crisis. The placement of [Ps 110](https://ref.ly/Ps110:1-Ps110:7) in Book Five reaffirms the future of the dynasty: David’s descendant must conform to God’s standard of integrity ([Ps 101](https://ref.ly/Ps101:1-Ps101:8)). His ministry will be transformed as he serves under God’s kingship ([Pss 93–100](https://ref.ly/Ps93:1-Ps100:5)). • You are a priest forever: The role of God’s messianic ruler changes. The priestly kingship of David and his descendants extended to serving as patrons of the Temple. David had the Ark brought to Jerusalem ([2 Sam 6:15](https://ref.ly/2Sam6:15)) and arranged for the Temple service ([1 Chr 6:31–48](https://ref.ly/1Chr6:31-1Chr6:48); [15:11–26](https://ref.ly/1Chr15:11-1Chr15:26); [16:4–42](https://ref.ly/1Chr16:4-1Chr16:42); [23:4–32](https://ref.ly/1Chr23:4-1Chr23:32); [25:1](https://ref.ly/1Chr25:1)). Solomon supervised the Temple construction ([1 Kgs 5:1–7:51](https://ref.ly/1Kgs5:1-1Kgs7:51)). Even so, Israel’s kingship was separate from its priesthood. In the messianic kingdom, the king would also minister as priest, as Melchizedek*,* king of Salem ([Gen 14:18](https://ref.ly/Gen14:18)), had done. The New Testament develops the ministry of Jesus Christ as a fulfillment of this new order (see [Heb 5:6–10](https://ref.ly/Heb5:6-Heb5:10); [6:20–7:25](https://ref.ly/Heb6:20-Heb7:25)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 110:4

## Psalms 110:5–6 (id: 23838)

at your right hand: This position brings help and protection (see [16:7–8](https://ref.ly/Ps16:7-Ps16:8); [108:13](https://ref.ly/Ps108:13)). • The Lord will strike down rebellious kings. Rebellion against the Lord is a capital offense ([Ps 2](https://ref.ly/Ps2:1-Ps2:12); [Rom 6:23](https://ref.ly/Rom6:23)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 110:5–PSA 110:6

## Psalms 110:5–7 (id: 23839)

The new priestly role of David’s descendant does not rescind his old role as conquering ruler. He must still bring the nations under his rule ([110:2–3](https://ref.ly/Ps110:2-Ps110:3); see [Ps 2](https://ref.ly/Ps2:1-Ps2:12)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 110:5–PSA 110:7

## Psalms 110:7 (id: 23840)

God’s messianic ruler obtains victory as a vigorous person, as if he had received nourishment from brooks along the way ([110:3](https://ref.ly/Ps110:3)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 110:7

## Psalms 111:1–5 (id: 23843)

The godly praise God and delight themselves in his great works. His mighty acts reflect his righteousness, grace, and compassion (see [116:5–7](https://ref.ly/Ps116:5-Ps116:7)). All who submit themselves to him experience his glory.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 111:1–PSA 111:5

## Psalms 111:1–10 (id: 23841)

This wisdom psalm contains many references to the works of the Lord that reveal his character. God is righteous, gracious, compassionate, faithful, just, trustworthy, upright, holy, and awe\-inspiring ([111:3](https://ref.ly/Ps111:3), [4](https://ref.ly/Ps111:4), [7](https://ref.ly/Ps111:7), [8](https://ref.ly/Ps111:8), [9](https://ref.ly/Ps111:9)). God’s character gives hope in the covenant relationship ([111:5](https://ref.ly/Ps111:5)). He rescued Israel from Egypt ([111:9](https://ref.ly/Ps111:9)), gave them the land ([111:6](https://ref.ly/Ps111:6)), and provides for his people ([111:5](https://ref.ly/Ps111:5)). However, God demands that the beneficiaries of this relationship also be people of righteousness and integrity.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 111:1–PSA 111:10

## Psalms 111:1–117.2 (id: 23842)

The refrain Praise the Lord! (Hebrew haleluyah) characterizes this group of psalms.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 111:1–PSA 117:2

## Psalms 111:5 (id: 23845)

God takes care of his people’s needs, even providing food. He remembers his covenant with Abraham (see [105:8–11](https://ref.ly/Ps105:8-Ps105:11)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 111:5

## Psalms 111:6–8 (id: 23846)

Giving Israel the lands of other nations was just and good because the Lord was executing his justice on those he dispossessed and showing grace to the Israelites. However, if the Israelites do not live faithfully and with integrity*,* they will also be dispossessed. The Lord’s people must reflect his character.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 111:6–PSA 111:8

## Psalms 111:9 (id: 23847)

The people of the Exodus generation went free because of God’s grace.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 111:9

## Psalms 111:10 (id: 23844)

True wisdom is the source of life ([Prov 3:18](https://ref.ly/Prov3:18); [9:11](https://ref.ly/Prov9:11); [Eccl 7:12](https://ref.ly/Eccl7:12)); it begins with the fear of the Lord ([Prov 9:10](https://ref.ly/Prov9:10)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 111:10

## Psalms 112:1–5 (id: 23849)

The fear of the Lord leads to a life of wisdom that honors God and blesses the family and community. The godly joyfully imitate God; their obedience is not slavish.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 112:1–PSA 112:5

## Psalms 112:1–10 (id: 23848)

This psalm reiterates the themes of wisdom and the fear of the Lord ([Ps 111](https://ref.ly/Ps111:1-Ps111:10)). The wise have reason to be happy ([112:1–5](https://ref.ly/Ps112:1-Ps112:5)) and vigorous ([112:6–10](https://ref.ly/Ps112:6-Ps112:10)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 112:1–PSA 112:10

## Psalms 112:2–3 (id: 23851)

successful: All will know the children of godly people (see [127:4](https://ref.ly/Ps127:4)) because the godly leave a legacy for their children (see [1:3](https://ref.ly/Ps1:3); cp. [Matt 6:20](https://ref.ly/Matt6:20)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 112:2–PSA 112:3

## Psalms 112:4–5 (id: 23852)

The godly imitate God by being generous, compassionate, and righteous ([51:1](https://ref.ly/Ps51:1); [111:1–10](https://ref.ly/Ps111:1-Ps111:10); [2 Cor 9:9](https://ref.ly/2Cor9:9)). They lend money to the poor without charging interest ([Pss 15:5](https://ref.ly/Ps15:5); [112:9](https://ref.ly/Ps112:9); [Exod 22:25](https://ref.ly/Exod22:25)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 112:4–PSA 112:5

## Psalms 112:6 (id: 23853)

The honesty and compassion of the wise keeps them from stumbling ([15:5](https://ref.ly/Ps15:5); [37:23–24](https://ref.ly/Ps37:23-Ps37:24)), ensuring that they will be long remembered ([Prov 10:7](https://ref.ly/Prov10:7)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 112:6

## Psalms 112:8 (id: 23854)

Because the godly joyfully expect God to prevail and rescue them, they face their foes triumphantly ([59:10](https://ref.ly/Ps59:10); [112:4](https://ref.ly/Ps112:4); [118:7](https://ref.ly/Ps118:7)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 112:8

## Psalms 112:9 (id: 23855)

Paul quotes this verse in his instructions about generous giving ([2 Cor 9:9](https://ref.ly/2Cor9:9)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 112:9

## Psalms 112:10 (id: 23850)

The wicked . . . grind their teeth in anger out of their bitter envy ([35:16](https://ref.ly/Ps35:16); [37:12](https://ref.ly/Ps37:12)). The vigor and reputation of the godly cause conflict with those who want them dead. • The wicked will slink away out of fear and shame.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 112:10

## Psalms 113:1–3 (id: 23857)

The name of the Lord (Hebrew *Yahweh;* see [Exod 3:15](https://ref.ly/Exod3:15)) reveals his being, character, and reputation. He is exalted in time (now and forever) and in space (from east to west).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 113:1–PSA 113:3

## Psalms 113:1–9 (id: 23858)

This hymn of praise exalts the greatness of the Lord’s name and glory. God is greatly exalted and glorious in heaven ([113:4](https://ref.ly/Ps113:4)); he also stoops down to take care of the lowly and needy on earth ([113:5–9](https://ref.ly/Ps113:5-Ps113:9)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 113:1–PSA 113:9

## Psalms 113:1–118.29 (id: 23856)

These psalms form what is known as the “Egyptian Hallel” (*hallel* means “praise”) because Jews use the collection in the celebration of Passover, which was instituted at the beginning of the exodus from Egypt. [Psalms 113–114](https://ref.ly/Ps113:1-Ps114:8) are recited before the Passover meal and [Pss 115–118](https://ref.ly/Ps115:1-Ps118:29) afterward.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 113:1–PSA 118:29

## Psalms 113:4 (id: 23859)

The Lord’s glory reaches to the heavens ([57:5](https://ref.ly/Ps57:5), [11](https://ref.ly/Ps57:11); [99:2](https://ref.ly/Ps99:2); [108:5](https://ref.ly/Ps108:5); [138:6](https://ref.ly/Ps138:6); [Isa 6:1](https://ref.ly/Isa6:1); [57:15](https://ref.ly/Isa57:15)) and throughout the world of human relationships.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 113:4

## Psalms 113:5–9 (id: 23860)

The incomparable Lord intimately involves himself in caring for people on earth.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 113:5–PSA 113:9

## Psalms 113:6 (id: 23861)

The Lord stoops to the world’s level to be directly involved with his people (see [138:6](https://ref.ly/Ps138:6); [Phil 2:6–8](https://ref.ly/Phil2:6-Phil2:8)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 113:6

## Psalms 113:7–8 (id: 23862)

These phrases are a quotation from Hannah’s prayer of praise ([1 Sam 2:8–9a](https://ref.ly/1Sam2:8-1Sam2:9)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 113:7–PSA 113:8

## Psalms 113:9 (id: 23863)

A childless woman was customarily treated with disdain ([Gen 16:4](https://ref.ly/Gen16:4)); the Lord has the power to make her a happy mother*,* as he made Sarah ([Gen 21:2](https://ref.ly/Gen21:2)), Rebekah ([Gen 25:21](https://ref.ly/Gen25:21)), Rachel ([Gen 30:23](https://ref.ly/Gen30:23)), and Hannah ([1 Sam 1:20](https://ref.ly/1Sam1:20)). • God’s greatness and goodness provide ample reason to praise him.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 113:9

## Psalms 114:1–2 (id: 23864)

At the time of Israel’s exodus from Egypt and their entrance into the Promised Land, Israel was one holy kingdom ([Exod 19:5–6](https://ref.ly/Exod19:5-Exod19:6)). • The separate references to the land of Judah and Israel indicate that the psalm was composed after the kingdom was divided ([1 Kgs 12:16–17](https://ref.ly/1Kgs12:16-1Kgs12:17); cp. [1 Sam 11:8](https://ref.ly/1Sam11:8); [1 Kgs 1:35](https://ref.ly/1Kgs1:35)), and probably after the Exile. The land of Judah became God’s sanctuary because the people worshiped God; his Tabernacle and later his Temple were located there.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 114:1–PSA 114:2

## Psalms 114:1–8 (id: 23865)

This lyrical celebration of the Lord’s power in nature recalls Israel’s beginning as a nation at the Exodus ([114:1–2](https://ref.ly/Ps114:1-Ps114:2)) and upon their entry to the Promised Land ([114:3–6](https://ref.ly/Ps114:3-Ps114:6)). It promotes reverence for the God of Jacob ([114:7–8](https://ref.ly/Ps114:7-Ps114:8)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 114:1–PSA 114:8

## Psalms 114:3–4 (id: 23866)

hurried out of their way! The waters divided for Israel to escape Egypt ([77:17–18](https://ref.ly/Ps77:17-Ps77:18); [Exod 14](https://ref.ly/Exod14:1-Exod14:31)). • The Jordan River turned away when Israel arrived to cross over (see [Josh 3](https://ref.ly/Josh3:1-Josh3:17)). • skipped like rams: God’s presence caused the mountains to quake ([Exod 19:16–20](https://ref.ly/Exod19:16-Exod19:20)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 114:3–PSA 114:4

## Psalms 114:8 (id: 23867)

The Lord miraculously provided for his people in hard times after the Exile, just as he had done in the wilderness after the Exodus.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 114:8

## Psalms 115:1–3 (id: 23869)

The community confesses their faith that God will rescue them for the glory of his name.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 115:1–PSA 115:3

## Psalms 115:1–18 (id: 23868)

In this hymn of thanksgiving for God’s blessings, the community ascribes all glory to the name of the Lord, who is the true source of hope and blessing. Meanwhile, those who trust in idols are greatly disappointed. The blessing of the Creator of heaven and earth extends to future generations ([115:14](https://ref.ly/Ps115:14)), and especially to the priesthood ([115:12](https://ref.ly/Ps115:12)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 115:1–PSA 115:18

## Psalms 115:2–3 (id: 23873)

Where is their God? People deny God’s presence or power when he does not act as they think he should (cp. [14:1](https://ref.ly/Ps14:1); [42:3](https://ref.ly/Ps42:3), [10](https://ref.ly/Ps42:10)). However, God is in the heavens—he has all power, authority, and knowledge. He does as he wishes*,* not what people think he should do. He works out his plans in accord with his will ([Eph 1:11](https://ref.ly/Eph1:11)) and acts in his own time and in ways he chooses.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 115:2–PSA 115:3

## Psalms 115:4–11 (id: 23874)

This entire section is repeated in [135:15–20](https://ref.ly/Ps135:15-Ps135:20). • Unlike the Lord ([95:3–5](https://ref.ly/Ps95:3-Ps95:5)), idols cannot do anything; they are good for nothing.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 115:4–PSA 115:11

## Psalms 115:8 (id: 23875)

Worshiping idols leads one astray and corrupts those who trust in them ([Isa 44:20](https://ref.ly/Isa44:20)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 115:8

## Psalms 115:9–11 (id: 23876)

Israel . . . priests . . . you who fear the Lord: The psalmist calls on all those in the God\-fearing community to commit their ways to the living God. The threefold address assures them that the Lord is their true helper and shield (cp. [118:2–4](https://ref.ly/Ps118:2-Ps118:4)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 115:9–PSA 115:11

## Psalms 115:12–13 (id: 23870)

The groups named in [115:9–11](https://ref.ly/Ps115:9-Ps115:11) receive assurance of the Lord’s blessing, regardless of their social status (see [113:8](https://ref.ly/Ps113:8)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 115:12–PSA 115:13

## Psalms 115:14–15 (id: 23871)

The psalmist blesses ([107:37–38](https://ref.ly/Ps107:37-Ps107:38), [41](https://ref.ly/Ps107:41)) all who trust in and fear the Lord. The Creator will care for the families of those who fear him. • who made heaven and earth: This statement speaks of the Lord’s all\-encompassing power in creation.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 115:14–PSA 115:15

## Psalms 115:16–18 (id: 23872)

The heavens belong to the Lord:’s: God’s exaltation begins in heaven ([113:4](https://ref.ly/Ps113:4)), far above the gods of the nations. Of course, the earth also belongs to him ([47:9](https://ref.ly/Ps47:9); [95:4](https://ref.ly/Ps95:4)). • The dead cannot participate in God’s blessings. The living praise God in thanksgiving for his blessings ([79:13](https://ref.ly/Ps79:13)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 115:16–PSA 115:18

## Psalms 116:1 (id: 23882)

I love the Lord: This unique opening expresses affection for and commitment to the Lord (see [18:1](https://ref.ly/Ps18:1); [Deut 6:5](https://ref.ly/Deut6:5)) on the basis of what the Lord has done.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 116:1

## Psalms 116:1–4 (id: 23878)

The psalmist praises the Lord for answering his prayers and rescuing him from death.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 116:1–PSA 116:4

## Psalms 116:1–19 (id: 23877)

This hymn of thanksgiving rejoices in God’s character and in rescue from death ([116:1–11](https://ref.ly/Ps116:1-Ps116:11)). It gives an assurance of God’s protection in life and reminds the godly that the Lord watches over them even at death. The psalmist commits to living as God’s servant and resolves to honor him publicly ([116:12–19](https://ref.ly/Ps116:12-Ps116:19)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 116:1–PSA 116:19

## Psalms 116:2 (id: 23883)

Because the Lord responds to the cry of his people ([107:41](https://ref.ly/Ps107:41); [113:6–8](https://ref.ly/Ps113:6-Ps113:8)), the psalmist now strongly believes in prayer.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 116:2

## Psalms 116:3 (id: 23884)

It isn’t clear if the psalmist’s crisis was a literal near\-death experience or if he was using the term figuratively.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 116:3

## Psalms 116:4 (id: 23885)

This is the first of three times that the psalmist calls on the Lord’s name (i.e., reputation).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 116:4

## Psalms 116:5–7 (id: 23886)

The gracious, righteous, and compassionate Lord (see [111:1–5](https://ref.ly/Ps111:1-Ps111:5)) rescued and gave rest to the psalmist.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 116:5–PSA 116:7

## Psalms 116:6 (id: 23887)

People with childlike faith readily receive his wisdom and instruction ([19:7–11](https://ref.ly/Ps19:7-Ps19:11); [Matt 18:3–4](https://ref.ly/Matt18:3-Matt18:4)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 116:6

## Psalms 116:8–11 (id: 23888)

The psalmist’s near\-death crisis made him more aware of life and of walking before the Lord. Though he had been in anguish, the Lord was faithful. However, people are all liars.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 116:8–PSA 116:11

## Psalms 116:9 (id: 23889)

I walk in the Lord’s presence: The psalmist already lived with integrity, but since his experience of deep distress, he now enjoys open fellowship with the Lord (see [56:13](https://ref.ly/Ps56:13); cp. [Job 42:5](https://ref.ly/Job42:5)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 116:9

## Psalms 116:10 (id: 23879)

I believed in you: Paul quotes this phrase in [2 Cor 4:13](https://ref.ly/2Cor4:13).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 116:10

## Psalms 116:12–14 (id: 23880)

The Lord’s gracious gifts are so great that the psalmist can do nothing to repay his debt. Keeping his promises publicly demonstrates his gratitude. • All he has done for the psalmist includes answers to prayer, rescue, and life. • The cup of salvation overflows with God’s blessings ([23:5](https://ref.ly/Ps23:5)), unlike the cup of judgment ([75:8](https://ref.ly/Ps75:8)). • The psalmist makes promises (“vows,” [116:18](https://ref.ly/Ps116:18)) to praise the Lord publicly ([116:17–18](https://ref.ly/Ps116:17-Ps116:18)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 116:12–PSA 116:14

## Psalms 116:15–19 (id: 23881)

No one lives or dies outside of God’s will. Having been given a second chance at life, the poet readily commits himself to the Lord with renewed acts of public devotion.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 116:15–PSA 116:19

## Psalms 117:1 (id: 23891)

Paul quotes this verse to show that Gentiles would eventually praise the God of Israel ([Rom 15:11](https://ref.ly/Rom15:11)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 117:1

## Psalms 117:1–2 (id: 23890)

This psalm, the shortest in the Psalter, invites all . . . people of the earth to praise the Lord because of his unfailing love and enduring faithfulness.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 117:1–PSA 117:2

## Psalms 118:1–29 (id: 23892)

With an exultant testimony, the psalmist gives thanks for the Lord’s goodness and encourages others to trust in his faithful love ([118:1–4](https://ref.ly/Ps118:1-Ps118:4), [29](https://ref.ly/Ps118:29)). This poem is the last of the Egyptian Hallel ([Pss 113–118](https://ref.ly/Ps113:1-Ps118:29)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 118:1–PSA 118:29

## Psalms 118:2–4 (id: 23896)

Israel . . . Aaron’s descendants . . . all who fear the Lord: These three groups represent the whole of the covenant community (cp. [115:9–11](https://ref.ly/Ps115:9-Ps115:11); [135:19–20](https://ref.ly/Ps135:19-Ps135:20)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 118:2–PSA 118:4

## Psalms 118:5–9 (id: 23902)

The Lord alone is the psalmist’s helper.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 118:5–PSA 118:9

## Psalms 118:6–7 (id: 23903)

The Lord is for me: Cp. [Rom 8:31](https://ref.ly/Rom8:31); [Heb 13:6](https://ref.ly/Heb13:6). • God’s presence cancels out the need to fear mere people ([Ps 56:11](https://ref.ly/Ps56:11)). The psalmist joyfully expects God’s rescue ([59:10](https://ref.ly/Ps59:10); [112:8](https://ref.ly/Ps112:8)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 118:6–PSA 118:7

## Psalms 118:8–9 (id: 23904)

Trusting in the Lord is better than placing confidence in even the most powerful human leaders ([118:6](https://ref.ly/Ps118:6); [146:3](https://ref.ly/Ps146:3)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 118:8–PSA 118:9

## Psalms 118:10–12 (id: 23893)

Strength comes in the name of the Lord, declared by the threefold mention of the attackers, the Lord’s name, and victory. • Even when hostile people blazed . . . like a crackling fire*,* the Lord caused them to subside like burning thorns (see [Isa 9:18](https://ref.ly/Isa9:18); [10:17](https://ref.ly/Isa10:17)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 118:10–PSA 118:12

## Psalms 118:14–18 (id: 23894)

The psalmist celebrates the victory of the Lord’s strong right arm*,* which kept him from death.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 118:14–PSA 118:18

## Psalms 118:17–21 (id: 23895)

God has restored the psalmist from death to life, so he praises the Lord publicly (cp. [116:6](https://ref.ly/Ps116:6), [12–19](https://ref.ly/Ps116:12-Ps116:19)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 118:17–PSA 118:21

## Psalms 118:22 (id: 23898)

The cornerstone (or *keystone*) of a building or an arch gives the structure its shape and foundation. It is the most important of all the stones. The Lord chooses and places this stone for his sanctuary ([Isa 28:16](https://ref.ly/Isa28:16)). Jesus referred to himself as this cornerstone ([Matt 21:42](https://ref.ly/Matt21:42); [Mark 12:10–11](https://ref.ly/Mark12:10-Mark12:11); [Luke 20:17](https://ref.ly/Luke20:17); see [Acts 4:11](https://ref.ly/Acts4:11); [Eph 2:20](https://ref.ly/Eph2:20); [1 Pet 2:6–7](https://ref.ly/1Pet2:6-1Pet2:7)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 118:22

## Psalms 118:22–24 (id: 23897)

The psalmist sees his own salvation as the beginning of a new day in which the Lord will do great things.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 118:22–PSA 118:24

## Psalms 118:24 (id: 23899)

This is the day the Lord has made: The day of the Lord’s victory has already arrived, although its completion awaits another day ([118:25](https://ref.ly/Ps118:25)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 118:24

## Psalms 118:25–29 (id: 23900)

The psalmist concludes with prayer and thanksgiving, anticipating an even greater revelation of God’s victory and rescue.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 118:25–PSA 118:29

## Psalms 118:26 (id: 23901)

The one who comes in the name of the Lord brings the Lord’s complete victory (see [118:10–12](https://ref.ly/Ps118:10-Ps118:12)). • During Jesus’ triumphant entry into Jerusalem, the crowds called out various blessings, including phrases taken from this verse ([Matt 21:9](https://ref.ly/Matt21:9); [Mark 11:9](https://ref.ly/Mark11:9); [Luke 19:38](https://ref.ly/Luke19:38); [John 12:13](https://ref.ly/John12:13)). Jesus himself quoted this passage as he wept over Jerusalem ([Matt 23:39](https://ref.ly/Matt23:39); [Luke 13:35](https://ref.ly/Luke13:35)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 118:26

## Psalms 119:1–4 (id: 23906)

The wise are happy. They are people of integrity (see [84:11](https://ref.ly/Ps84:11)) who follow the path of divine instruction. They obey God’s revelation and search for it with all their hearts (see [27:7](https://ref.ly/Ps27:7); [119:10](https://ref.ly/Ps119:10), [45](https://ref.ly/Ps119:45), [94](https://ref.ly/Ps119:94), [155](https://ref.ly/Ps119:155)), and they reject all forms of evil. Cp. [1:1–2](https://ref.ly/Ps1:1-Ps1:2).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:1–PSA 119:4

## Psalms 119:1–8 (id: 23907)

Aleph (א): God, the author of these instructions*,* commands that his followers live by them. The psalmist prays to be given the grace to live by that revelation.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:1–PSA 119:8

## Psalms 119:1–176 (id: 23905)

This psalm combines elements of wisdom, lament, praise, thanksgiving, and confession. Eight Hebrew words are used frequently, translated as “instructions,” “laws,” “words,” “regulations,” “statutes,” “commands,” “decrees,” “commandments,” and “promises.” Together, these words encourage love for and obedience to God’s instructions, as found in the Scriptures (see [2 Tim 3:14–17](https://ref.ly/2Tim3:14-2Tim3:17)). The expression of deep commitment to these instructions unifies the psalm.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:1–PSA 119:176

## Psalms 119:4 (id: 23944)

To keep God’s commandments means to guard them by obeying them.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:4

## Psalms 119:9 (id: 23961)

A young person tends toward foolishness ([Prov 22:15](https://ref.ly/Prov22:15)) and can easily make mistakes that destroy his life ([Prov 7:6–23](https://ref.ly/Prov7:6-Prov7:23)). Youth is also the best time to develop personal discipline and pursue wisdom (see [Ps 34:11](https://ref.ly/Ps34:11); [Prov 1:4](https://ref.ly/Prov1:4)). • To stay pure means to remain uncorrupted by wickedness and sin and to develop the integrity of life defined in [Ps 15](https://ref.ly/Ps15:1-Ps15:5).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:9

## Psalms 119:9–16 (id: 23956)

Beth (ב): The psalmist is determined to pursue purity and encourages the cultivation of wisdom through God’s principles ([119:9](https://ref.ly/Ps119:9)) and instructions ([119:10–16](https://ref.ly/Ps119:10-Ps119:16)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:9–PSA 119:16

## Psalms 119:10 (id: 23912)

The student asks God the teacher to discipline him so that he will not wander.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:10

## Psalms 119:14 (id: 23923)

God’s wisdom is far greater than any riches humans seek ([119:72](https://ref.ly/Ps119:72), [127](https://ref.ly/Ps119:127); [Prov 3:14–15](https://ref.ly/Prov3:14-Prov3:15)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:14

## Psalms 119:15 (id: 23926)

The way of wisdom includes meditating on God’s ways (see [119:1](https://ref.ly/Ps119:1), [3](https://ref.ly/Ps119:3)). The wise reflect on the implications of God’s word.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:15

## Psalms 119:17–18 (id: 23930)

The psalmist seeks to please the Lord with a full and obedient life of praise ([118:17](https://ref.ly/Ps118:17); [119:25](https://ref.ly/Ps119:25), [77](https://ref.ly/Ps119:77), [116](https://ref.ly/Ps119:116), [144](https://ref.ly/Ps119:144), [175](https://ref.ly/Ps119:175)). Only the Lord can remove his adversaries and enable him to see the wonderful truths found in God’s instructions.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:17–PSA 119:18

## Psalms 119:17–24 (id: 23931)

Gimel (ג): Like a foreigner in hostile territory, God’s servant needs God’s guidance.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:17–PSA 119:24

## Psalms 119:20–21 (id: 23933)

The arrogant are probably those who mock the psalmist ([119:22–23](https://ref.ly/Ps119:22-Ps119:23)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:20–PSA 119:21

## Psalms 119:23–24 (id: 23934)

Those who meditate on God’s instructions receive wise advice from them.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:23–PSA 119:24

## Psalms 119:25–32 (id: 23935)

Daleth (ד): Though the poet feels anguish and sorrow, he entreats the Lord to revive him because he wants to obey the Lord. Suffering and death may result from the Lord’s chastening ([118:17–18](https://ref.ly/Ps118:17-Ps118:18); [119:67](https://ref.ly/Ps119:67), [71](https://ref.ly/Ps119:71), [75](https://ref.ly/Ps119:75)), but his instruction revives the weary soul (see [119:12](https://ref.ly/Ps119:12)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:25–PSA 119:32

## Psalms 119:29 (id: 23936)

lying to myself: Self\-deception is a fruit of sinful human nature ([Jer 17:9](https://ref.ly/Jer17:9)); it leads to folly. • Access to God’s word is a privilege, not a right.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:29

## Psalms 119:33–40 (id: 23937)

He (ה): As a student, the poet asks his teacher, God, to renew life and to transform disgrace into righteousness.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:33–PSA 119:40

## Psalms 119:36 (id: 23938)

The love for money can lead to sin (cp. [Exod 18:21](https://ref.ly/Exod18:21); [1 Tim 3:1–5](https://ref.ly/1Tim3:1-1Tim3:5); [6:10](https://ref.ly/1Tim6:10)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:36

## Psalms 119:41–43 (id: 23939)

The psalmist asks to be saved from enemies who speak harshly (see [42:10](https://ref.ly/Ps42:10); [44:16](https://ref.ly/Ps44:16); [89:50–51](https://ref.ly/Ps89:50-Ps89:51); [102:8](https://ref.ly/Ps102:8)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:41–PSA 119:43

## Psalms 119:41–48 (id: 23940)

Waw (ו): The psalmist prays that God’s word would continue to be the source of his love and salvation.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:41–PSA 119:48

## Psalms 119:44–46 (id: 23941)

The psalmist is determined to obey the Lord.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:44–PSA 119:46

## Psalms 119:47–48 (id: 23942)

The psalmist finds delight in God’s word in spite of pain ([119:92](https://ref.ly/Ps119:92), [143](https://ref.ly/Ps119:143)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:47–PSA 119:48

## Psalms 119:49–56 (id: 23943)

Zayin (ז): The psalmist asks God to remember his word as the psalmist also remembers God’s word and his name. Remembrance expresses devotion.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:49–PSA 119:56

## Psalms 119:52 (id: 23945)

The age\-old regulations are the Torah (God’s “instructions” or “law”), a term that refers to the books of Genesis—Deuteronomy.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:52

## Psalms 119:57–64 (id: 23946)

Heth (ח): The psalmist seeks God’s favor and unfailing love. Although surrounded by evildoers, he remains a loyal servant of the Lord.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:57–PSA 119:64

## Psalms 119:61 (id: 23947)

Evil people try to drag him into sin*,* but the psalmist’s memory of God’s word keeps him standing firm (see [119:16](https://ref.ly/Ps119:16)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:61

## Psalms 119:64 (id: 23948)

God’s goodness fills the earth*;* the whole created order provides evidence of his goodness (see [Isa 6:3](https://ref.ly/Isa6:3); [11:9](https://ref.ly/Isa11:9)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:64

## Psalms 119:65–68 (id: 23949)

Good judgment and knowledge come from wisdom ([111:10](https://ref.ly/Ps111:10)). • The psalmist admits that he used to wander off like a stray sheep ([119:176](https://ref.ly/Ps119:176)). • you disciplined me: See [119:25–29](https://ref.ly/Ps119:25-Ps119:29). • You are good and do only good: God’s character is perfect ([97:2](https://ref.ly/Ps97:2); [Jas 1:17](https://ref.ly/Jas1:17); [1 Jn 1:5](https://ref.ly/1John1:5)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:65–PSA 119:68

## Psalms 119:65–72 (id: 23950)

Teth (ט): The psalmist describes himself as a penitent sinner who gratefully accepts the Lord’s discipline.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:65–PSA 119:72

## Psalms 119:73–76 (id: 23951)

As God’s child, the psalmist asks for divine wisdom.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:73–PSA 119:76

## Psalms 119:73–80 (id: 23952)

Yodh (י): In this prayer for comfort and compassion, the psalmist commits himself to his Creator, who has afflicted him. He wants God to pay back his enemies for the wrongs they have done. He also prays to receive the gift of life. He not only prays for himself but also considers the whole community of the godly, asking that God’s answers to prayer would encourage them.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:73–PSA 119:80

## Psalms 119:81–88 (id: 23953)

Kaph (כ): The psalmist is worn out from waiting for the Lord, but his hope is in God’s future rescue.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:81–PSA 119:88

## Psalms 119:85–88 (id: 23954)

God’s word is trustworthy*,* in contrast to the deceptions of the enemies who hunt the psalmist down without cause (see [119:78](https://ref.ly/Ps119:78)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:85–PSA 119:88

## Psalms 119:89–96 (id: 23955)

Lamedh (ל): The stability of God’s wisdom gives understanding. God’s word provides order and a framework for living, even when under pressure from adversaries.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:89–PSA 119:96

## Psalms 119:95 (id: 23957)

The wicked intended to kill the psalmist, but destruction ([1:6](https://ref.ly/Ps1:6)) was their own fate.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:95

## Psalms 119:96 (id: 23958)

Even perfection has its limits: Humans cannot fully understand God’s ways (see [Eccl 3:11](https://ref.ly/Eccl3:11)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:96

## Psalms 119:97–102 (id: 23959)

make me wiser: God’s word provides wisdom and perspective. God is the true source of wisdom.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:97–PSA 119:102

## Psalms 119:97–104 (id: 23960)

Mem (מ): The instruction and wisdom of God through his word are far superior to the best that human teachers can offer.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:97–PSA 119:104

## Psalms 119:103–104 (id: 23908)

Wisdom is preferable to even the finest food ([19:10](https://ref.ly/Ps19:10); [81:16](https://ref.ly/Ps81:16)). • The psalmist had already rejected the delusion offered by the way of folly (see [119:18](https://ref.ly/Ps119:18), [78](https://ref.ly/Ps119:78), [86](https://ref.ly/Ps119:86), [163](https://ref.ly/Ps119:163)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:103–PSA 119:104

## Psalms 119:105–106 (id: 23909)

The Lord’s word is a lamp that provides perspective, hope, and guidance in darkness ([18:25–29](https://ref.ly/Ps18:25-Ps18:29); [119:130](https://ref.ly/Ps119:130)). Even more, this light gives life ([Prov 6:23](https://ref.ly/Prov6:23)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:105–PSA 119:106

## Psalms 119:105–112 (id: 23910)

Nun (נ): The psalmist’s devotion to God’s word comes from within his being ([119:112](https://ref.ly/Ps119:112)) and guides his external life.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:105–PSA 119:112

## Psalms 119:108–112 (id: 23911)

offering of praise: This Hebrew expression is unique in the Old Testament (cp. [50:23](https://ref.ly/Ps50:23)). • The psalmist is vulnerable to his opponents because of his commitment to a wise life.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:108–PSA 119:112

## Psalms 119:113 (id: 23914)

The godly hate the wicked and their deeds ([5:4–6](https://ref.ly/Ps5:4-Ps5:6); cp. [Ezek 33:11](https://ref.ly/Ezek33:11)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:113

## Psalms 119:113–120 (id: 23913)

Samekh (ס): The psalmist declares his hatred of evil and his love for God and his ways.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:113–PSA 119:120

## Psalms 119:121–128 (id: 23915)

Ayin (ע): The servant of the Lord strains to endure the evil around him. He boldly petitions the Lord to rescue him immediately!

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:121–PSA 119:128

## Psalms 119:125 (id: 23916)

Simply possessing God’s law does not provide any benefits. The psalmist knows that only as the Lord gives discernment will he understand it.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:125

## Psalms 119:129–136 (id: 23917)

Pe (פ): The psalmist prays earnestly for God to speak to him as he suffers from his adversities.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:129–PSA 119:136

## Psalms 119:137–144 (id: 23918)

Tsadhe (צ): God is righteous, and his word is right and just, especially in contrast to the deceptions of the wicked.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:137–PSA 119:144

## Psalms 119:139 (id: 23919)

The psalmist’s indignation (cp. [69:9](https://ref.ly/Ps69:9)) comes from seeing the wicked disregard God’s word.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:139

## Psalms 119:141 (id: 23920)

The psalmist is greatly troubled by his oppressors (see [119:143](https://ref.ly/Ps119:143); cp. [Isa 53](https://ref.ly/Isa53:1-Isa53:12)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:141

## Psalms 119:145–148 (id: 23921)

*I rise* and *anticipate* translate the same Hebrew verb.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:145–PSA 119:148

## Psalms 119:145–152 (id: 23922)

Qoph (ק): The psalmist prays to the Lord at night. Even when God seems distant, he is actually close.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:145–PSA 119:152

## Psalms 119:150–151 (id: 23924)

*Coming to attack me* (or *draw near*) is a Hebrew wordplay on *You are near*. The wicked stay far from God's instructions, but the psalmist stays close, so he does not need to fear.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:150–PSA 119:151

## Psalms 119:153–160 (id: 23925)

Resh (ר): This request for life appears throughout [Psalm 119](https://ref.ly/Ps119:1-Ps119:176), but it is focused in this stanza.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:153–PSA 119:160

## Psalms 119:161–164 (id: 23927)

my heart trembles . . . I rejoice: Fear, trembling, and joy mark the psalmist’s devotion to God. • God’s word is a treasure. • In the Old Testament, seven signifies wholeness.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:161–PSA 119:164

## Psalms 119:161–168 (id: 23928)

Shin (ש): The psalmist looks beyond his adversaries to the peace of God. This perspective allows him to praise God throughout the day.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:161–PSA 119:168

## Psalms 119:169–176 (id: 23929)

Taw (ת): God’s servant petitions the Lord one final time; he still feels like a lost sheep.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:169–PSA 119:176

## Psalms 119:176 (id: 23932)

God, the Great Shepherd, seeks out his lost sheep ([23:1](https://ref.ly/Ps23:1); [Luke 15:4–6](https://ref.ly/Luke15:4-Luke15:6)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 119:176

## Psalms 120:1–2 (id: 23968)

The psalmist is surrounded by liars*,* so he makes his lament to the Lord*,* the only one who can help him.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 120:1–PSA 120:2

## Psalms 120:1–7 (id: 23969)

This short, individual lament expresses the psalmist’s trust that the Lord will deal with deceptive evildoers. It also laments living as a stranger among hateful liars. The psalmist’s picture of his life in a foreign land might have been a reality as he set out for Jerusalem, or it might depict his feelings and concerns as he begins his pilgrimage. Overwhelmed with injustice, he trusts God and looks forward to arriving in the Lord’s presence.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 120:1–PSA 120:7

## Psalms 120:1–134.3 (id: 23967)

These short, appealing songs were sung during pilgrims’ journeys to Jerusalem for the national festivals three times per year ([Deut 16:16](https://ref.ly/Deut16:16)). The title of these psalms includes the Hebrew word for stairs, which some take to mean “ascending to Jerusalem.” These psalms (sometimes called the Songs of Ascents) take the reader on a pilgrimage to Jerusalem to praise God for his goodness to Israel throughout history.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 120:1–PSA 134:3

## Psalms 120:3–4 (id: 23970)

The psalmist dialogues with the liars who surround him. He feels reassured that the Lord will judge them. • The Divine Warrior (see [7:12–13](https://ref.ly/Ps7:12-Ps7:13); [11:4–6](https://ref.ly/Ps11:4-Ps11:6)) will throw sharp arrows and glowing coals on the liars.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 120:3–PSA 120:4

## Psalms 120:5 (id: 23972)

Meshech was a Japhethite territory far to the north of Canaan. Kedar was an Ishmaelite territory in Arabia. Violent people lived in both locations. Meshech was the home of a famous slave trade ([Ezek 27:13](https://ref.ly/Ezek27:13); cp. [Exod 21:16](https://ref.ly/Exod21:16)) and Kedar of renowned warriors ([Isa 21:16–17](https://ref.ly/Isa21:16-Isa21:17)). These places can be understood as representative of the apostate, violent land where the psalmist suffered.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 120:5

## Psalms 120:5–7 (id: 23971)

The psalmist feels the anguish of alienation, isolation, and perpetual conflict.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 120:5–PSA 120:7

## Psalms 120:6–7 (id: 23973)

peace: See [37:11](https://ref.ly/Ps37:11); [122:6–9](https://ref.ly/Ps122:6-Ps122:9); [125:5](https://ref.ly/Ps125:5); [128:6](https://ref.ly/Ps128:6).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 120:6–PSA 120:7

## Psalms 121:1 (id: 23975)

The mountains were known for their idolatrous worship ([Deut 12:2](https://ref.ly/Deut12:2)), and Israel was enticed to the hilltop shrines ([Hos 4:13](https://ref.ly/Hos4:13)). This verse can be understood as a rhetorical question expecting a negative answer: The gods of the hilltop shrines cannot rescue anyone. Others understand the mountains to be a symbol of the Lord’s strength ([Ps 95:4](https://ref.ly/Ps95:4)). In that case, the question would be interpreted literally (*Where does my help come from?*), with the answer given in the next verse

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 121:1

## Psalms 121:1–8 (id: 23974)

The leader of the group of pilgrims uses word pictures to assure the group of the Lord’s presence during the journey.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 121:1–PSA 121:8

## Psalms 121:4 (id: 23977)

God watches over his own, even and especially when they face many troubles ([12:5](https://ref.ly/Ps12:5), [7](https://ref.ly/Ps12:7); [69:29](https://ref.ly/Ps69:29); [91:14](https://ref.ly/Ps91:14); [146:9](https://ref.ly/Ps146:9)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 121:4

## Psalms 121:4–6 (id: 23976)

The Creator ([121:2](https://ref.ly/Ps121:2)) is the guardian of Israel. • God stands beside Israel, supporting and caring for the godly (see [16:7–8](https://ref.ly/Ps16:7-Ps16:8)). • Both the sun and the moon were regarded as deities in the ancient Near East, but the Creator limits their power. They, too, praise the Lord ([148:3](https://ref.ly/Ps148:3)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 121:4–PSA 121:6

## Psalms 122:1 (id: 23979)

The central sanctuary was the house of the Lord. This phrase originally referred to the Tabernacle ([Exod 23:19](https://ref.ly/Exod23:19); [34:26](https://ref.ly/Exod34:26)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 122:1

## Psalms 122:1–9 (id: 23978)

Jerusalem is here idealized as the city of God, the city of David, and the city of faith. A group of people on a pilgrimage joyfully arrive in the city ([122:1–2](https://ref.ly/Ps122:1-Ps122:2)). The psalmist sings an ode to Jerusalem ([122:3–5](https://ref.ly/Ps122:3-Ps122:5)) and prays for the city’s peace ([122:6–9](https://ref.ly/Ps122:6-Ps122:9)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 122:1–PSA 122:9

## Psalms 122:2 (id: 23980)

Several psalms celebrate or look forward to being inside the gates of the city ([9:14](https://ref.ly/Ps9:14); [87:2](https://ref.ly/Ps87:2); [100:4](https://ref.ly/Ps100:4); [118:19](https://ref.ly/Ps118:19)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 122:2

## Psalms 122:3 (id: 23982)

In the time of David and Solomon, Jerusalem was renowned as a place of security ([1 Kgs 10:6–7](https://ref.ly/1Kgs10:6-1Kgs10:7)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 122:3

## Psalms 122:3–5 (id: 23981)

Jerusalem is a metaphor for God’s heavenly dwelling. David was the archetype for God’s chosen rulers.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 122:3–PSA 122:5

## Psalms 122:4 (id: 23983)

Each of the people of Israel belonged to one of the tribes, and all of the tribes belonged to the Lord. • To give thanks is to present an offering acceptable to the Lord ([50:14](https://ref.ly/Ps50:14), [23](https://ref.ly/Ps50:23); [100:4](https://ref.ly/Ps100:4); [118:19](https://ref.ly/Ps118:19)). • as the law requires of Israel: See [Exod 23:17](https://ref.ly/Exod23:17); [Deut 16:16](https://ref.ly/Deut16:16).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 122:4

## Psalms 122:5 (id: 23984)

the thrones where judgment is given: In the eras of David and Solomon ([1 Kgs 3:28](https://ref.ly/1Kgs3:28)), Jerusalem was the home of wisdom and justice; it would be so again ([Isa 9:7](https://ref.ly/Isa9:7)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 122:5

## Psalms 122:6–9 (id: 23985)

Prayers for the peace of Jerusalem are motivated by love of family and God’s sanctuary.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 122:6–PSA 122:9

## Psalms 123:1–4 (id: 23986)

This lament on the psalmist’s lowly position expresses vivid trust in the Lord ([123:1–2](https://ref.ly/Ps123:1-Ps123:2)). The psalmist prays for God’s favor on the community, as the reality of evil surrounds them ([123:3–4](https://ref.ly/Ps123:3-Ps123:4)). The poet looks beyond Jerusalem ([Ps 122](https://ref.ly/Ps122:1-Ps122:9)) to God’s throne in heaven.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 123:1–PSA 123:4

## Psalms 124:1–2 (id: 23987)

The negative rhetorical questions emphasize the positive idea that the Lord was indeed on their side.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 124:1–PSA 124:2

## Psalms 124:1–8 (id: 23988)
