This thanksgiving song describes what might happen if the Lord were not present with his people.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 124:1–PSA 124:8

## Psalms 124:4–5 (id: 23989)

the raging waters of their fury: The enemies could have overwhelmed the Israelites and wiped them out if the Lord had not been with his people (cp. [69:15](https://ref.ly/Ps69:15); [Jer 46:8](https://ref.ly/Jer46:8)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 124:4–PSA 124:5

## Psalms 124:6–8 (id: 23990)

The enemies of God’s people, like lions or bears who tear their prey with their teeth (see [57:4](https://ref.ly/Ps57:4); [Prov 28:15](https://ref.ly/Prov28:15)), had their mouths shut by the Lord ([Dan 6:22](https://ref.ly/Dan6:22)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 124:6–PSA 124:8

## Psalms 125:1–5 (id: 23991)

The psalmist expresses the community’s confidence in the Lord’s protection ([125:1–2](https://ref.ly/Ps125:1-Ps125:2)) and prays for peace ([125:3–5](https://ref.ly/Ps125:3-Ps125:5)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 125:1–PSA 125:5

## Psalms 125:2 (id: 23992)

surrounds: God guards and protects like a wall of fire ([Zech 2:5](https://ref.ly/Zech2:5)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 125:2

## Psalms 125:3 (id: 23993)

The godly might be tempted through peer pressure and cultural domination.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 125:3

## Psalms 125:4–5 (id: 23994)

People who reject the straight path of the upright are fools ([Prov 2:12–15](https://ref.ly/Prov2:12-Prov2:15)). God pours out his goodness on the godly (see [Ps 122:6–9](https://ref.ly/Ps122:6-Ps122:9)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 125:4–PSA 125:5

## Psalms 126:1–3 (id: 23995)

The Lord brought about Israel’s restoration from exile, just as he had brought Israel out of Egypt ([114:1](https://ref.ly/Ps114:1)). The restoration transformed the weeping of the Lord’s people into laughter and showed the Lord’s character to the nations ([9:11](https://ref.ly/Ps9:11); [64:9](https://ref.ly/Ps64:9); [Isa 12:4](https://ref.ly/Isa12:4)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 126:1–PSA 126:3

## Psalms 126:1–6 (id: 23996)

This hymn celebrates Israel’s return from exile ([126:1–3](https://ref.ly/Ps126:1-Ps126:3)). The psalmist prays for full restoration ([126:4–6](https://ref.ly/Ps126:4-Ps126:6)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 126:1–PSA 126:6

## Psalms 126:4–6 (id: 23997)

The prophets had spoken of the restoration as a time when the wilderness would change into the Garden of Eden ([Isa 51:3](https://ref.ly/Isa51:3); [Ezek 47](https://ref.ly/Ezek47:1-Ezek47:23)); the reality fell far short of paradise. Here the restoration community prays for full redemption (see [Hag 2:19](https://ref.ly/Hag2:19)). • as streams renew the desert: The seasonal rains filled the dry river beds (*wadis*), and the land turned green again. The prayer looks for a similar transformation of Israel’s fortunes*,* a fulfillment of the imagery of the “Second Exodus” in Isaiah (see “The Promise of a Second Exodus” Theme Note). • The harvest represents God’s full restoration.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 126:4–PSA 126:6
* **Associated Articles:** The Promise of a Second Exodus (ID: `500298@TyndaleStudyNotesThemes`)

## Psalms 127:1–2 (id: 23998)

Unless: These conditional sentences emphasize the positive idea that the Lord will protect the city (cp. [124:1–2](https://ref.ly/Ps124:1-Ps124:2)). • Human effort is futile unless the Lord blesses it (see [44:3](https://ref.ly/Ps44:3)). • from early morning until late at night: This depicts an aggressive and competitive lifestyle. • God’s loved ones enjoy a quiet night’s sleep ([3:5](https://ref.ly/Ps3:5); [4:8](https://ref.ly/Ps4:8)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 127:1–PSA 127:2

## Psalms 127:1–5 (id: 23999)

Blessing and protection come from God. Without his presence, there is no success ([127:1–2](https://ref.ly/Ps127:1-Ps127:2)). This is particularly true for children, who are God’s gift ([127:3–5](https://ref.ly/Ps127:3-Ps127:5)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 127:1–PSA 127:5

## Psalms 127:3–5 (id: 24000)

Children are one of God’s blessings. The words translated “children” (Hebrew banim) and “builders” (bonim*,* [127:1](https://ref.ly/Ps127:1)) form a wordplay. Having children builds a family.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 127:3–PSA 127:5

## Psalms 127:4–5 (id: 24001)

like arrows: God uses children to protect the reputation of his people against the wicked (cp. [120:4](https://ref.ly/Ps120:4); [7:12–13](https://ref.ly/Ps7:12-Ps7:13)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 127:4–PSA 127:5

## Psalms 128:1–2 (id: 24002)

Enjoying the fruit of one’s labor means gaining benefit from whatever work one does.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 128:1–PSA 128:2

## Psalms 128:1–6 (id: 24003)

The godly, who fear the Lord, will know true happiness ([128:1–2](https://ref.ly/Ps128:1-Ps128:2)). The Lord is with them (see [127:1–2](https://ref.ly/Ps127:1-Ps127:2)), building their home life ([128:3–4](https://ref.ly/Ps128:3-Ps128:4)) and blessing them across the generations ([128:5–6](https://ref.ly/Ps128:5-Ps128:6)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 128:1–PSA 128:6

## Psalms 128:3 (id: 24004)

Like vigorous young olive trees*,* children are saplings filled with potential. Olive oil symbolizes God’s blessing ([104:15](https://ref.ly/Ps104:15); [Num 18:12](https://ref.ly/Num18:12); [Jer 31:12](https://ref.ly/Jer31:12); [Hag 2:19](https://ref.ly/Hag2:19)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 128:3

## Psalms 128:4–6 (id: 24005)

God will continually bless all who fear him ([133:3](https://ref.ly/Ps133:3)) from his dwelling in Zion ([20:2](https://ref.ly/Ps20:2); [50:2](https://ref.ly/Ps50:2); [110:2](https://ref.ly/Ps110:2)), no matter where they live. • grandchildren: God’s blessings extend from generation to generation for the faithful ([79:12–13](https://ref.ly/Ps79:12-Ps79:13); [89:1](https://ref.ly/Ps89:1); [100:4–5](https://ref.ly/Ps100:4-Ps100:5); [103:17–19](https://ref.ly/Ps103:17-Ps103:19)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 128:4–PSA 128:6

## Psalms 129:1–2 (id: 24006)

Israel’s earliest youth as a nation was during its sojourn in Egypt.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 129:1–PSA 129:2

## Psalms 129:1–8 (id: 24007)

The psalmist briefly reviews Israel’s history of trouble ([129:1–2](https://ref.ly/Ps129:1-Ps129:2)) and redemption ([129:3–4](https://ref.ly/Ps129:3-Ps129:4)). He concludes with curses against the enemies and blessings on the godly ([129:5–6](https://ref.ly/Ps129:5-Ps129:6)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 129:1–PSA 129:8

## Psalms 129:3–4 (id: 24008)

the Lord is good: He rescued Israel from Egypt, from many enemy attacks, and from the Babylonian exile.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 129:3–PSA 129:4

## Psalms 129:6–8 (id: 24009)

Grass on a rooftop had shallow roots and would scorch easily. A crop was ignored by the harvester when the yield was low. The enemies who had sown hurt among God’s people would gain little.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 129:6–PSA 129:8

## Psalms 130:1–3 (id: 24016)

A cry from the depths is from a place of deep distress (cp. [69:2](https://ref.ly/Ps69:2), [14](https://ref.ly/Ps69:14); [Isa 51:10](https://ref.ly/Isa51:10); [Ezek 27:34](https://ref.ly/Ezek27:34)). Out of the frailty of his being, the psalmist prays for divine favor.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 130:1–PSA 130:3

## Psalms 130:1–8 (id: 24017)

Beginning with himself as a representative of the community, the psalmist cries for God’s mercy ([130:1–3](https://ref.ly/Ps130:1-Ps130:3)) out of deep distress. He places his hope in the Lord ([130:4–6](https://ref.ly/Ps130:4-Ps130:6)), knowing that the Lord will rescue when and as he chooses. Based on this confidence, the psalmist invites Israel to wait for the Lord ([130:7–8](https://ref.ly/Ps130:7-Ps130:8)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 130:1–PSA 130:8

## Psalms 130:3 (id: 24018)

The psalmist knows that his sins make him guilty and deserving of God’s judgment.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 130:3

## Psalms 130:4–6 (id: 24019)

The good news comes in God’s readiness to forgive sinners. His grace encourages people to fear him and hope in him.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 130:4–PSA 130:6

## Psalms 130:5 (id: 24020)

God’s word imparts hope ([119:42–43](https://ref.ly/Ps119:42-Ps119:43), [49](https://ref.ly/Ps119:49); [147:11](https://ref.ly/Ps147:11)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 130:5

## Psalms 130:7–8 (id: 24021)

Israel is invited to hope in the Lord ([9:18](https://ref.ly/Ps9:18); [27:14](https://ref.ly/Ps27:14); [131:3](https://ref.ly/Ps131:3)) because the Lord pays the costly price for redemption and covers whatever sin separates humans from him (see also [111:9](https://ref.ly/Ps111:9); [Exod 6:6–8](https://ref.ly/Exod6:6-Exod6:8); [2 Sam 7:23–24](https://ref.ly/2Sam7:23-2Sam7:24); [Isa 43:1–4](https://ref.ly/Isa43:1-Isa43:4); [Titus 2:14](https://ref.ly/Titus2:14); [Heb 9:12](https://ref.ly/Heb9:12); [1 Pet 1:18](https://ref.ly/1Pet1:18)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 130:7–PSA 130:8

## Psalms 131:1 (id: 24023)

The heart represents the whole being (see [27:8](https://ref.ly/Ps27:8)). • God hates arrogance, which is a foolish way of life ([Prov 6:16–19](https://ref.ly/Prov6:16-Prov6:19)). • The psalmist does not trouble himself with matters that properly belong to the Lord.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 131:1

## Psalms 131:1–3 (id: 24022)

Out of his contentment in the Lord, the psalmist invites Israel to seek their rest in God ([131:3](https://ref.ly/Ps131:3)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 131:1–PSA 131:3

## Psalms 131:2 (id: 24024)

The psalmist calmed and quieted himself, surrendering his ambitions and taming his ego ([Gal 2:20](https://ref.ly/Gal2:20)). • like a weaned child: The psalmist sees himself as a contented child.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 131:2

## Psalms 132:1–18 (id: 24025)

This psalm celebrates the Lord’s faithfulness to David. When David wanted to bring the Ark into Jerusalem ([132:1–5](https://ref.ly/Ps132:1-Ps132:5)), the Lord granted the request and made Jerusalem his earthly home ([132:6–10](https://ref.ly/Ps132:6-Ps132:10)). The choice of Jerusalem marked God’s election of David’s line ([132:11–13](https://ref.ly/Ps132:11-Ps132:13)), of Zion ([132:14–17](https://ref.ly/Ps132:14-Ps132:17)), and of the priesthood ([132:9](https://ref.ly/Ps132:9), [16](https://ref.ly/Ps132:16)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 132:1–PSA 132:18

## Psalms 132:6 (id: 24031)

Ephrathah is Bethlehem ([Gen 35:19](https://ref.ly/Gen35:19); [48:7](https://ref.ly/Gen48:7)). • Jaar is the singular form of the plural “Jearim.” The Ark was at Kiriath\-jearim for twenty years in Samuel’s time ([1 Sam 7:1–2](https://ref.ly/1Sam7:1-1Sam7:2)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 132:6

## Psalms 132:6–10 (id: 24030)

These verses form a recollection of David’s moving the Ark of the Covenant to Jerusalem ([2 Sam 6:1–15](https://ref.ly/2Sam6:1-2Sam6:15)) and of the Lord’s oath to David ([2 Sam 7:4–16](https://ref.ly/2Sam7:4-2Sam7:16)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 132:6–PSA 132:10

## Psalms 132:8–10 (id: 24032)

These verses are a quotation from Solomon’s prayer at the dedication of the Temple ([2 Chr 6:41–42](https://ref.ly/2Chr6:41-2Chr6:42)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 132:8–PSA 132:10

## Psalms 132:9 (id: 24033)

The priests were to exhibit righteousness in their lives ([132:16](https://ref.ly/Ps132:16); [Mal 2:6](https://ref.ly/Mal2:6)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 132:9

## Psalms 132:11–12 (id: 24026)

The Lord swore an oath to David ([2 Sam 7:4–16](https://ref.ly/2Sam7:4-2Sam7:16)): God’s promise is unconditional, but the covenant is not (If . . . then). Those who break God’s covenant can expect the discipline of God’s judgment (see [Ps 89:30–37](https://ref.ly/Ps89:30-Ps89:37)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 132:11–PSA 132:12

## Psalms 132:13–17 (id: 24027)

The psalmist recounts the selection of Jerusalem and of the priests.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 132:13–PSA 132:17

## Psalms 132:17 (id: 24028)

anointed one: The ruler God chose and established (see [Pss 1–8](https://ref.ly/Ps1:1-Ps8:9)) would never cease to provide light for the Lord’s people. This light would burn continually (see [1 Kgs 11:36](https://ref.ly/1Kgs11:36); [2 Kgs 8:19](https://ref.ly/2Kgs8:19); cp. [John 8:12](https://ref.ly/John8:12); [Rev 21:23–24](https://ref.ly/Rev21:23-Rev21:24)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 132:17

## Psalms 132:18 (id: 24029)

The adversaries will be humiliated, in contrast to the glorious king ([132:9](https://ref.ly/Ps132:9), [16](https://ref.ly/Ps132:16)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 132:18

## Psalms 133:1 (id: 24036)

Brothers are related by blood, by profession, or by commitment.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 133:1

## Psalms 133:1–2 (id: 24034)

The psalmist tells of the joy of consecrated relationships.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 133:1–PSA 133:2

## Psalms 133:1–3 (id: 24035)

In this wisdom psalm (see [Ps 1](https://ref.ly/Ps1:1-Ps1:6)), peaceful and harmonious relationships manifest the presence of God.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 133:1–PSA 133:3

## Psalms 133:2 (id: 24037)

The anointing oil was the oil used to ordain and consecrate Aaron for service in his office (see [Exod 29:7](https://ref.ly/Exod29:7)). • head . . . beard . . . border of his robe: The oil consecrated Aaron completely.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 133:2

## Psalms 133:3 (id: 24038)

The dew represents the richness of divine blessings; in Jerusalem, it comes from moist winds from the Mediterranean Sea. Mount Hermon*,* which is capped with snow, is a place of abundant moisture. • A blessing is God’s life\-giving power, a guarantee of his provision and protection ([5:12](https://ref.ly/Ps5:12); [41:2](https://ref.ly/Ps41:2)), secured by his presence ([21:6](https://ref.ly/Ps21:6); [67:1](https://ref.ly/Ps67:1)). Even the other nations will ultimately be blessed ([Pss 67](https://ref.ly/Ps67:1-Ps67:7); [72:17](https://ref.ly/Ps72:17)). Zion is the focal point of God’s blessing ([134:3](https://ref.ly/Ps134:3); [147:13](https://ref.ly/Ps147:13)). • God gives life everlasting to human beings.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 133:3

## Psalms 134:1–2 (id: 24039)

Those who serve at night were the priests and Levites (see also [135:2](https://ref.ly/Ps135:2)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 134:1–PSA 134:2

## Psalms 134:1–3 (id: 24040)

In the last of the pilgrims’ songs ([Pss 120–134](https://ref.ly/Ps120:1-Ps134:3)), the travelers call the Temple workers to praise the Lord. In return, they will receive a much\-anticipated blessing.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 134:1–PSA 134:3

## Psalms 135:1–21 (id: 24041)

God, the Creator and the Lord of history, “made heaven and earth” ([134:3](https://ref.ly/Ps134:3)). He deserves praise because, unlike idols, he redeems his people.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 135:1–PSA 135:21

## Psalms 135:4 (id: 24046)

The synonyms Jacob and Israel include all twelve tribes. The Lord cherishes his chosen people. They are his treasure out of all the kingdoms of the world ([Exod 19:5–6](https://ref.ly/Exod19:5-Exod19:6)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 135:4

## Psalms 135:5 (id: 24047)

The Lord is superior to any real or imagined supernatural being (see [95:3–5](https://ref.ly/Ps95:3-Ps95:5); [115:4–8](https://ref.ly/Ps115:4-Ps115:8)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 135:5

## Psalms 135:6 (id: 24048)

God is sovereign over the whole created order—he does whatever pleases him him. • The phrase heaven and earth refers to all of creation.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 135:6

## Psalms 135:7 (id: 24049)

The psalmist tells of God’s sovereignty over the weather ([Pss 29](https://ref.ly/Ps29:1-Ps29:11); [77:17–18](https://ref.ly/Ps77:17-Ps77:18); [78:26](https://ref.ly/Ps78:26); [104:4](https://ref.ly/Ps104:4); [147:8–9](https://ref.ly/Ps147:8-Ps147:9); [148:5–6](https://ref.ly/Ps148:5-Ps148:6)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 135:7

## Psalms 135:8–11 (id: 24050)

In the tenth and culminating plague against Egypt, God destroyed the firstborn of each family. • The miraculous signs and wonders are the ten plagues (see [Exod 7–11](https://ref.ly/Exod7:1-Exod11:10); [Deut 4:34](https://ref.ly/Deut4:34); [Neh 9:10](https://ref.ly/Neh9:10)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 135:8–PSA 135:11

## Psalms 135:8–12 (id: 24051)

The Lord was sovereign over the Exodus and the conquest of the Promised Land.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 135:8–PSA 135:12

## Psalms 135:13–18 (id: 24042)

The Lord’s name and character stand in contrast to idols.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 135:13–PSA 135:18

## Psalms 135:15–18 (id: 24043)

Idols corrupt the thinking because they are merely things made by humans; they cannot speak, see, hear, or breathe ([Isa 41:22–24](https://ref.ly/Isa41:22-Isa41:24); [44:9](https://ref.ly/Isa44:9), [18](https://ref.ly/Isa44:18); [Rom 1:21–23](https://ref.ly/Rom1:21-Rom1:23)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 135:15–PSA 135:18

## Psalms 135:15–20 (id: 24044)

This entire section is repeated in [115:4–11](https://ref.ly/Ps115:4-Ps115:11).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 135:15–PSA 135:20

## Psalms 135:19–21 (id: 24045)

The groups named here comprised the covenant community (see [115:9–11](https://ref.ly/Ps115:9-Ps115:11)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 135:19–PSA 135:21

## Psalms 136:1–3 (id: 24053)

The psalmist invites the community to praise the Lord, who is good and full of love, the true Lord of humanity. Verse 1 alludes to the poetic expression in [2 Chr 5:13](https://ref.ly/2Chr5:13).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 136:1–PSA 136:3

## Psalms 136:1–26 (id: 24052)

This is the last of the Great Hallel psalms ([Pss 120–136](https://ref.ly/Ps120:1-Ps136:26)). It distinctively repeats the refrain His faithful love endures forever in every verse. The hymn is framed by a call to praise ([136:1–3](https://ref.ly/Ps136:1-Ps136:3), [26](https://ref.ly/Ps136:26)). It proclaims the Lord as the Creator of all and the Redeemer of Israel, both in the distant ([136:10–22](https://ref.ly/Ps136:10-Ps136:22)) and in the recent past ([136:23–24](https://ref.ly/Ps136:23-Ps136:24)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 136:1–PSA 136:26

## Psalms 136:10–22 (id: 24054)

The psalmist recounts the early history of Israel’s redemption.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 136:10–PSA 136:22

## Psalms 136:23–24 (id: 24055)

The psalmist relates the recent history of Israel’s redemption, although the circumstances are not specified.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 136:23–PSA 136:24

## Psalms 136:25 (id: 24056)

The Lord provides for all of his creatures.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 136:25

## Psalms 136:26 (id: 24057)

The phrase God of heaven is an exilic and postexilic designation for the Lord; it is found in Ezra ([Ezra 1:2](https://ref.ly/Ezra1:2); [5:11](https://ref.ly/Ezra5:11), [12](https://ref.ly/Ezra5:12); [6:9](https://ref.ly/Ezra6:9), [10](https://ref.ly/Ezra6:10); [7:12](https://ref.ly/Ezra7:12); etc.), Nehemiah ([Neh 1:5](https://ref.ly/Neh1:5); [2:4](https://ref.ly/Neh2:4), [20](https://ref.ly/Neh2:20); etc.), and Daniel ([Dan 2:18](https://ref.ly/Dan2:18), [19](https://ref.ly/Dan2:19), [37](https://ref.ly/Dan2:37), [44](https://ref.ly/Dan2:44)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 136:26

## Psalms 137:1–9 (id: 24058)

In response to the pain of exile ([137:1–4](https://ref.ly/Ps137:1-Ps137:4)), the psalmist resolves to remember Jerusalem even though the memories cause him pain ([137:4–6](https://ref.ly/Ps137:4-Ps137:6)). He also writes an astounding imprecation, or prayer for vengeance ([137:7–9](https://ref.ly/Ps137:7-Ps137:9)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 137:1–PSA 137:9

## Psalms 137:2–4 (id: 24059)

Because the music of Jerusalem was tied to the joys of life in the Promised Land, the Exile removed any occasion for singing joyous songs. The Babylonians wanted the Judeans to sing and dance for them, but the exiles’ grief made doing so either distasteful or impossible. The songs celebrating the Lord speak of his power and goodness, but his people were filled with doubts and questions. They hung their harps in trees, perhaps signifying the death of their joy under God’s curse ([Deut 21:23](https://ref.ly/Deut21:23)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 137:2–PSA 137:4

## Psalms 137:5–6 (id: 24060)

The psalmist pledges his loyalty to Jerusalem*,* the city at the center of God’s reign and the location of fellowship with him.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 137:5–PSA 137:6

## Psalms 137:7–9 (id: 24061)

The poet witnessed the betrayal of God’s people from Judah by the Edomites*,* so he curses Edom. The long rivalry between Edom and Judah came to a head during Judah’s last days, when the Edomites handed the Judeans over to the Babylonians ([Obad 1:10–11](https://ref.ly/Obad1:10-Obad1:11)) and rejoiced in Jerusalem’s fall. • This prayer for vengeance is shocking.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 137:7–PSA 137:9

## Psalms 138:1–3 (id: 24063)

The Lord receives praise before the gods of the nations.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 138:1–PSA 138:3

## Psalms 138:1–8 (id: 24064)

In this wisdom psalm, the Lord is presented as the God of gods. He rescued his people and has a perfect plan for them as individuals. The nations will join Israel in glorifying God.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 138:1–PSA 138:8

## Psalms 138:1–145.21 (id: 24062)

In this final collection of psalms of David, praise and wisdom psalms ([Pss 138–139](https://ref.ly/Ps138:1-Ps139:24), [145](https://ref.ly/Ps145:1-Ps145:21)) form a frame around five poems of lament ([Pss 140–144](https://ref.ly/Ps140:1-Ps144:15)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 138:1–PSA 145:21

## Psalms 138:4–5 (id: 24065)

As the Lord’s glory fills the earth, the world’s population must willingly submit to him. Every king (cp. [Ps 2](https://ref.ly/Ps2:1-Ps2:12)) will join the community of praise as they hear the Lord’s ways of truth and love.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 138:4–PSA 138:5

## Psalms 138:6 (id: 24067)

God’s holiness and excellence are great*,* beyond the scope of humanity (see [99:2](https://ref.ly/Ps99:2); [113:4](https://ref.ly/Ps113:4); [Isa 6:1](https://ref.ly/Isa6:1); [57:15](https://ref.ly/Isa57:15)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 138:6

## Psalms 138:6–8 (id: 24066)

The exalted God takes care of the humble ([138:6](https://ref.ly/Ps138:6)), especially his servant the psalmist ([138:7–8](https://ref.ly/Ps138:7-Ps138:8)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 138:6–PSA 138:8

## Psalms 138:8 (id: 24068)

The psalmist expresses confidence in the Lord’s plans*,* which are perfect, and prays for God’s continued involvement. The psalmist sees himself as part of God’s plans (see [9:10](https://ref.ly/Ps9:10); [139:14](https://ref.ly/Ps139:14)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 138:8

## Psalms 139:1–6 (id: 24070)

The Lord knows the psalmist well; God has examined him thoroughly, in an inescapable examination that is painful at times ([Job 7:17–19](https://ref.ly/Job7:17-Job7:19)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 139:1–PSA 139:6

## Psalms 139:1–24 (id: 24069)

In this wisdom psalm, the psalmist opens every aspect of his being, character, behavior, and speech to God’s examination. As hard as life is, he wants to ensure his own growth in wisdom so that he does not come under God’s judgment of the wicked ([141:5](https://ref.ly/Ps141:5); [142:3](https://ref.ly/Ps142:3); [143:8](https://ref.ly/Ps143:8), [10](https://ref.ly/Ps143:10); [144:3–4](https://ref.ly/Ps144:3-Ps144:4)). Further, the poet recognizes that he cannot escape from the Lord. His sense of stress disappears when he considers the Lord’s loving care for him, even before birth ([139:13–18](https://ref.ly/Ps139:13-Ps139:18)). He then invites the Lord to continue examining him as he walks in the path of wisdom ([139:23–24](https://ref.ly/Ps139:23-Ps139:24)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 139:1–PSA 139:24

## Psalms 139:2 (id: 24077)

The phrase sit down or stand up refers to daily activities (cp. [Deut 6:6–9](https://ref.ly/Deut6:6-Deut6:9)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 139:2

## Psalms 139:3–6 (id: 24078)

The Lord’s omniscience and omnipotence provide comfort to the godly, but they imprison the hearts of the wicked ([2:3](https://ref.ly/Ps2:3)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 139:3–PSA 139:6

## Psalms 139:6 (id: 24079)

The Lord’s wonderful understanding lies beyond the psalmist’s ability to comprehend (see [Judg 13:18](https://ref.ly/Judg13:18)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 139:6

## Psalms 139:7–12 (id: 24080)

The psalmist expresses his awe at the Lord’s omnipresence.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 139:7–PSA 139:12

## Psalms 139:8 (id: 24081)

down to the grave: God has total access to his entire creation—even the most hard\-to\-reach places.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 139:8

## Psalms 139:9 (id: 24082)

ride the wings of the morning: This poetic expression describes traveling eastward, as far as the sunrise, if that were possible. • the farthest oceans: This expression takes the traveler in the opposite direction, far to the west.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 139:9

## Psalms 139:13 (id: 24071)

The delicate, inner parts of the body include a person’s very being. • Even when hidden in his mother’s womb*,* the psalmist was guided by the Lord.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 139:13

## Psalms 139:17 (id: 24072)

How precious are your thoughts about me: God’s investigation reveals loving care. Fellowship with the Lord provides riches beyond description.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 139:17

## Psalms 139:19–24 (id: 24073)

The psalmist’s sense of awe leads him to consider the wicked and to reflect on himself. The Lord, as the examiner of all people, judges the wicked for their destructive acts and speech; thus, the psalmist prays that he will not be among them.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 139:19–PSA 139:24

## Psalms 139:21 (id: 24074)

I hate: Rejection of evil is a mark of wisdom (see [1:1](https://ref.ly/Ps1:1); [5:4–6](https://ref.ly/Ps5:4-Ps5:6)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 139:21

## Psalms 139:23–24 (id: 24075)

The psalmist’s prayer against the wicked leads him also to reflect on himself; he does not presume that he is righteous. This prayer has been repeated by believers over the centuries.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 139:23–PSA 139:24

## Psalms 139:24 (id: 24076)

The path of wisdom leads to everlasting life (see [1:6](https://ref.ly/Ps1:6); [Prov 4:18](https://ref.ly/Prov4:18); [6:23](https://ref.ly/Prov6:23)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 139:24

## Psalms 140:1–3 (id: 24091)

The psalmist prays for the Lord to rescue him from wicked people.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 140:1–PSA 140:3

## Psalms 140:1–13 (id: 24090)

In this individual lament, the psalmist artistically sketches God’s enemies with all their evil intents. He prays for the Lord’s protection and rescue with confidence in God’s strength and justice. He foresees the evil as being judged by fire ([140:9–11](https://ref.ly/Ps140:9-Ps140:11)) and himself as being vindicated and dwelling in the Lord’s presence ([140:13](https://ref.ly/Ps140:13)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 140:1–PSA 140:13

## Psalms 140:3 (id: 24093)

sting like a snake . . . a viper: These creatures depict the wicked as very corrupt people (see [Prov 23:32](https://ref.ly/Prov23:32); [Isa 14:29](https://ref.ly/Isa14:29); [Rom 3:13](https://ref.ly/Rom3:13)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 140:3

## Psalms 140:4–5 (id: 24094)

The psalmist asks for divine protection (see [Ps 121](https://ref.ly/Ps121:1-Ps121:8)), praying that the Lord will keep him safe from the many schemes of the wicked.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 140:4–PSA 140:5

## Psalms 140:7 (id: 24095)

The expression Sovereign Lord comes from combining the name Yahweh with the title Adonai (Master). See also [68:20](https://ref.ly/Ps68:20); [69:6](https://ref.ly/Ps69:6); [71:16](https://ref.ly/Ps71:16); [73:28](https://ref.ly/Ps73:28); [109:21](https://ref.ly/Ps109:21); [141:8](https://ref.ly/Ps141:8).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 140:7

## Psalms 140:9–11 (id: 24096)

The psalmist prays for God’s judgment on the wicked.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 140:9–PSA 140:11

## Psalms 140:10 (id: 24092)

The psalmist wants fire to descend on his enemies, and he wants them thrown into pits so they can never attack again. The language foreshadows the New Testament teaching on hell ([Matt 5:22](https://ref.ly/Matt5:22), [29–30](https://ref.ly/Matt5:29-Matt5:30); [10:28](https://ref.ly/Matt10:28); [18:9](https://ref.ly/Matt18:9); [Mark 9:43–47](https://ref.ly/Mark9:43-Mark9:47); [Luke 12:5](https://ref.ly/Luke12:5); [Jas 3:6](https://ref.ly/Jas3:6); [2 Pet 2:4](https://ref.ly/2Pet2:4)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 140:10

## Psalms 141:1–2 (id: 24098)

The psalmist prays urgently for rescue. He does not have at hand either incense or an evening offering ([Exod 29:38–39](https://ref.ly/Exod29:38-Exod29:39)), but his prayers and devotion are the reality that those elements represent (cp. [Isa 1:13](https://ref.ly/Isa1:13); [Rev 5:8](https://ref.ly/Rev5:8)). • Upraised hands are a posture of prayer ([Pss 28:2](https://ref.ly/Ps28:2); [88:9](https://ref.ly/Ps88:9); [143:6](https://ref.ly/Ps143:6); [Exod 9:29](https://ref.ly/Exod9:29); [1 Tim 2:8](https://ref.ly/1Tim2:8)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 141:1–PSA 141:2

## Psalms 141:1–10 (id: 24097)

The psalmist prays for rescue and wisdom, and he envisions the end of evil. The principle of retribution ([141:10](https://ref.ly/Ps141:10)) unifies the psalm.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 141:1–PSA 141:10

## Psalms 141:3–5 (id: 24099)

Wisdom sometimes requires protection from oneself. One could say or think things that lead to the evil path ([Prov 13:3](https://ref.ly/Prov13:3); [21:23](https://ref.ly/Prov21:23)). • Wisdom opens itself to correction from godly people (see [Prov 3:11](https://ref.ly/Prov3:11); [9:8](https://ref.ly/Prov9:8); [15:31](https://ref.ly/Prov15:31); [19:25](https://ref.ly/Prov19:25)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 141:3–PSA 141:5

## Psalms 142:1–3 (id: 24100)

Though overwhelmed by his persecutors ([142:6](https://ref.ly/Ps142:6)), the psalmist looks to the Lord for wisdom.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 142:1–PSA 142:3

## Psalms 142:1–7 (id: 24101)

regarding his experience in the cave: Cp. [Ps 57:title](https://ref.ly/Ps57:1).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 142:1–PSA 142:7

## Psalms 142:7 (id: 24105)

His experience of confinement and duress is like being in prison (see [107:10](https://ref.ly/Ps107:10)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 142:7

## Psalms 142:3–4 (id: 24102)

The psalmist reaches a point of despair (see [77:3](https://ref.ly/Ps77:3)), and the Lord cares for him in his distress. The psalmist commits himself to the Lord’s wisdom (see [Ps 139](https://ref.ly/Ps139:1-Ps139:24)) but laments his entrapment by the wicked ([5:9–10](https://ref.ly/Ps5:9-Ps5:10); [140:5](https://ref.ly/Ps140:5); [141:9](https://ref.ly/Ps141:9); [142:3](https://ref.ly/Ps142:3)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 142:3–PSA 142:4

## Psalms 142:5 (id: 24103)

Though he is alone, the psalmist’s trust remains in the Lord, who is his life (see [9:9](https://ref.ly/Ps9:9); [16:5](https://ref.ly/Ps16:5); [27:13](https://ref.ly/Ps27:13)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 142:5

## Psalms 142:6–7 (id: 24104)

Though overwhelmed by loneliness and trouble, the psalmist focuses on the Lord’s goodness and protection. He knows that the Lord alone is his Redeemer, so he offers his praise.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 142:6–PSA 142:7

## Psalms 142 (id: 24106)

The psalmist faces severe persecution, so he cries to the Lord, and the Lord will rescue him.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 142:1–PSA 142:7

## Psalms 143:1–2 (id: 24108)

The psalmist prays for God’s love and mercy.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 143:1–PSA 143:2

## Psalms 143:1–12 (id: 24107)

In this lament, the psalmist feels overwhelmed by constant harassment from his foes, so he turns to the Lord’s love, righteousness, and faithfulness. He remembers God’s acts in the past and yearns for the renewal of the Lord’s love. He opens himself to God’s wisdom because he knows that instruction will lead to life.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 143:1–PSA 143:12

## Psalms 143:2 (id: 24111)

All people are guilty before God ([Rom 3:20–24](https://ref.ly/Rom3:20-Rom3:24)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 143:2

## Psalms 143:3–4 (id: 24112)

I am losing all hope: The psalmist confesses his desperation as his life slips away under oppressive and ruthless foes.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 143:3–PSA 143:4

## Psalms 143:5–6 (id: 24113)

Remembering God’s acts from the past reassures the psalmist of God’s faithfulness ([42:4](https://ref.ly/Ps42:4); [63:6](https://ref.ly/Ps63:6); [77:3](https://ref.ly/Ps77:3), [6](https://ref.ly/Ps77:6); [119:55](https://ref.ly/Ps119:55)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 143:5–PSA 143:6

## Psalms 143:6 (id: 24114)

The psalmist’s thirst is a deep longing for God’s redemption (see [42:1–2](https://ref.ly/Ps42:1-Ps42:2)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 143:6

## Psalms 143:7 (id: 24116)

The psalmist experiences depression. He feels that he is dying from anguish ([31:10](https://ref.ly/Ps31:10); [119:87](https://ref.ly/Ps119:87)), exhausted ([39:10](https://ref.ly/Ps39:10); [71:9](https://ref.ly/Ps71:9); [119:81](https://ref.ly/Ps119:81)), fainting with longing ([84:2](https://ref.ly/Ps84:2)), and overwhelmed by the weariness of life ([90:7](https://ref.ly/Ps90:7), [9](https://ref.ly/Ps90:9)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 143:7

## Psalms 143:7–10 (id: 24115)

The psalmist petitions the Lord for a renewal of his love.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 143:7–PSA 143:10

## Psalms 143:8–10 (id: 24117)

The psalmist prays for wisdom (see [5:8](https://ref.ly/Ps5:8); [25:4–6](https://ref.ly/Ps25:4-Ps25:6); [138](https://ref.ly/Ps138:1-Ps138:8); [143:10](https://ref.ly/Ps143:10)). • your gracious Spirit: The Spirit brings God’s goodness (see [23:6](https://ref.ly/Ps23:6)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 143:8–PSA 143:10

## Psalms 143:11 (id: 24109)

To preserve means in this case to restore from despair ([80:19](https://ref.ly/Ps80:19); [85:6](https://ref.ly/Ps85:6); [138:7](https://ref.ly/Ps138:7)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 143:11

## Psalms 143:12 (id: 24110)

A prayer for vindication and renewal of life concludes the psalm.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 143:12

## Psalms 144:1–2 (id: 24119)

The psalmist’s descriptive names for the Lord reveal his deep love for him.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 144:1–PSA 144:2

## Psalms 144:1–15 (id: 24118)

This lament begins with an exclamation of love for the Lord. The community then reflects on the transitory nature of life ([144:3–4](https://ref.ly/Ps144:3-Ps144:4)). The psalmist prays for divine intervention and anticipates victory ([144:5–11](https://ref.ly/Ps144:5-Ps144:11)). A new song ([144:9–10](https://ref.ly/Ps144:9-Ps144:10)) and a prayer for rescue ([144:11](https://ref.ly/Ps144:11)) open up the theme of the Lord’s blessing through his provisions and protection ([144:12–15](https://ref.ly/Ps144:12-Ps144:15)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 144:1–PSA 144:15

## Psalms 144:3–4 (id: 24123)

what are human beings? The same question in [8:4–6](https://ref.ly/Ps8:4-Ps8:6) elicits the answer that humans are mere mortals but are also glorious rulers. The psalmist depicts humans as having a transitory, empty existence (see [90:3](https://ref.ly/Ps90:3), [7–10](https://ref.ly/Ps90:7-Ps90:10); [102:11](https://ref.ly/Ps102:11); [109:23](https://ref.ly/Ps109:23); [146:4](https://ref.ly/Ps146:4)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 144:3–PSA 144:4

## Psalms 144:5–8 (id: 24124)

The psalmist prays for God’s intervention against his enemies (cp. [18:7–19](https://ref.ly/Ps18:7-Ps18:19)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 144:5–PSA 144:8

## Psalms 144:12 (id: 24121)

The psalmist compares sons and daughters to plants and pillars, which are images of strength and beauty.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 144:12

## Psalms 144:12–15 (id: 24120)

This prayer for the Lord’s blessing brings the laments of [Pss 140–144](https://ref.ly/Ps140:1-Ps144:15) to a close. It offers a vision of God’s provision and protection (see [Ps 127](https://ref.ly/Ps127:1-Ps127:5)), not only for the psalmist, but for his descendants and those of all the godly.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 144:12–PSA 144:15

## Psalms 144:13–14 (id: 24122)

no enemy . . . no cries of alarm: These images depict peace and security.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 144:13–PSA 144:14

## Psalms 145:1–3 (id: 24126)

The psalmist praises God, the Great King who reigns over all other rulers (see [47:2](https://ref.ly/Ps47:2)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 145:1–PSA 145:3

## Psalms 145:1–21 (id: 24125)

This hymn of praise is the last in this collection of the psalms of David ([Pss 138–145](https://ref.ly/Ps138:1-Ps145:21)). Praise continues in the last five psalms ([Pss 146–150](https://ref.ly/Ps146:1-Ps150:6)). This psalm celebrates the Lord as King of all ([145:1–3](https://ref.ly/Ps145:1-Ps145:3), [10–13](https://ref.ly/Ps145:10-Ps145:13)). God’s actions reveal his royal qualities ([145:4–7](https://ref.ly/Ps145:4-Ps145:7)). He cares for all creatures ([145:14–17](https://ref.ly/Ps145:14-Ps145:17)) and for those who fear him ([145:18–20](https://ref.ly/Ps145:18-Ps145:20)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 145:1–PSA 145:21

## Psalms 145:4–7 (id: 24130)

This litany praises God’s character and mighty deeds. Each generation will continue to testify to God’s power ([22:30](https://ref.ly/Ps22:30)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 145:4–PSA 145:7

## Psalms 145:8–9 (id: 24131)

God consistently demonstrates his character toward all his creation (see[136:25](https://ref.ly/Ps136:25)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 145:8–PSA 145:9

## Psalms 145:10–13 (id: 24127)

These verses form a description of the Lord’s kingdom.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 145:10–PSA 145:13

## Psalms 145:14–20 (id: 24128)

The Lord cares for his creatures.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 145:14–PSA 145:20

## Psalms 145:20 (id: 24129)

The Lord cares for those who love him and fear him. God\-fearers love the Lord and find refuge in him ([5:11](https://ref.ly/Ps5:11)); they seek him as their only true Savior ([40:16](https://ref.ly/Ps40:16); [70:4](https://ref.ly/Ps70:4)). They will experience a grand future ([69:36](https://ref.ly/Ps69:36)), as well as God’s peace ([119:165](https://ref.ly/Ps119:165)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 145:20

## Psalms 146:1 (id: 24134)

This verse is reminiscent of [103:1](https://ref.ly/Ps103:1), [2](https://ref.ly/Ps103:2), [22](https://ref.ly/Ps103:22); [104:1](https://ref.ly/Ps104:1), [35](https://ref.ly/Ps104:35).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 146:1

## Psalms 146:1–10 (id: 24132)

The call to praise ([146:1–2](https://ref.ly/Ps146:1-Ps146:2)) leads into a warning against folly and false confidence ([146:3–4](https://ref.ly/Ps146:3-Ps146:4)). The psalm concludes with a blessing for all who place their hope in the Lord ([146:5–7](https://ref.ly/Ps146:5-Ps146:7)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 146:1–PSA 146:10

## Psalms 146:1–150.6 (id: 24133)

The Psalter ends with five hallelujah psalms, so named because each begins and ends with Praise the Lord! (Hebrew haleluyah).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 146:1–PSA 150:6

## Psalms 146:8–9 (id: 24135)

The fourfold repetition of the name of the Lord emphasizes that only he heals, unburdens, loves, and protects.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 146:8–PSA 146:9

## Psalms 147:1 (id: 24141)

This verse is a call to worship.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 147:1

## Psalms 147:1–20 (id: 24136)

The psalmist calls for the Lord to be praised for restoring and blessing Zion, caring for the poor, displaying his power over nature, and revealing himself to his people.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 147:1–PSA 147:20

## Psalms 147:2–6 (id: 24142)

The psalmist recalls the restoration of Jerusalem and the Lord’s afflicted exiles.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 147:2–PSA 147:6

## Psalms 147:4–5 (id: 24143)

The Lord created the heavens. • He counts the stars: God’s people can feel secure in knowing that the Lord attends to every detail of his creation; he knows all that belongs to him.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 147:4–PSA 147:5

## Psalms 147:6 (id: 24144)

God measures out his justice on the poor and on the wicked ([55:22](https://ref.ly/Ps55:22); [140:12](https://ref.ly/Ps140:12); [145:14](https://ref.ly/Ps145:14); [146:7](https://ref.ly/Ps146:7)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 147:6

## Psalms 147:7–11 (id: 24145)

Human achievements fail to impress the God who commands nature; rather, he takes pleasure in those who fear him.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 147:7–PSA 147:11

## Psalms 147:8 (id: 24146)

God holds sovereign power over the weather ([77:17–18](https://ref.ly/Ps77:17-Ps77:18); [78:26](https://ref.ly/Ps78:26); [104:4](https://ref.ly/Ps104:4); [148:5–6](https://ref.ly/Ps148:5-Ps148:6)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 147:8

## Psalms 147:10–11 (id: 24137)

human might: Any physical or intellectual achievement is a gift from the Lord, just like the strength of a horse. These gifts are a reason to praise the Lord, not to boast ([Jer 9:23–24](https://ref.ly/Jer9:23-Jer9:24)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 147:10–PSA 147:11

## Psalms 147:13 (id: 24138)

The bars of the city gates symbolize defenses against enemies. • God blessed his people by empowering them with safety, prosperity, peace, and provisions (see [133:3](https://ref.ly/Ps133:3)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 147:13

## Psalms 147:15–18 (id: 24139)

Simply by speaking his command*,* the Lord can change the season from unbearable winter to refreshing spring (see [147:8](https://ref.ly/Ps147:8); [148:5–6](https://ref.ly/Ps148:5-Ps148:6)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 147:15–PSA 147:18

## Psalms 147:19–20 (id: 24140)

words . . . decrees . . . regulations: The Lord gave powerful words to Israel so that they might obey him ([105:45](https://ref.ly/Ps105:45)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 147:19–PSA 147:20

## Psalms 148:1 (id: 24150)

During Jesus’ triumphant entry into Jerusalem, the crowds called out various blessings, including a phrase taken from this verse ([Matt 21:9](https://ref.ly/Matt21:9); [Mark 11:10](https://ref.ly/Mark11:10); [Luke 19:38](https://ref.ly/Luke19:38)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 148:1

## Psalms 148:1–14 (id: 24147)

This psalm calls for the whole created order to praise the Lord because he has honored his faithful people.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 148:1–PSA 148:14

## Psalms 148:6 (id: 24151)

The created order is stable because of the Lord’s word (see [33:9](https://ref.ly/Ps33:9)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 148:6

## Psalms 148:8 (id: 24152)

In the ancient Near East, people viewed different gods as having control over separate aspects of nature. The Lord, however, reigns sovereign over all natural phenomena; all the parts of creation are his servants, bringing praise to him through their obedience ([77:17–18](https://ref.ly/Ps77:17-Ps77:18); [104:4](https://ref.ly/Ps104:4); [135:7](https://ref.ly/Ps135:7); [147:8](https://ref.ly/Ps147:8), [15–18](https://ref.ly/Ps147:15-Ps147:18); [Num 11:31](https://ref.ly/Num11:31)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 148:8

## Psalms 148:11–12 (id: 24148)

The psalmist calls all humans to offer praise to God, regardless of status, age, or gender.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 148:11–PSA 148:12

## Psalms 148:13–14 (id: 24149)

Universal praise of the Lord is fitting because he is glorious, and he has blessed his people (see [147:13](https://ref.ly/Ps147:13); [Isa 46:13](https://ref.ly/Isa46:13); [Eph 3:10](https://ref.ly/Eph3:10)). • His faithful ones are his trusting and devoted servants ([Ps 86:2](https://ref.ly/Ps86:2)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 148:13–PSA 148:14

## Psalms 149:1–9 (id: 24153)

This hymn of praise celebrates the Lord’s victory. He is the Maker of Israel ([149:1–2](https://ref.ly/Ps149:1-Ps149:2)) and the victorious King who shares his glory with his faithful ones ([149:3–9](https://ref.ly/Ps149:3-Ps149:9)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 149:1–PSA 149:9

## Psalms 149:4 (id: 24154)

God’s people, whom the world ignores and despises, will be vindicated ([Matt 19:30](https://ref.ly/Matt19:30)). The humble will experience victory over their oppressors and persecutors (see [Isa 61:3](https://ref.ly/Isa61:3)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 149:4

## Psalms 149:6–9 (id: 24155)

Vengeance is the Lord’s business (see [2:3](https://ref.ly/Ps2:3); [94:1](https://ref.ly/Ps94:1); [102:20](https://ref.ly/Ps102:20); [142:7](https://ref.ly/Ps142:7); [146:7](https://ref.ly/Ps146:7)).

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 149:6–PSA 149:9

## Psalms 150:1 (id: 24162)

The phrase mighty heaven alludes to [Gen 1](https://ref.ly/Gen1:1-Gen1:31) and to God’s glorious work in filling the emptiness.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 150:1

## Psalms 150:1–6 (id: 24161)

Everything that breathes is commanded to praise the Lord as he deserves. The whole Psalter describes the greatness of the Lord, so this psalm is a fitting conclusion.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 150:1–PSA 150:6

## Psalms 150:3–5 (id: 24163)

The psalmist calls all people to praise God with instruments and dancing. flutes: These wind instruments are not mentioned as being used in Temple worship. • clanging cymbals: Temple musicians clapped two bronze bowls together as percussion instruments.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 150:3–PSA 150:5

## Psalms 150:6 (id: 24164)

Praise the Lord: This refrain is a fitting conclusion to the entire book of Psalms.

* **Associated Passages:** PSA 150:6
